801 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Turner v. Massiah


No. 94-CA-29


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-CA-29 (La.App. 5 Cir. 7/1/94); 641 So. 2d 610; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2015



July 1, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused September 16, 1994. Released for Publication September 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 386-542, DIVISION "O". HONORABLE RONALD P. LOUMIET, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a patient and her husband, and defendants, a plastic surgeon and a compensation fund, appealed a judgment from the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division O (Louisiana). The trial court awarded judgment in favor of plaintiffs in their medical malpractice action and entered judgment against two doctors and the compensation fund.


OVERVIEW: A woman who received breast implants repeatedly complained to her plastic surgeon of discomfort in her right breast. The plastic surgeon told her that a hardening in the breast was a common result of augmentation surgery and did not send the patient for diagnostic tests. The woman also complained to her obstetrician/gynecologist (OB/GYN), who told her she should follow up with her plastic surgeon. When other doctors diagnosed breast cancer, the patient and her husband filed a medical malpractice action against her plastic surgeon and her OB/GYN. The trial court entered judgment for plaintiffs. The court affirmed. The jury did not commit manifest error in finding that the plastic surgeon was negligent in his treatment by not ordering a mammogram and that his negligence proximately damaged the patient; a medical review panel found that the surgeon failed to comply with the proper standard of care. The trial court did not err in awarding damages to plaintiffs under a cap for each doctor, rather than a cap for plaintiffs' total award. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B) permitted the application of separate caps to each separate act of negligence by each liable health care provider.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of plaintiffs in their medical malpractice action, and the court affirmed the judgment that the statutory cap was applicable to each doctor and his negligence, rather than to plaintiffs' total recovery.

 

802 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. May


No. 93-KA-2180


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


93-2180 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/30/94) 639 So. 2d 1225; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1970



June 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS. PARISH NO. 359-724, SECTION "C". HONORABLE JEROME M. WINSBERG, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed an order from the Criminal District Court, Orleans, Section C (Louisiana), convicting defendants of attempted illegal use of a weapon by discharging a firearm from a vehicle on public highway and imposing a ten year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged their conviction for attempted illegal use of a weapon by discharging a firearm from a motor vehicle on public highway and their sentences. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that one of the defendants was not entitled to a new trial because while there were discrepancies in the officer's testimony regarding the driver of the vehicle, the jury clearly decided that the officer's testimony was credible and decided to reject the discrepancies. Next, the court held that the ten year sentence was not excessive. Although the sentence imposed was greater than the maximum sentence for the alleged act, the trial court had discretion to deviate where the record supported the deviation and the specified aggravating or mitigating circumstances justified the departure. The court noted that the defendants opened fire on women and a baby and that such actions were deplorable and mandated a stiff sentence from the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' conviction for attempted illegal use of a weapon and their sentences.

 

803 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mayeux


No. 94-KA-105


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-105 (La.App. 5 Cir. 6/28/94); 639 So. 2d 828; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2023



June 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 89-485, DIVISION "J". HONORBLE JACOB L. KARNO, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), that convicted her of aggravated battery and criminal conspiracy, arguing that the district court erred in permitting the State to introduce the recorded statements of a key witness into evidence in violation of the rule against hearsay and that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction.


OVERVIEW: After the victim broke up with her boyfriend, he contacted his sister, the defendant, and expressed a desire that someone throw acid in the victim's face. The victim procured the assistance of two acquaintances and participated in mixing up the liquid. The defendant was subsequently charged with and convicted of aggravated battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34 and criminal conspiracy in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:26. The defendant appealed. In affirming, the court concluded that the recorded statement of a key witness, one of the attackers, was properly used to impeach her where she evaded questions by claiming that she did not recall the prior statement made to police. The statement was thus properly admitted under La. Evid. Code Ann. art. 607 to impeach the witness's claims at trial that the defendant was not involved in the attack. Further, where the evidence included the defendant's admission of her involvement to a fellow inmate and the testimony of the attackers regarding the defendant's involvement, the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

804 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Thibodeau v. Mayor & Councilmen of Morgan City


No. 92 CA 1050R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


92 CA 1050R (La.App. 1 Cir. 6/24/94); 640 So. 2d 830; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2048



June 24, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 30, 1994. Released for Publication August 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 16th Judicial District Court in and for St. Mary Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 83,855. Honorable Paul J. deMahy, Judge



DISPOSITION: AMENDED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injury victim sought review of a judgment of the 16th Judicial District Court in and for St. Mary Parish (Louisiana) Which awarded damages to plaintiff for injury from a diving accident, but limited the damages to $ 500,000 and dismissed plaintiff's parents' claim for loss of consortium.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured in a diving accident and brought suit against defendants. The trial court found that plaintiff suffered general damages of $ 3,500,000. His parents were awarded damages for loss of consortium. The appellate court proportioned fault 67 percent to plaintiff, 22 percent to the city, and 11percent to the state. Plaintiff's award of general damages was limited to $ 500,000.00 pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106, which set a cap on damage awards against the state and its political subdivisions. The parent's loss of consortium claims were dismissed because plaintiff's general damages exhausted the monetary limits of the cap on damages. After The supreme court granted the plaintiff a writ, and remanded to the appellate court to reconsider the award of total damages on account of a supreme court decision declaring the cap in § 13:5106 unconstitutional. The court amended the judgment to award the plaintiff general damages of to $ 770,000 and reversed the judgment dismissing the parents' claim and awarded them $ 2,200 each. The court also and awarded interest under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2924 from date of judicial demand.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment awarding general damages to the plaintiff and reversed the judgment dismissing the parents' claim for loss of consortium and awarded damages to the parents.

 

805 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Connelley v. City of Hammond


93 CA 1534


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


93 CA 1534 (La.App. 1 Cir. 6/24/94); 638 So. 2d 722; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2061



June 24, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 21st Judicial District Court Parish of Tangipahoa, Louisiana. Docket No. 9200967, Division "F". Honorable Jefferson D. Hughes, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED; PLAINTIFF'S CLAIM DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a judgment from the 21st Judicial District Court, Division F, Parish of Tangipahoa (Louisiana), which affirmed action taken by a municipal civil service board (board) in which the board failed to grant any relief to the employee with respect to his complaint of a discriminatory implementation of defendant city's pay classification plan.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a city police officer, complained that a new pay classification plan implemented by the city was discriminatory and unconstitutional because it did not provide uniform pay to persons who had the same pay grade code. The employee filed a complaint with the board concerning the discriminatory implementation of the pay classification plan. The board's action failed to grant any relief to the employee. The trial court then affirmed the board's action. On appeal, the court vacated the trial court's judgment and dismissed the employee's claim to the board. The court found that the employee's complaint did not pertain to a discharge or any corrective or disciplinary action, which were the only grounds that afforded him the appeal procedure to the board provided by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2501(A). The court determined that § 33:2501(A) did not apply in this case. The court ruled that the board was without legal authority to entertain the employee's complaint or to render any decision with respect to the employee's allegations of unconstitutional discrimination. The court found that the board was not the proper forum for the employee to raise his constitutional issues.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the trial court that affirmed the board's action. The court dismissed the employee's claim to the board.

 

806 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thomas


No. 26,116-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


26,116 (La.App. 2 Cir. 6/22/94); 639 So. 2d 408; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1832



June 22, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 11, 1994. Released for Publication August 11, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 29,118. Honorable Robert Y. Butler, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville (Louisiana) convicting him of distribution of cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A)(1). He was sentenced to serve 150 months at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from a conviction of distribution of cocaine, the court affirmed, holding that the record contained sufficient evidence upon which to base defendant's conviction. The court held that statutes were presumed to be valid, and the constitutionality of a statute should be upheld whenever possible. The facts in the instant case did not involve an extension of state criminal authority beyond the proper reach of government into a constitutionally protected area of defendant's life. Accordingly, the court did not reach the question of whether either La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:967(A)(1) or 40:961(13) were unconstitutionally broad in its scope. Further, where a statute was ambiguous and susceptible of two constructions, courts should give that construction which best comported with the principles of reason, justice, and convenience. Defendant's construction of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:961(13) was incorrect. Further, the language of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:961(13) and 40:967(A) made it sufficiently clear that selling $ 20 rocks of crack cocaine on the street to the general public was unlawful. Such conduct was not authorized by the Uniform Controlled Dangerous Substances Law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the evidence, when viewed in a light favorable to the prosecution, was sufficient to support defendant's conviction of distribution of cocaine. Accordingly, defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

807 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Sherrill v. Sherrill


No. 25,889-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


25,889 (La.App. 2 Cir. 6/22/94); 639 So. 2d 794; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1863



June 22, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 11, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 58,058. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; REMANDED; AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former wife appealed from the decision of the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, which denied her request for a partition of defendant former husband's military benefits.


OVERVIEW: The husband began receiving military retirement benefits in 1978. In 1982, the parties were legally separated and they subsequently entered into a community property settlement, which did not mention the retirement benefits. At the time, case law provided that such benefits were separate property. In 1992, the wife filed a petition to partition the retirement benefits and sought retroactive application of 10 U.S.C.S. § 1408(c)(1), which overruled existing case law on the subject of military retirement benefits. The trial court denied the petition and ruled that the retroactive application was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed and held that Congress intended that the statute be applied retroactively. The court further found that retroactive application did not deprive the husband of vested substantive rights. The court noted that until the decision that held that the benefits were separate property, the parties must have reasonably expected that the pension would have been treated as community property. The court further determined that because the divorce settlement did not address the retirement benefits, the wife's right to the benefits had been preserved.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment entered in favor of the former husband and held that the military retirement benefits were community property. The trial court remanded the case to the trial court for a calculation of the former wife's share of benefits.

 

808 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


DiBenedetto v. Automotive Casualty Ins. Co.


No. 94-CA-35


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-CA-35 (La.App. 5 Cir. 5/31/94); 638 So. 2d 385; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1768



May 31, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FORTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA. DOCKET NO. 23568, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE MADELINE JASMINE, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development appealed from the judgment of the 40th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. John the Baptist (Louisiana) awarding damages in the personal injury action brought by the provisional tutor of decedent's infant against defendants, the driver of the vehicle in which decedent was riding, the driver's insurance company, the state, and the Department. The Department was found liable.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was riding in a vehicle, driven by one of the defendants, on a highway when the vehicle flipped out of control. The decedent died as a result of her injuries. While the driver's blood alcohol level was found to be .05, the state police trooper who investigated the accident did not cite her. Eyewitnesses on the scene soon after the accident all testified that they saw the condition of the highway and that there was no reconstruction going on or any obstacle in the road. It was alleged that the accident was caused by a defect due to the Department's improper testing procedures of materials used in the reconstruction of the highway. The court affirmed the judgment below awarding damages against the Department. The court found that the Department violated its own testing procedures thereby causing the material to be defective, and that such defect created an unreasonably dangerous condition. Further, where the Department was responsible for maintaining the highways and knew it did not follow the proper procedures, the court found there was constructive knowledge of the defect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment awarding damages against the Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development in the personal injury suit against it and others brought by the provisional tutor of the infant of the decedent, who died in the single-car accident. The matter was remanded so that an increased damage award could be assessed against the Department.

 

809 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


No. 93-KA-838


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


93-KA-838 (La.App. 5 Cir. 5/31/94); 638 So. 2d 394; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1770



May 31, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ST. CHARLES NO. 92-0437 DIVISION "C", HONORABLE RUCHE J. MARINO, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Twenty-Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Charles (Louisiana), convicting defendant of possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the officer's stop of his vehicle violated his constitutional rights, that the jury selection was tainted and that his sentence was excessive. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that defendant's traffic violation constituted reasonable cause for a stop. The court then held that the officer had reasonable suspicion based on the fact that the officer was in a high crime area, defendant and his passenger ignored the officer's request to exist the vehicle, and defendant and the passenger acted nervously and kept placing his hands in his groin area leading the officer to believe that he had a weapon. Second, the court held the trial court did not err in denying defendant's challenge for cause as to one juror because the juror's acquaintance with some of the officers did not render him ineligible where the juror had been disassociated from his employment at the sheriff's office and expressed his ability to render a fair and impartial judgment and to hold the state to its burden of proof. Third, the court held that defendant's sentence was not excessive in light of his prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and amended his sentence.

Keller v. Evans Cooperage, Inc.


No. 94-CA-006


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-CA-006 (La.App. 5 Cir. 5/31/94); 641 So. 2d 552; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1787



May 31, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused September 16, 1994. Released for Publication September 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 442-108, DIVISION "I". HONORABLE JO ELLEN GRANT, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiffs, a temporary employee and his mother, against defendant corporation, the employee, the mother, and intervenor insurer sought review of the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, No. 442-108, Division I (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of the corporation on the ground that it was immune from ordinary tort liability under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1032.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who was employed by a temporary employment agency that furnished supplemental workers to the corporation, was injured in the course and scope of his employment at the corporation's plant. The employee brought ordinary tort and intentional tort claims against the corporation; the agency's insurer intervened, seeking reimbursement for worker's compensation benefits paid to the employee. The trial court granted the corporation's motion for summary judgment, holding that the corporation was the employee's statutory employer and that it was therefore immune from ordinary tort liability under § 23:1032; the trial court additionally held that § 23:1032 was constitutional. On appeal the court affirmed. The court held that § 23:1032 did not deny the employee equal protection of the laws or due process by restricting his remedy against the corporation as a statutory employer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

811 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Washington


No. 93-K-2283


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


93-K-2283 (La.App. 4 Cir. 5/26/94); 638 So. 2d 1115; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1557



May 26, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REMAND FROM THE SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA. APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF CERTIORARI AND PROHIBITION. CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NO. 364-515, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Supreme Court of Louisiana, the court was asked to determine if defendant's original sentence for possession of phencyclidine (PCP) was, as determined by the trial court, unconstitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of possession of PCP and sentenced to 10 years at hard labor. Subsequently, the state filed a multiple bill and defendant admitted to a prior conviction of possession of PCP. The trial court vacated and set aside defendant's sentence and sentenced him as a second offender to seven years at hard labor under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. The State contended that defendant's seven year sentence was illegal because it was below the statutory minimum sentence of ten years at hard labor under the habitual offender law. The supreme court remanded to the court to determine if defendant's original sentence was unconstitutionally excessive. The court held that, given the presumption that a sentence under the habitual offender law was constitutional, and considering that defendant was eligible for parole, the minimum sentence mandated by the legislature was not grossly out of proportion to the severity of the crime. The court held that the trial court erred in finding that the enhanced sentence was excessive, and in reducing defendant's sentence below the minimum of ten years at hard labor without credit for good time mandated under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded for resentencing.

 

812 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Trahan


No. 93 KA 1116


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


93 1116 (La.App. 1 Cir. 5/20/94); 637 So. 2d 694; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1722



May 20, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Seventeenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Lafourche, Louisiana. Trial No. 236774. Honorable Sidney A. Ordoyne, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Seventeenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Lafourche (Louisiana), which found him guilty of three counts of vehicular homicide, claiming that he was entitled to a new trial, and that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant struck a car while driving and killed three people. Defendant was charged and convicted of three counts of vehicular homicide, and appealed his conviction. The court held that the evidence was legally sufficient for the jury to find that defendant was the driver of his vehicle at the time of the accident, because his passenger did not know how to operate a truck, and physical evidence indicated that defendant was the driver. The court also determined that it was error for a prosecution witness, the accident investigator, to testify that in his opinion defendant was the driver of the truck that struck the victim's, because under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 704, the expert witness was prohibited from giving an opinion on the ultimate issue. However, the court stated that the evidence was harmless, because defendant's guilt was overwhelming. Finally, the court concluded that defendant's sentence of 10 years imprisonment on each count was not unconstitutionally excessive, because the circumstances did not warrant a less onerous sentencing alternative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court finding defendant guilty.

 

813 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Babin


No. 93 KA 1361


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


93 1361 (La.App. 1 Cir. 5/20/94); 637 So. 2d 814; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1735



May 20, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 23rd Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ascension, Louisiana. Case No. 5732. Honorable A. J. Kling, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a conviction from the 23rd Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ascension of molestation of a juvenile over whom he had control or supervision, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2. Defendant was sentenced to pay a fine and to serve a 48-month term of imprisonment at hard labor. The court suspended the term of imprisonment and placed defendant on supervised probation for five years subject to special conditions.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from a conviction of molestation of a juvenile over whom he had control or supervision, the court affirmed the conviction, and the sentence was affirmed as amended. Defendant, the victim's stepfather, contended that the trial court erred by finding him guilty on the basis of insufficient evidence. The court held that the testimony of the victim alone was sufficient to prove the elements of an offense. The fact that the trial court found defendant guilty indicated that the trial court accepted the victim's testimony and rejected defendant's testimony insofar as he denied committing the offense. On appeal, the appellate court would not assess the credibility of witnesses to overturn a fact finder's determination of guilt. The court found that the evidence proved all of the elements of molestation of a juvenile and defendant's identity as perpetrator. Also, in evaluating whether newly discovered evidence warranted a new trial, the test was whether the new evidence was so material that it ought to produce a verdict different from that rendered at trial. The court rejected defendant's contention that the district court allowed the prosecution to make improper remarks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of molestation of a juvenile over whom he had control or supervision. The court affirmed the sentence as amended by an order deleting certain special conditions of his probation.

 

814 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Albarado v. City of Lafayette


No. 93-1300


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


93-1300 (La.App. 3 Cir. 5/4/94); 640 So. 2d 469; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1403



May 4, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana; the Honorable G. Bradford Ware, presiding.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, engineers employed by the City, sought review of a judgment from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), dismissing defendants, the City and various other City boards and officials, from the engineers' lawsuit claiming that they were aggrieved by certain hiring practices and compensation decisions.


OVERVIEW: The engineers employed by the City filed suit to obtain upward pay adjustments comparable to those received by six other engineers employed by the City. The engineers contended that the Civil Service Board Rule IV, Sec. 1.7, pertaining to incumbent salary realignment, was unconstitutional. The City countered that the engineers did not receive a pay adjustment, because they were either in a different classification or they lacked the requisite educational background and work experience. All parties filed motions for summary judgment, and the trial court ruled in favor of the City and the other defendants. On review, the court held that the suit had to be remanded for joinder and re-trial because the engineers failed to join the Attorney General as an indispensable party. According to the court, the Attorney General was an indispensable party because the civil service rule was alleged to be unconstitutional. The court also noted that only certain engineers in the same pay class would have standing to bring the suit.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal of a judgment dismissing the engineers' suit alleging that a civil service rule was unconstitutional and remanded to the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

815 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walker


No. 26,026-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


26,026 (La.App. 2 Cir. 5/4/94); 637 So. 2d 583; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1365



May 4, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 164,145. Honorable C.J. Bolin, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him of the illegal use of weapons while engaged in a crime of violence in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:94(A) and (F) and sentenced him as a third felony offender to 12 years and 8 months at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Following his conviction of the illegal use of weapons while engaged in a crime of violence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:94, defendant appealed and asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion for mistrial pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 775(3) because, during his trial, the prosecutor threatened to file a bill of information charging one of the defense witnesses with perjury. The appellate court held that defendant failed to demonstrate that he suffered any prejudice precluding a fair trial because of the prosecutor's conduct. Defendant also contended that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction and that the trial court erred by denying his motion for a post-verdict judgment of acquittal. The court held that the assignment of error lacked merit because, when viewed in the light most favorable to the prosecution, the evidence demonstrates that defendant fired a gun at an occupied car. Finally, defendant argued that the sentence imposed was unconstitutional. The court held that defendant failed to sustain his burden on the issue and affirmed both the conviction and the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the sentence imposed by the trial court.

 

816 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jamison


No. CR93-1633


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


CR93-1633 (La.App. 3 Cir. 5/4/94); 640 So. 2d 438; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1409



May 4, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, Honorable Alfred Mansour, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Ninth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Rapides (Louisiana) convicting him of attempted aggravated rape, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27, 14:42. After denying defendant's motion for a new trial, the court sentenced defendant to 20 years at hard labor for the attempted aggravated rape of his stepdaughter.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from a conviction of attempted aggravated rape, the court held that the elements which the prosecution must prove in a prosecution for aggravated rape of a child under 12 were (1) anal or vaginal penetration deemed to be without consent of the victim because of (2) the victim's age at the time of the rape. The jury could have found that the prosecution proved beyond a reasonable doubt that the victim was under the age of 12 at the time of defendant's sexual intercourse. Further, the court found no error in the trial court's failure to instruct the jury as defendant requested. Defendant's proposed instruction did not meet the requirements of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 807. Also, other sex crimes against the same victim were admissible in a prosecution for aggravated rape. The court held that a sentence imposed within statutory limits would not be deemed excessive in the absence of manifest abuse of discretion. The sentencing court had ample grounds for an upward departure from the guidelines grid range and correctly characterized that the case called for a greater sentence than that shown in the Louisiana Felony Sentencing Guidelines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for attempted aggravated rape, with instructions.

State v. Fairley


No. 25,951-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT

State v. Billings


No. CR93-1542


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


CR93-1542 (La.App. 3 Cir. 5/4/94); 640 So. 2d 500; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1391



May 4, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana; the Honorable W. Ross Foote, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction entered in the Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which accepted defendant's guilty plea to a reduced charge of attempted aggravated rape and sentenced him to 15 years at hard labor, subject to defendant's right to review the denial of his motion to introduce evidence of the victim's prior sexual activity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for aggravated rape. He pled guilty to the reduced charge of attempted aggravated rape and was sentenced to 15 years at hard labor and also ordered to submit to a psychological evaluation. Prior to pleading guilty to the reduced charge and before sentencing, defendant filed a motion to introduce prior sexual activity. After its denial, defendant entered a plea, reserving his right to review the denial of his motion to introduce prior sexual activity. Defendant attempted to argue that the medical records from a certain hospital established that the victim already had inappropriate knowledge of certain sexual activities and that the victim's knowledge and the alleged sexual abuse was possibly a result of the victim's biological father or uncle molesting her, and not defendant. The court found that defendant's motion was properly denied based on relevancy, because the timing of the victim's hospitalization and the timing of defendant becoming a member of her family raised the probability that it was defendant who committed these crimes upon the victim. The court upheld defendant's conviction, but amended his sentence to allow him credit for time served.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for attempted aggravated rape. However, the court amended defendant's sentence to allow credit for time served. The case was remanded to the trial court to amend the commitment and minute entry of the sentence to reflect that defendant was given credit for time served and to inform defendant of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief.

 

819 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Langley


K94-326


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-326 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/14/94); 635 So. 2d 784; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1208



April 14, 1994, Decided  
March 11, 1994, Lodged


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, Honorable Fred Godwin, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On an application for writ of certiorari from the 14th Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, defendant raised multiple claims of error related to pre-trial rulings in his capital murder trial which included a challenge to the finding of validity of the parole violation warrant used to arrest him, and a challenge to a ruling on the limitation on evidence of diminished capacity under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 651.


OVERVIEW: On defendant's writ application, the court determined that the Georgia parole violation warrant on which the Louisiana authorities relied to arrest defendant was not stale, and its execution was not unreasonably delayed. Defendant's whereabouts were not known for all but a total of three months from the time the warrant was issued until his arrest. The actions of the Georgia authorities, initiating the process for transfer of parole supervision to Louisiana, did not vitiate the warrant or establish a waiver of Georgia's right to enforce it. Until the transfer of parole supervision was completed, Georgia retained authority to execute the warrant. Therefore, there is no error in the trial court's ruling that the parole violation warrant was valid. Also, because the defense of diminished capacity was not recognized in Louisiana, defendant could not introduce evidence of a mental condition or defect which rendered him incapable of forming specific intent to commit a crime, unless he entered a dual plea of not guilty and not guilty by reason of insanity as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. Art. 651. Therefore, defendant's motion to quash was properly denied.


OUTCOME: Defendant's request for a stay of the capital murder proceedings was denied.

 

820 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Price


No. 93-KA-1472


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


93-1472 (La.App. 4 Cir. 4/14/94); 635 So. 2d 1298; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 991



April 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 269-823, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, granted an out of time appeal, complained of his conviction by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), of first degree murder and sentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defense counsel did not file a contemporaneous objection, so the issue of the constitutionality of the charge on the definition of "reasonable doubt" was not preserved for appeal. Because counsel's failure to object to the charge in this case occurred prior to Cage v. Louisiana, 498 U.S. 39, 111 S.Ct. 328, 112 L.Ed.2d 339 (1990), the failure to object could not have been deficient. The court held that there was sufficient testimony for the jury to conclude that the victim was not armed and defendant did not reasonably believe he was in imminent danger of losing his life or receiving great bodily harm. Viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, a rational factfinder could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant did not act in self-defense. The court concluded that a rational trier of fact, viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, could have found that the mitigating factors of "heat of blood" and "sudden passion" were not established by a preponderance of the evidence, and the jury could have found that the defendant had the specific intent to kill or inflict great bodily harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

Southside Civic Ass'n v. Warrington


No. 93 CA 0890


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


93-0890 (La.App. 1 Cir. 4/8/94); 635 So. 2d 721; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 900



April 8, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 386,931. Honorable Robert D. Downing, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff civic association appealed a decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which sustained a peremptory exception pleading the objection of no cause of action and dismissed its suit against defendants, a homeowner and a city.


OVERVIEW: The homeowner requested a zoning variance. The Board of Adjustment granted the request. The civic association filed suit pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4727E(1) requesting judicial review of the Board's decision. The homeowner filed a dilatory exception pleading the objection of pleading nonconformity with La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 891. The city filed a similar dilatory exception and later filed peremptory exceptions pleading the objections of peremption and no right of action. The civic association filed an amended petition. The trial court sustained the exception of no cause of action based on peremption and overruled all other exceptions as moot. On appeal the court found that because the only difference between the original petition and the amended petition was that the latter added the verification required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4727E(1), the trial court should have allowed the amended petition to relate back to the date of filing of the original petition. The court held that because the original petition set forth a cause of action within the time required by the statute, any subsequent amendment curing a technical deficiency related back.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court sustaining the exception pleading the objection of no cause of action was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

822 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Dockery v. DuPont


No. 93-1021


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


93-1021 (La.App. 3 Cir. 4/6/94); 635 So. 2d 679; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1002



April 6, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF RAPIDES, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HON. B. DEXTER RYLAND, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED as AMENDED and RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tax purchasers and their buyers appealed from the summary judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Rapides (Louisiana) annulling the purchase of certain land at a tax sale and setting aside the subsequent conveyance of the land by the tax purchasers to their buyers, whose exception of prescription was overruled. Plaintiff successors in title to the land had filed the petition to annul such tax sale.


OVERVIEW: The buyers of the subject land from the tax purchasers urged that the five-year period in which to file a petition to annul a tax sale had expired, and argued that the judgment below for the petitioners, the successors in title to such land, was error. The mortgagees of the land had conveyed it to the successors in title after the mortgagees had reacquired the land from the mortgagors, the original grantees, in a bankruptcy proceeding. However, unbeknownst to the mortgagors and mortgagees, the land previously had been sold in a tax sale, due to the mortgagors' unpaid tax debt, and then sold to the buyers. Yet the mortgagors remained in continuous corporeal possession of the land. The court, inter alia, affirmed the judgment and held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180 required notice to tax debtors of tax delinquency and a pending tax sale and that the tax sale therefore was a nullity where the mortgagors, as tax debtors, received no notice thereof. Further, the petition to annul the tax sale had not prescribed, as the five-year period in which to annul a tax sale either did not commence or had been interrupted by the mortgagors' continuous corporeal possession of the land.


OUTCOME: The court amended and affirmed the summary judgment annulling the tax purchasers' acquisition of the property in question and setting aside their subsequent conveyance of the property. The judgment was amended to require the successors in title to such property to pay the purchase price, inter alia, to the buyers to whom the subject property had been conveyed by the tax purchasers.

City of Crowley v. Comeaux


No. 93-1116


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


93-1116 (La.App. 3 Cir. 4/6/94); 638 So. 2d 658; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3837



April 6, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Office of Workers Compensation, Louisiana Department of Labor; Sheral Keller, Hearing Officer, Presiding. Previously Reported at: 637 So. 2d 565 and Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of the judgment of the Office of Workers Compensation, Louisiana Department of Labor, which had found that employee was subject to an offset against the Social Security disability benefits he was receiving. The employee argued that the office had improperly accepted defendant employer's argument that the employee was permanently totally disabled.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, the employee, a former technician possessing some education in electronics, was injured while employed as a laborer by the employer. The employee received disability benefits. The employer filed a petition styled as a petition for workers compensation offset. The office found that the employee was permanently totally disabled, and thus subject to an offset under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1225 against the social security disability benefits he was receiving. On review, the court reversed. The court held that the office improperly found the employee was permanenetly totally disabled under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 1:3, 1:4, 23:1221, 23:1225, 23:1226A, B(1)(a) - (g), (2), (3), D, and La. Const. art. 1, §§ 1, 3 (1974) where the office failed to consider the possible benefits of rehabilitation and retraining, and where the employee was unable to return to work without additional training. The court noted the public policy goal that every worker regardless of age or class of the pursuit of the increasingly indistinguishable hopes of rehabilitation and reemployment. The court further found that the employee ws entitled to short-term or long-term retraining.


OUTCOME: The court held in favor of the employee, reversed the judgment of the office, and remanded. The court ordered that the employee was to have been offered short-term or long-term retraining.

Coleman v. Caddo Parish Sch. Bd.


No. 25,617-CA, No. 25,925-CW, No. 25,931-CW (consolidated cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


25,617 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/31/94); 635 So. 2d 1238; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 756



March 31, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted in Part, Denied in Part May 2, 1994, Reported at: 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1282. Released for Publication May 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed and on Application for Writs from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 385,230. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment on appeal AFFIRMED IN PART, AMENDED IN PART, AND RECAST. Contempt judgments REVERSED AND SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, school board and school board president, sought review of the judgment from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) in favor of plaintiff parents, which struck certain passages from sex education textbooks used by the schools as violative of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:281.


OVERVIEW: Parents contended that passages in the sex education curricula adopted by the school board (board) violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:281. The trial court found that several passages did violate the law and ordered them struck. After the decision, the president of the school board commented adversely about the trial judge's ruling, and the board's method of implementing the trial court order was not totally effective. The trial court therefore found the board and the president in contempt. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the trial court did not use an improper standard of review to evaluate the curricula. The trial court's findings that the statements regarding morals and sex violated the statute was not clearly wrong. The court replaced passages suggesting that students abstain from homosexual acts. The court affirmed the trial court's enjoining of statements concerning AIDS as factually inaccurate. The board's contempt citation was reversed because they only acted negligently. The board president's contempt conviction was reversed because even if she intended to show disrespect for the court, her speech was constitutionally protected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's judgment striking certain passages from the textbooks. The court held that while a number of statements in the texts did violate the statute's ban on religious beliefs or inaccurate statements, some did not. The board's contempt was reversed because it was only negligent, while the board president's contempt was reversed because her speech was constitutionally protected.

Craig v. Scandia, Inc.


No. 25,707-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


25,707 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/30/94); 634 So. 2d 944; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 685



March 30, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 28, 1994. Released for Publication May 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Eleventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 45,681. Honorable Elizabeth A. Pickett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the parents of decedent, sought review of the order of the Eleventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto, Louisiana, that granted the peremptory exception of no right of action made by appellees, the decedent's employer and power company, in appellants' wrongful death action under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315. Appellees argued that decedent left a surviving spouse and the parents had no statutory right of action.


OVERVIEW: Decedent died while at work and appellants, her parents, brought a wrongful death action against appellees, employer and others, on her behalf. Appellees filed a peremptory exception of no right of action and contended that decedent left a surviving spouse, therefore, the parents had no right of action under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315. The trial court granted the exception. The parents argued that the statute was unconstitutional since their daughter had been judicially separated from her husband for over four years, and her husband had not suffered any damages as a result of her death. The court affirmed the dismissal and held that, although they were separated, the decedent left a surviving spouse within the meaning of art. 2315. The court held that art. 2315 should be strictly construed and did not authorize the parents, as members of a secondary class of beneficiaries, to proceed even if the husband, primary beneficiary, renounced his rights. The court further held that the issue of the constitutionality of the statute was not properly raised in the trial court and would not be considered on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the exception of no right of action because the deceased left a surviving spouse and her parents were not authorized to bring the wrongful death action.

Police Ass'n v. City of New Orleans


No. 93-CA-1279 CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 93-CA-2057


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


93-1279 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/29/94); 635 So. 2d 380; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 748



March 29, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NOS. 91-3990 C/W 90-23634, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE GERALD P. FEDOROFF, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, police and firefighters association, sought review of a judgment from the Civil District Court, for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which upheld the constitutionality of a city ordinance referred to as the "domicile ordinance." The ordinance was designed to require certain city employees, including the police and firefighters, to be domiciled in the city.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city passed a domicile ordinance to require city employees to reside within the city. A prior trial court decision had issued an injunction preventing the city from enforcing the ordinance. The city appealed and the Louisiana Supreme Court upheld the ordinance. The city then amended the ordinance. The amendment redefined "domicile" and provided that the only employees exempted from the domicile requirement were those employees who were hired prior to a certain date and they were denied promotional opportunities. The trial court upheld the amendment. The court reversed and rendered judgment that the amended ordinance, which denied promotional opportunities to certain employees was unconstitutional and violated the due process and equal protection articles of Louisiana's constitution. The court held that the attempt to permanently bar promotional opportunities to certain incumbent classified civil service employees destroyed the competitive promotional system based on merit and infringed upon the civil service commission's express and exclusive powers to adopt rules regulating promotion and establishing a general system of promotion pursuant to La. Const. art. X, § 7.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the trial court and rendered judgment that the ordinance as amended violated the state constitution.

State v. Littleton


No. 94-K-0462


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-0462 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/29/94); 635 So. 2d 398; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 733



March 29, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NO. 366-933, SECTION "E". HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans (Louisiana) that sentenced defendant to serve 12 months in prison following her guilty pleas to charges of crime against nature by solicitation and two prior felony convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to crime against nature by solicitation. When she appeared for sentencing, the State filed a multiple bill charging her with two prior felony convictions entered on the same date. She pled guilty to the charge, and she was found to be a second offender. The trial court refused to impose the minimum sentence, and instead sentenced her to serve 12 months at hard labor with credit for time served. In affirming the decision, the court held that a lesser sentence than the minimum under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 could be imposed, and the trial judge was entitled to find the imposition of the minimum sentence under § 15:529.1 was excessive. The fact that the trial judge found the whole concept--that consensual sex for hire was a crime--to be repugnant did not mean that he found the crime or the penalty itself to be unconstitutional. The reasons given for the imposition of less than the minimum sentence were sufficient to support the decision to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision sentencing defendant to 12 months in prison following her convictions.

829 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Rankins v. Louisiana State Bd. of Elementary & Secondary Educ.


No. 93 CA 1879


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


93 1879 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/17/94); 637 So. 2d 548; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1444



March 17, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana Trial Court No. 394,923, Honorable Joseph Keogh, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state board of education sought review of an order of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which issued a preliminary injunction prohibiting the board of education from withholding plaintiff students' high school diplomas despite their graduation exit examination (GEE) failure.


OVERVIEW: The students sought the award of their high school diplomas and a declaration as to the invalidity of the board of education's GEE policy. The trial court held that the GEE had been unconstitutionally administered in violation of the equal protection clause of the federal and state constitutions. The court held that the board of education had authority to establish the GEE as a requirement for obtaining a state diploma and that the trial court erred in holding that the GEE was being administered in violation of the equal protection clause. Under constitutional proscriptions, the board of education could not dictate the curriculum or set exit exam requirements in non-public schools; to do so would be an "excessive entanglement" violative of U.S. Const. amend. I. The state could impose an exit exam requirement on students without violating equal protection provided the exam was specifically tied to the curriculum. The court held that the GEE did not violate the equal protection clause because its administration was rationally related to the state's legitimate interest of insuring minimum competency among persons obtaining a state diploma.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the district court's judgment which stated that the GEE violated the equal protection clause and vacated the preliminary injunction issued with respect to the students' diplomas.

 

830 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Toliver


No. 93-KA-909


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


93-909 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/16/94); 635 So. 2d 1190; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 814



March 16, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA NUMBER 93-66, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE DOUGLAS A. ALLEN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a sentence imposed by the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), in which he was sentenced as an habitual offender to 49 1/2 years imprisonment. Defendant argued that the habitual offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, was an unconstitutional violation of the separation of powers provided for in La. Const. art. 2, § 2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to armed robbery and was sentenced as an habitual offender to 49 1/2 years imprisonment. On appeal, defendant argued that the habitual offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, was an unconstitutional violation of the separation of powers provided for in La. Const. art. 2, § 2, because the legislature usurped the courts' sentencing discretion. The court disagreed and affirmed defendant's sentence. By imposing certain habitual offender statutes and corresponding penalties, the Legislature merely established a procedure which enabled a district attorney to seek and the courts to exact more severe sentences on defendants who repeatedly violated the criminal laws. The legislature acted within its constitutional authority which allowed it to determine and define a crime and provide its penalty. It did not delegate any of its duties to the judicial or executive branches, nor did it usurp the judiciary's discretion in sentencing a defendant. Accordingly, no separation of powers violation existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence as a habitual offender.

 

831 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Ieyoub v. Phipps


No. 93 CA 0603


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


93 0603 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/11/94); 634 So. 2d 51; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 791



March 11, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana Trial Court No. 383,730. Honorable Joseph F. Keogh, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which permanently enjoined defendant and his agents from engaging in the promotion, solicitation and sale of what the court characterized as a pyramid scheme in Louisiana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's Paymaster Profit Systems/Multi-Fax plan operated by allowing an individual to purchase an informational kit from a success consultant or sponsor for $ 179. Defendant would receive $ 79.00 and the sponsor would receive $ 100. The $ 100.00 payment placed the individual at the bottom of a payment chain. To maintain a place in the chain, an individual had to pay up-line sponsors a total of $ 1,000.00 per month. To receive money, the individual would have to line up new sales of the informational kit. The court affirmed the injunction. The court concluded that the trial court's determination that the Paymaster plan was an illegal pyramid scheme because it was a chain distributor system and therefore in violation of the Unfair Trade Practices Act was correct. Defendant's contention that he was not connected with the scheme was false as he maintained the program, referred to the program as his and admitted a direct financial interest in perpetuating the scheme. The purpose of the licensing statutes that defendant avoided was to protect the public from fraudulent conduct on the part of those operating endless chain businesses and was a valid exercise of state police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to permanently enjoin defendant and his agents from engaging in the promotion, solicitation and sale of what the trial court characterized as a pyramid scheme in Louisiana.

 

832 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Benoit v. Maco Mfg.


93 CA 0396


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


93 0396 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/11/94); 633 So. 2d 1301; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 779



March 11, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from District 7 Office of Workers' Compensation Administration, State of Louisiana, Suit No. 91-03218. Honorable Pamela Moses Laramore, Hearing Officer



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a ruling by the Office of Workers' Compensation Administration (Louisiana) that denied him compensation benefits, and dismissed his action against defendant employer after it found that the employee's heart attack was not a "work-related" injury under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1021(7)(3).


OVERVIEW: The employee challenged the ruling of the office of workers' compensation administration that denied and dismissed his claim for workers' compensation benefits. The office found that the employee's heart attack was not work-related under § 23:1021(7)(3). The court affirmed and found that the employee asserted that § 23:1021(7)(3) was constitutionally vague. The employee argued that he was required to prove that his physical stress that allegedly caused his heart attack was greater than that of the "average worker." The court held that although the term "average worker" was not defined, there was nothing in the language of the statute that was so vague as to have deprived the employee of his due process rights. The court noted that the term took its literal meaning from the dictionary, and that the meaning of the term was clear and unambiguous. The court rejected the employee's equal protection claim, and held that a rational distinction existed for the employee's burden of proof by clear and convincing evidence that his heart attack was work-related, and the burden of proof by a preponderance of the evidence that other workers had to meet for other work-related injuries.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the Office of Workers' Compensation Administration that denied and dismissed the employee's claim for workers' compensation benefits.

 

833 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Bozeman v. Reed


No. 92 CA 0858


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


92 0858 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/11/94); 633 So. 2d 944; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 763



March 11, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, SUIT NUMBER 343,212, HONORABLE BOB DOWNING, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART, AMENDED AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Public Safety and Corrections (DPS) sought review of the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which found it solely at fault in breaching its duty under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:403.2 in its licensing of decedent driver with multiple sclerosis, resulting in damages to plaintiffs, a passenger and survivors of accident victims, when the driver allegedly failed to react to an emergency.


OVERVIEW: When a car switched lanes in front of his car, the driver swerved across the medial strip and collided head on with another vehicle, killing himself and a married couple and injuring a passenger. Pretrial settlements in the various ensuing suits eliminated several defendants, leaving only the DPS and the driver's liability insurer. On appeal from the adverse judgment, the DPS argued that the trial court erred in finding it liable and failing to find the driver liable. In reversing in part, the court ruled that, in issuing and renewing his operator's license, the DPS breached its duty under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:403.2 to obtain a detailed medical report on the driver and to adopt procedures for protecting the public from the risk presented by his potentially dangerous physical disability. The court held that state immunity did not arise under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1 because no policy decision was involved. The court also ruled that the driver had a duty to refrain from driving if he were physically impaired, even if he were mistakenly licensed by the state, and that the failure to allocate 50 percent fault to him was error. The court affirmed the quantum of damages.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's finding of no liability of the deceased driver, amended the judgment to reduce the recovery against DPS to reflect the 50 percent fault allocated to the driver, and rendered judgment against the driver's liability insurer.

Chamberlain ex rel. Chamberlain v. State ex rel. Department of Transp. & Dev.


No. CA 91 1942R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


91 1942 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/11/94); 633 So. 2d 871; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 797



March 11, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 1994.
Related proceeding at Chamberlain v. Kennedy, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3726 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 31, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Terrebonne, Louisiana, Trial Court No. 88836. Honorable Paul R. Wimbish, Judge
Chamberlain v. State ex rel. Department of Transp., 624 So. 2d 874, 1993 La. LEXIS 2467 (La., 1993)



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state department of transportation appealed the judgment of the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), which held that plaintiffs, parents and injured minor, were entitled to $ 2,000,000 in damages for the minor's near-drowning accident, because the minor received extensive injures and required care for the rest of his life.


OVERVIEW: A minor almost drowned in an accident, and suffered extensive mental and physical damages. The minor and the parents sued the state department of transportation. The trial court awarded the parents $ 2,000,000 and the State appealed the ruling. On remand, the court held that because the minor had suffered severe injuries, and required care for the rest of his life, the statutory limit did not adequately reflect the amount of damages the minor suffered. The court concluded that the trial court's award of $ 2,000,000 was reasonable, and that the parents were entitled to a prejudgment interest rate of 12 percent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court in favor of the parents and the minor.

Bueto v. Video Gaming Div., Office of State Police, Dep't of Pub. Safety


94 CA 0334


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 0334 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/04/94); 637 So. 2d 544; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 1446



March 4, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish, Trial Court No. 399,649, Honorable Frank Saia, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART, AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the state's video gaming division, appealed from a decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which declared La. Admin. Code tit. 55, § 4215(A)(1)(e)(iii), (iv), (v) and (vi) to be invalid and unconstitutional, permanently enjoined future enforcement of the provisions and ordered issuance of a Type V video poker license to plaintiff, a truck stop operator.


OVERVIEW: The video gaming division denied the truck stop operator a video gaming license on the basis of La. Admin. Code tit. 55, § 4215(A)(1)(e)(iii), which provided that no truck stop facility constructed after September 6, 1991, would be allowed to apply for a license for a period of two years. The court affirmed the finding of invalidity, the permanent injunction against enforcement of the rules, and the issuance of the license to the operator. The court determined that the matter was properly before it in a judicial proceeding to review the validity of an agency rule under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:963 because the operator made a prior request for agency review and no remedy would have resulted from a contested adjudicated case. The administrative provisions establishing the two-year rule were invalid because the state police exceeded the authority given it by the legislature in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4862.6A. The state police were not allowed to add the additional two-year qualification. The mandatory injunction was appropriate to enforce the declaratory judgment because the parties stipulated that the only reason for denying the license was the invalid two-year rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that administrative code provisions were invalid, but reversed the determination of unconstitutionality as unnecessary and inappropriate, and affirmed the injunction prohibiting enforcement of the invalid rules and the mandatory injunction granting the truck stop operator a license.

 

836 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Town of Berwick v. Justilian


No. 93-854


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


93-854 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/02/94); 634 So. 2d 1365; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 560



March 2, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from District 04, Office of Workers Compensation, State of Louisiana, Sheral C. Kellar, Hearing Officer, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant claimant appealed from the decision of the Office of Workers' Compensation (Louisiana), which found that plaintiff employer was entitled under La. Rev. Stat. § 23:1225(C)(1)(b) to a set-off for old age benefits by the claimant when the claimant received those benefits before becoming employed by the employer and the employer did not contribute anything to the claimant's social security old age account.


OVERVIEW: The retired claimant received old age Social Security benefits that had been equally funded by his contributions and those of his previous employer when the employer hired him. The claimant was injured while working for the employer and sought workers' compensation benefits. The court affirmed the determination that under La. Rev. Stat. § 23:1225C(1)(b) the employer could reduce the claimant's workers' compensation benefits due to the claimant's receipt of Social Security old-age benefits before he was employed by the employer and the employer did not contribute anything to the claimant's social security old-age account. Had the claimant been injured prior to the effective date of § 23:1225C(1)(b) he would have been entitled to the relief sought; however, the governing law in workers' compensation actions was that which was in effect at the time of the alleged injury. The clear and unambiguous language of the statute indicated that the "social security reduction" of workers' compensation to which an employer might be entitled was applicable only to certain social security disability benefits, not to social security benefits payable by reasonable of attainment of a specified age.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the hearing officer's determination that the employer was entitled to a set-off for old-age benefits by the claimant when the claimant received such benefits before he was employed by the employer and the employer did not contribute anything to the claimant's social security old-age account.

Estate of Williams v. Louisiana Office of Risk Management


No. 93-795


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


93-795 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/02/94); 634 So. 2d 1260; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 552



March 2, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 3, State of Louisiana. Robert P. Shelton, Hearing Officer, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Louisiana Office of Risk Management (Risk Management) appealed from the judgment of the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 3 (Louisiana), which awarded death benefits to plaintiff estate.


OVERVIEW: In 1987 the decedent suffered a work-related heart attack and was rendered disabled. The condition required daily doses of medication and periodic visits to treating physicians. The decedent suffered a second heart attack in 1991 and died shortly thereafter. The estate sought death benefits under La. Rev. Stat. § 23:1231. The court affirmed the denial of Risk Management's peremptory exception because the legislative amendment of § 23:1231A could be applied retroactively to revive a claim extinguished by preemption more than three years prior to the amendment's effective date. The statute created a right of action and defined its existence with reference to a specific time period within which death of the worker had to occur; thus, the time period was neither prescriptive nor preemptive. The statute applied retroactively because it was procedural and did not disturb Risk Management's rights, as it provided that the time from which the two year period would begin to run was suspended as long as the injured worker was being treated for his work-related accident. The court reversed the death benefits award because the only issue before the hearing officer was the peremptory exception.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the hearing officer's retroactive application of a legislative amendment to revive a claim extinguished by preemption more than three years prior to the amendment's effective date. The court reversed the hearing officer's award of death benefits to the estate.
