State v. 1979 Cadillac Deville


No. 24,954-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


24,954-CA (La.App. 2 Cir. 2/28/94); 632 So. 2d 1221; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 428



February 28, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 24, 1994. Released for Publication March 24, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 372,430. Honorable C. J. Bolin, Jr., Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted drug possessor sought review of a judgment from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which pursuant to a civil action filed by the State ordered the forfeiture of the drug possessor's vehicle and cash. The drug possessor claimed that the forfeiture violated his rights against double jeopardy under the U.S. Const. amend. V and La. Const. art. V, § 8.


OVERVIEW: The drug possessor was arrested for the possession of cocaine with the intent to distribute. During the course of the arrest, his vehicle and a small amount of cash were seized. He was sentenced to one year in prison. Thereafter, the State filed a civil forfeiture action for the forfeiture of the vehicle and the cash. The trial court ordered their forfeitures. He appealed and claimed that the proceeding was a violation of his rights against double jeopardy. The court reversed and found under the facts of the case that the forfeiture of the automobile did constitute punishment in violation of the double jeopardy clause. The court held that the forfeitures did not occur because the items were contraband and they were not instrumentalities of the crime. And the forfeiture of the vehicle could not be said to serve a solely remedial purpose. The court noted that single proceedings for both the criminal action and the forfeiture would have solved the double jeopardy problem.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the trial court and held that the forfeiture of the items constituted double jeopardy.

State v. Stroughter


No. 25,630-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


25,630-KA (La.App. 2 Cir. 2/25/94); 632 So. 2d 923; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 741



February 25, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 24, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 136,675. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, III, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his resentence entered by the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), on a conviction for armed robbery, to 30 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant contended that the resentencing judge erred because the original sentencing judge did not state that the sentence was without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to armed robbery, and the trial court sentenced him to 30 years at hard labor under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64. The statute provided for a mandatory sentence without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence, but the trial court failed to state such conditions. Defendant filed a motion to correct illegal sentence, and the trial court resentenced him to 30 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant filed a motion to reconsider, which was denied. Defendant appealed and alleged that the resentencing judge erred in determining that the original sentencing judge intended to impose the conditions, because he failed to state them in the sentence and, therefore, his intent could not be determined. The court affirmed the sentence and held that the resentencing judge reviewed the facts and circumstances, including the entire record, and did not err in his sentence, which was within the guidelines and therefore not excessive. The court found no patent errors, but the court amended the sentence to show credit for time served.


OUTCOME: The court amended the sentence to reflect credit for time served and, as amended, affirmed the sentence.

State v. Bagneris


No. 93-K-2454


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


93-K-2454 (La.App. 4 Cir. 2/25/94); 633 So. 2d 835; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 417



February 25, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI AND PROHIBITION FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 366-257, SECTION "B". HONORABLE PATRICK G. QUINLAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought a writ of certiorari and prohibition from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which sentenced defendant to a suspended sentence of four years at hard labor, with two years of active probation, for possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had pleaded guilty to simple robbery six months previously, pled guilty to possession of cocaine and was sentenced by the trial court to a suspended sentence of four years at hard labor, with two years of active probation on various conditions. The trial court denied the state's motion to correct sentence, and the state sought a writ of certiorari. The court granted the writ and vacated the sentence. The court held that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893(A) and (B) permitted a court to suspend a sentence on a second offense only if it found that the offense occurred at least five years after satisfaction of the sentence imposed for the first conviction. The court held that because less than five years had elapsed from the defendant's plea in the prior case the trial court erred by suspending the defendant's sentence and placing him on probation. The court held, however, that if the sentence was the result of a plea bargain, the guilty plea would be constitutionally infirm where the state could not fulfill the bargain. The court remanded the case for a hearing on whether the guilty plea should be vacated based upon breach of a plea bargain.


OUTCOME: The court granted a writ of certiorari to the state, vacated the sentence, and remanded the case for a hearing on whether the guilty plea should be vacated based upon breach of a plea bargain.

 

841 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Saucier v. Favorite


93-CA-886


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


93-CA-886 (La.App. 5 Cir. 2/23/94); 632 So. 2d 11; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 519



February 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 17, 1994. Released for Publication March 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 405-485. HONORABLE ERNEST V. RICHARDS, IV



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an automobile accident case, the Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA) moved for partial summary judgment on the issue of whether plaintiff was required to first exhaust her remedies against defendant, her underinsured motorist liability insurer, before seeking recovery from LIGA. The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) ruled in favor of LIGA and the insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court was whether the Nonduplication of Recovery Statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386, which regulated liability of LIGA, had retroactive application. The claim was pending on the effective date of Act 237 of 1992, which amended § 22:1386, because partial summary judgment on the case was rendered after the effective date, and the judgment was not yet final due to the appeal. The court held that retroactive application of the amendment did not violate the federal or state constitutional prohibitions against impairment of contractual obligations. As such, the 1992 amendment applied retroactively and required plaintiff to exhaust her remedies against her underinsured motorist liability insurer before seeking recovery from LIGA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court judgment.

State v. Johnson


No. 93-K-2557


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT

DISPOSITION: APPLICATION GRANTED; REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: By application for writ of certiorari and prohibition, the State sought review of a ruling from the Criminal District Court, Section "D," Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion for a new trial with respect to a charge of possession of more than 400 grams of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by bill of information with possession of cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F)(3), and being a convicted felon in possession of a firearm, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1. Previously, the State had sent a notice of a pending forfeiture pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2608(3)(A) with respect to $ 976 seized from defendant at his arrest. The court found that the amount forfeited, $ 976, did not constitute a sanction overwhelmingly disproportionate to the damages defendant caused. The court ruled that the amount forfeited to the government did not qualify as "punishment," but rather was rationally related to the goal of compensating the State for its loss.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's writ application and reversed the ruling of the trial court. The court remanded the case to the trial court for proceedings consistent with its opinion.

 

843 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Duplechin


No. 93-806


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


93-806 (La.App. 3 Cir. 2/2/94); 631 So. 2d 669; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 210



February 2, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Fred Godwin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana) imposing prison time for her marijuana distribution convictions instead of granting probation, arguing that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of distribution of marijuana. Almost three months later, she was charged with twelve similar counts. Subsequently, after defendant pled guilty to seven counts, she was sentenced to seven concurrent five-year terms of imprisonment. While the trial judge was inclined to grant probation, he did not, finding that she was ineligible under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893, which prohibited a suspended sentence for a defendant charged with any other felony since the date of first conviction. On appeal, defendant contended that art. 893 was unconstitutional. The court noted that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1(B), overrode the requirements of art. 893, so that a sentence in the discretionary sanction zone was subject to probation even though probation was barred by art. 893. Because the trial court improperly relied on La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893 in denying defendant probation where her criminal history index classification fell within the discretionary sanction zone, the court vacated her sentence and remanded the case with instructions for the trial court to consider probation in accordance with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1(B).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court denying defendant a sentence suspension was vacated and the case was remanded to the trial court so that it could consider imposing probation as provided by statute.

State v. Laroux

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 11th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Sabine, Louisiana, which convicted him of illegal possession of stolen things in violation of La. OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to illegal possession of stolen things pursuant to a plea bargain agreement. He was sentenced to two years at hard labor. The sentence was suspended and he was placed on probation, subject to the conditions that he pay a monthly probation fee of $ 31, submit to random drug tests, and pay a $ 3,000 fine plus costs. The court affirmed, and held that: (1) the trial court committed a patent error when it failed to notify defendant of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief as required by La. Code Crim. The court ordered the trial court to inform defendant of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief.

State v. Gamble

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Thirty-Sixth Judicial District Court, Parish of Beauregard (Louisiana), which convicted him of one count of distribution of marijuana, a schedule I controlled dangerous substance, in violation of La. OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of one count of distribution of marijuana, a schedule I controlled dangerous substance. The conviction was the result of a transaction in which defendant helped undercover officers purchase marijuana. State v. Kennedy


No. 93-KA-776


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


93-KA-776 (La.App. 5 Cir. 1/25/94); 631 So. 2d 1195; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 123



January 25, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON. NO. 92-7075 DIVISION "D". HONORABLE WALTER E. KOLLIN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of six counts of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:27 and two counts of attempted armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:64.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for six counts of armed robbery and two counts of attempted armed robbery based upon four separate incidents whereupon several of the victims either directly identified defendant or the shotgun and vehicle used in the crimes. The court affirmed defendant's convictions. Defendant's request to approach the jury so they could compare his actual features with those described by the victims was properly denied because defendant was either seated or standing at the defense table at all times during trial. Thus, defendant was allowed to exhibit his scar to the jury although he was not allowed to physically approach them. In addition, defense counsel thoroughly cross-examined all witnesses about any discrepancies in the identification. Although the trial judge could have elaborated more on the reasons for imposing consecutive sentences, the sentences were not excessive and did not violate La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 883. Defendant created a "reign of terror." The victims were placed in very grave danger and could have easily been killed. Given the serious nature of the crime, consecutive sentences were not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for six counts of armed robbery and two counts of attempted armed robbery.

 

847 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilson


No. 93-KA-617


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


93-KA-617 (La.App. 5 Cir. 1/25/94); 631 So. 2d 1213; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 113



January 25, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 17, 1994.
Writ denied by State v. Wilson, 644 So. 2d 1046, 1994 La. LEXIS 2566 (La., Nov. 4, 1994)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, Remanded by Wilson v. Cain, 1999 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 22664 (E.D. La., Feb. 11, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON. STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 87-1246. DIVISION "C". THE HONORABLE JO ELLEN GRANT, JUDGE
State v. Wilson, 538 So. 2d 1124, 1989 La. App. LEXIS 260 (La.App. 5 Cir., 1989)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who had been convicted of two counts of first degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and sentenced to life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence, sought review of the denial, by the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, of his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the trial court's refusal to grant post-conviction relief. It held that, where defendant failed to contemporaneously object to the jury instruction on reasonable doubt, as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 841, 801, the trial court properly denied his application for post-conviction relief on this ground. The court further held that there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's verdict that defendant was guilty of both counts of first degree murder. The court also held that information regarding the identity of three witnesses sought by defendant did not constitute exculpatory evidence, and that where defendant was given ample opportunity at trial to cross-examine two detectives about statements taken from the witnesses and defendant knew of the existence of the witnesses and could have subpoenaed them himself, no actual prejudice was shown to defendant, and thus any failure by the state to disclose was not reversible error. The court finally held that a review of both trial and appellate counsels' performances reflected that defendant was afforded effective legal representation within the guarantees of the Sixth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying defendant's application for post-conviction relief.

Department of Social Servs. v. Shano


No. 93-CA-607


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


93-CA-607 (La.App. 5 Cir. 1/25/94); 631 So. 2d 1263; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 106



January 25, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JUVENILE COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON. STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 84-CN-613. SECTION "B". HONORABLE THOMAS P. MCGEE, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed a decision of the Juvenile Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which maintained the exceptions of lack of subject matter jurisdiction and prescription filed by plaintiff Department of Social Services. The exceptions were raised in response to a Petition To Disavow Paternity.


OVERVIEW: The Department sued the father seeking child support pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 46:236.1(F), for three minor children born during his marriage to the mother. The father was ordered to pay child support and he asked for a hearing before the juvenile court. After filing an answer denying paternity of two of the children, the father then filed a petition to disavow paternity. The Department filed an exception of prescription under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 189, and an exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The juvenile court granted the exceptions. The court affirmed the grant of the exception of jurisdiction holding that because there were no special statutory provisions granting the juvenile court authority to adjudicate an action to disavow as part of its duties to set and enforce child support, the juvenile court was not clearly wrong in granting the exception. The court held that once the juvenile court determined it had no authority to render a judgment for lack of jurisdiction, pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. arts. 2 and 3, it also lacked authority to determine issues related to that subject; thus, it vacated the judgment on the exception of prescription.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the juvenile court maintaining the exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction was affirmed. The judgment of the juvenile court maintaining the peremptory exception of prescription was vacated. The matter was remanded to the juvenile court for further proceedings.

State v. Ruiz


No. 92-KA-2092


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


630 So. 2d 897; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3965



December 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 22, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 347-310, SECTION "E". HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED, REMANDED FOR SENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of vehicular homicide, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1, and sentenced him to 15 years as a multiple offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving a pick-up truck that ran into the back of a semi-truck stopped on the shoulder of a highway. As a result of the accident, the passenger in defendant's truck was killed. Defendant's blood alcohol was tested at .27 percent, and the trial court convicted defendant of vehicular homicide in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1. On review, defendant alleged, among other things, that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the chemical analysis of his blood sample. The court concluded that the procedures were sufficient to insure the integrity and reliability of the chemical test and that the State properly complied with those procedures in this case. However, with respect to sentencing, the court found that the trial court followed the old sentencing guidelines, despite the fact that the new guidelines took effect on January 31, 1992 and the defendant's sentencing took place after that date. According to the court, the failure of the trial court to indicate consideration of the new guidelines mandated that defendant's sentence be vacated and the matter remanded for resentencing in compliance with the sentencing guidelines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for vehicular homicide but vacated and remanded defendant's sentence for resentencing in compliance with the sentencing guidelines.

State v. Payne


No. 93 KA 0495


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


633 So. 2d 701; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3942



December 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, NO. 5-92-1293, EAST BATON ROUGE PARISH, LOUISIANA, HONORABLE J. MICHAEL MCDONALD, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED. SENTENCES AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana) of five counts of indecent behavior with juveniles, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81, and the sentences imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded nolo contendere to five counts of indecent behavior with juveniles. He was sentenced to five concurrent sentences of seven years at hard labor, with credit for time served. Five years of each sentence was suspended, and defendant was placed on active, supervised probation for four years with special conditions of probation. In affirming the decision, the court held that the sentence imposed was not excessive. Although five concurrent sentences of seven years at hard labor were imposed, five years of each sentence were suspended. As a result, defendant received, in effect, five concurrent sentences of two years at hard labor. The period of probation was not illegal, because the two-year period of imprisonment was not imposed as a condition of probation and was not added to the four-year term of probation. However, requiring defendant to register as a sex offender pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:540-549 was an unconstitutional violation of the ex post facto provisions in U.S. Const. art. 1, § 9 and La. Const. art. I, § 23. Finally, the sentences imposed were not excessive. Considering the reasons for sentencing, the record amply supported the sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, and affirmed his sentences as amended to delete the special condition of probation and/or the order for defendant to register as a sex offender.

Tex/Con Oil & Gas Co. v. Batchelor


No. CA 92 2113


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


634 So. 2d 902; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 4030



December 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 370,965, DIVISION "F"), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE FRANK J. SAIA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant conservation commissioner appealed from a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial district Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which favored plaintiff oil companies in their application to determine the costs for three wells. The lease owners filed the action in the district court to review the commissioner's order that the dollar-for-dollar method of depreciation applied to the well costs.


OVERVIEW: The conservation commissioner revised the ownership interests in three wells in which the oil company owned a lease interest based on new geological information, and the oil company filed an application with the commissioner for a determination of the reasonable cost of each of the wells. The commissioner used the dollar-for-dollar method of depreciation and determined that because the production from the wells had exceeded costs, the owners of the original units were not entitled to charge costs to the subsequent owners of the revised units. The oil company brought an action in the district court in which it claimed that the unit of production depreciated well cost method was proper. The trial court agreed, and the commissioner appealed. On review, the court held that the plain language of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 30:10A(2)(d) mandated the dollar-for-dollar method of depreciation. The trial court erred as a matter of law in interpreting the statute, and the trial court's conclusion that the depreciated well cost analysis should have been used was an erroneous substitution of the trial court's judgment for that of the commissioner's.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and reinstated the orders of the conservation commissioner that found that the dollar-for-dollar method of depreciation applied to the wells. The court assessed the costs of the appeal against the oil company.

Lakeside Imports v. State


CA 92 2149


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


634 So. 2d 891; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 4032



December 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, NO. 380,247, HONORABLE MICHAEL PONDER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car dealership appealed from the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:193 was constitutional and denied the dealership's requests for a permanent injunction, a declaratory judgment, and attorney's fees in its suit against defendant State to allow it to open on Sundays. Intervenor automobile association joined the State.


OVERVIEW: The dealership sold auto parts and did repair work in addition to selling new and used cars and trucks. It claimed that § 51:193 caused it to lose business to other parts stores and repair shops because it prohibited licensed motor vehicle dealers from opening on Sunday. The court found that § 51:193 was not per se unconstitutional, and that it did not create arbitrary and unreasonable business classifications that had no bearing on the public health and welfare considerations that prompted enactment of Sunday Closing Laws. The classification was rationally related to a legitimate state interest. If Sunday dealership openings were determined by local legislation under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:191, large city dealers would benefit over small rural dealerships who would have to remain open on Sundays to remain competitive and who would likely go out of business. Also, most consumers preferred that dealerships be closed on Sunday to give them an opportunity to examine the vehicles by themselves, so La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:193 encouraged consumers to make informed decisions. It also gave sales personnel a forced day of rest, which safeguarded their health and general welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court finding that the law prohibiting Sunday openings by car dealerships was constitutional and denying the dealership's request for a permanent injunction, a declaratory judgment, and attorney's fees.

State v. Gamberella


Nos. 93 KA 0829, 93 KA 0830


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


633 So. 2d 595; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 4050



December 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF TERREBONNE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NUMBERS 228,133 AND 231,706, HONORABLE BARON B. BOURG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant appealed the judgment of the 32nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), that convicted him of intentionally exposing another to the AIDS virus under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.5, arguing that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and was unconstitutional because it violated his privacy rights.


OVERVIEW: After learning that he was HIV-positive, the defendant began engaging in sexual intercourse with his victim. After their relationship ended, the victim learned that she had become infected by the defendant, who was charged with and convicted of the intentional exposure of the AIDS virus in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.5. The defendant appealed. In affirming, the court rejected the defendant's constitutionality challenge for vagueness. The conduct proscribed was unambiguous in prohibiting the intentional exposure to another to the AIDS virus through sexual contact without the victim's knowledge and consent. The statute offered a clear and definite standard of conduct, and the words were readily understandable by an ordinary person of reasonable intelligence. The court likewise rejected the defendant's argument that the statute violated his right to privacy by interfering with the right of an HIV-infected person to engage in sexual activities. The right of privacy was not absolute, and the state had a compelling interest in discouraging the spread of the HIV virus.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

State v. Cortina


No. 93 KA 0363


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


632 So. 2d 335; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 4034



December 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 21, 1994. Released for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, NUMBER 4-90-14, EAST BATON ROUGE PARISH, LOUISIANA, HONORABLE A. FOSTER SANDERS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED, CONDITIONS OF PROBATION VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THE DISTRICT COURT FOR PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to two counts of forgery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:72 in the Nineteenth Judicial District court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), and sought review of his sentence. Defendant, who was an attorney, was granted co-counsel status and filed a pro se brief that alleged numerous assignments of error.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an attorney, pleaded guilty to two counts of forgery in connection with signing a client's name to a settlement check and utilizing those proceeds for personal use. The trial court sentenced defendant to five years supervised probation with numerous special conditions, which included two years in the parish prison. The court affirmed the conviction, vacated the conditions of probation, and remanded the case. The court held that defendant could not argue the issue of the constitutionality of the prosecution by the attorney general's office because he waived any nonjurisdictional defects by withdrawing his not guilty plea and entering a plea of guilty without reserving his right to appellate review of the pre-plea rulings on his motions. The court held that the trial court set conditions of probation that were legally incorrect and the trial court erred in failing to set a specific amount of restitution to be paid. The court further held that defendant had abandoned other assignments of error since he failed to brief them. Other claims were not formally assigned as error and were not reviewed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's forgery conviction, vacated the conditions of probation as not legally correct, and remanded the case.

State v. Williams


No. 93 KA 0353


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


632 So. 2d 351; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 4035



December 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 21, 1994. Released for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NUMBER 8-91-1038, HONORABLE FOSTER SANDERS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which convicted him of aggravated rape and aggravated burglary, arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support a conviction and that the district court erred in failing to instruct the jury regarding all responsive verdicts related to the aggravated rape charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions of aggravated rape and aggravated burglary stemming from a brutal attack upon his estranged wife. In affirming, the court rejected defendant's contention that the evidence was insufficient to support the jury's verdict. Although there was no medical or physical evidence to establish the requisite element of penetration for aggravated rape, the testimony of the victim was competent to establish that element. Further, although the house into which defendant entered had served as the family home, defendant no longer lived there, the burgled property was the separate property of the victim, and the victim had made it known to defendant that she did not want him to come into her home. The court likewise rejected defendant's argument that the district court erred in failing to instruct the jury on all possible responsive verdicts. The district court correctly excluded guilty of sexual battery, guilty of simple rape, and guilty of attempted simple rape from the list of responsive verdicts applicable to defendant's aggravated rape charge because each was inapplicable where the victim was the offender's spouse.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

Trombatore v. Saia Motor Freight Line


No. 93-CA-479


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


627 So. 2d 1387; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3995



December 15, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 91-06801. HONORABLE MARK ZIMMERMAN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a decision from the Office of Worker's Compensation Administration (OWCA) (Louisiana) that granted defendant employer's exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction and dismissed the employee's claim for retaliatory discharge. The employer filed a motion to dismiss the appeal on the basis that it was not timely filed.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a dockworker, was injured unloading a trailer and received weekly compensation benefits and medical expenses pursuant to the Louisiana Worker's Compensation Act. After the employee was released to return to work by his treating physician, he was terminated by the employer. Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1361, the employee filed a claim with OWCA for alleged discriminatory or retaliatory discharge. The employer filed an exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction asserting that OWCA was not the proper forum for litigating a wrongful discharge claim. The trial court granted the exception and dismissed the employee's claim. On appeal, the court affirmed OWCA's decision. As a preliminary matter, the court denied the employer's motion to dismiss the appeal because the record indicated that the appeal was timely filed. The court determined that jurisdiction over discriminatory discharge cases vested in civil district court and not OWCA. The court ruled that the retaliatory discharge claim was not a worker's compensation matter but was a delictual employment law matter.


OUTCOME: The court denied the employer's motion to dismiss the appeal. The court affirmed the decision of the OWCA that granted the employer's exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

Simpson v. State ex rel. Department of Transp. & Dev.


Nos. 92 CA 0115, 92 CA 0116, 92 CA 0117


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


636 So. 2d 608; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 4096



December 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated January 20, 1994. Rehearing Granted in Part, Denied in Part March 21, 1994, Reported at: 1994 La. App. LEXIS 674. Released for Publication March 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NOS. 83098, 84062 AND 84276), PARISH OF TANGIPAHOA, HONORABLE BRUCE C. BENNETT, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART, AMENDED IN PART, AND AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The twenty-first Judicial District Court (Louisiana) entered a judgment against the appellant Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development in a personal injury action that was filed by the appellees, driver and passengers, after they were injured when the truck they were riding in hit a bridge that was under the garde of the department. The department appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The driver of a pickup truck encountered a sudden downpour. The truck fishtailed when the driver applied the brakes, and slid into the exposed railing of a bridge. The department contended that the sole cause-in-fact of the accident was the driver's inability to maintain control of the vehicle and that the sole legal cause was the driver's negligence in failing to maintain control. The department also argued that the condition of the bridge, however defective, was not the cause of the driver's losing control of his vehicle. The court held that the department's duty to maintain reasonably safe highways and shoulders was not to be defined in terms of the driver's conduct because, under comparative fault principles, there could be more than one cause in fact, which would make both wrongdoers liable. The court stated that the negligence of the driver merely reduced, but did not bar, his own damages, and his negligence made him solidarily liable with the department for his passengers' injuries. The court found that the trial court's conclusion that the driver was not at fault was manifestly erroneous. The court allocated fault between the driver and the department at 50 percent each.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed in part, amended in part, and affirmed as amended.

Johnson v. Department of Pub. Safety


No. 25,225-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


627 So. 2d 732; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3669



December 1, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 13, 1994. Released for Publication January 13, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 38,521. Honorable E. J. Bleich, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents appealed an order from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln (Louisiana), dismissing the parents' negligence suit against defendant department of transportation.


OVERVIEW: The parents' son was killed in an automobile accident. The driver collided with the son's vehicle while he was having an epileptic seizure. The parents alleged that the department of transportation was negligent in automatically renewing the driver's operating privileges. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the trial court's finding that the department of transportation did not have notice of the driver's epileptic seizure was supported by the evidence. There were discrepancies in the driver's testimony regarding whether he disclosed his medical condition to the department of transportation and it was for the trier of fact to resolve the issue of credibility. The court further held that imposing a duty on the department of transportation under the facts of the case would expand the department of transportation's liability beyond the legislature's intent. Next, the court determined that the department of transportation was immune from liability because any liability imposed would be for negligent policymaking and the rules and procedures for the issuance and renewal of drivers' license was a discretionary act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Weaver v. Plaquemines Parish Sch. Bd.


No. 93-CA-0640


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


627 So. 2d 724; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3625



November 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 13, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 25th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PLAQUEMINES PARISH. NO. 36-285, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE MICHAEL E. KIRBY, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school board sought review of a decision of the 25th Judicial District Court, Plaquemines Parish (Louisiana), which granted plaintiff teachers' writs of mandamus and ordered the school board to pay the teachers the difference between their regular pay and a substitute's pay.


OVERVIEW: A group of teachers were all away from work while on sick leave. Each of the teacher's leaves lasted longer than the 10 days granted under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:1201(A)(1). The school board refused to pay the teachers' salaries for any time spent on sick leave over 10 days. The teachers filed mandamus actions, which were consolidated, seeking to receive the difference between the teachers' regular pay and the amount paid to any substitute teacher, if one was employed; otherwise, the full salary was sought. The trial court granted the teachers' writs. The court affirmed, holding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:1202 prohibited a school board from deducting from a teacher's pay more than the amount paid to a substitute teacher. It was immaterial whether the teacher sought or was denied additional sick leave; the only issue was whether the teacher was absent for medical reasons.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the teachers' mandamus writs in the action seeking salary payments for sick leaves over 10 days in duration.

 

862 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Everett


No. 93-KA-0253


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


628 So. 2d 148; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3635



November 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 13, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 358-494, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting him of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64 and sentencing him under La. Rev. Stat. ann. § 15:529 as a second offender.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted and sentenced defendant under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 as a second offender and defendant appealed, contending that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash the multiple bill brought against him and in finding that he was a multiple offender. On appeal the court held that the multiple offender statute did not violate the constitutional provisions regarding separation of powers, due process, and equal protection. The legislature established a procedure which enabled the district attorney to seek and the courts to exact more severe sentences on defendants who repeatedly violated the criminal laws. The legislature did not delegate any of its duties nor did it usurp the judiciary's discretion in sentencing a defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing defendant.

 

863 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gaynard


No. 93-KA-0657


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


629 So. 2d 1240; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3904



November 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted, Reported at: 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3906. Released for Publication January 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 348-247, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which sentenced him as a multiple offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 after defendant pled guilty to distribution of marijuana. Defendant claimed, inter alia, that § 15:529.1 violated the constitutional provisions regarding separation of powers under La. Const. art. 2, § 2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to distribution of marijuana. The trial court sentenced defendant under the multiple offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. Defendant claimed, inter alia, that § 15:529.1 violated the constitutional provisions regarding separation of powers under La. Const. art. 2, § 2. The court held that art. 2, § 2 divided the state's government into three separate branches and that this division created in the judicial branch powers with which the legislative and executive branches could not interfere. The court ruled that the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 did not violate Louisiana's constitutional separation of powers. The court held that by imposing certain habitual offender statuses and corresponding penalties the legislature merely established a procedure that enabled a district attorney to seek and the courts to exact more severe sentences on defendants who repeatedly violated the criminal laws and that it did not usurp the judiciary's discretion in sentencing a defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence as a multiple offender.

Vonderhaar v. Parish of St. Tammany


No. 92 CA 1572


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


633 So. 2d 217; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3762



November 24, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM A JUDGMENT OF THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY, SUITE NUMBER 92 10902-1, HONORABLE A. CLAYTON JAMES, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, bar owner and exotic dancers, sought review of a judgment from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), whichdissolved the temporary restraining order, denied the motion for preliminary injunction, denied appellee parish's objection of res judicata, and maintained the parish's objection of no cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The bar owners and exotic dancers sought to enjoin the enforcement of a local ordinance adopted by the parish police that required dancers to be more fully clothed when entertaining than was required by statute. They contended that the ordinance infringed on their right to freedom of expression guaranteed by La. Const. art. I, § 7. The bar owner and exotic dancers filed a petition for a temporary restraining order in state court and it was granted. The parish filed a peremptory exception raising the objections of res judicata and no cause of action. The trial court dissolved the temporary restraining order, denied the motion for preliminary injunction, denied the parish's objection of res judicata, and maintained the parish's objection of no cause of action. The court held that the denial of the preliminary injunction was not an abuse of discretion. The court reversed the maintaining of the exception of no cause of action in the action for a declaratory judgment, and remanded the case. The court held that the amended ordinances were valid exercises of the broad discretion of the parish to regulate the sale of alcoholic beverages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the suit for a preliminary injunction. The court reversed the maintaining of the exception of no cause of action in the suit for a declaratory judgment in favor of the parish, and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Matthews


No. 93 KA 0275


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


632 So. 2d 294; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3766



November 24, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 21, 1994. Released for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NO. 238950), PARISH OF LAFOURCHE, HONORABLE SIDNEY A. ORDOYNE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Seventeenth Judicial District Court, Parish of LaFourche (Louisiana), which convicted him, by jury trial, of three counts of distribution of cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967.


OVERVIEW: On three dates, defendant sold rock cocaine to undercover police officers. Defendant was charged by grand jury indictment with three counts of distribution of cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967. Defendant pleaded not guilty and, after a jury trial, was found guilty as charged. Defendant was sentenced to a term of imprisonment of 240 months (20 years) on each count, to be served concurrently, with credit for time served. On appeal, defendant filed 23 assignments of error. The court held that defendant's assignments of error were all meritless because they were raised for the first time on appeal. The court noted that there was no requirement for a trial court to instruct the jury about the presumption of innocence during preliminary instructions. The court further noted that during the entire examination of the informant and the officer, defendant did not make any objection and therefore could not now challenge his testimony. The court determined that the state properly established that the cocaine introduced into evidence was the same cocaine purchased from defendant and satisfactorily explained why some of it was in powder form.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of defendant on 3 counts of distribution of cocaine and the sentence of 20 years on each count.

 

866 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Hung Chi Ly v. State ex rel. Department of Pub. Safety & Corrections


No. CA 92 1054R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


633 So. 2d 197; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3799



November 24, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 362,445, DIVISION "A"), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE BOB D. DOWNING, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant survivors sought review of a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Division A, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which awarded them damages against appellee State Police arising out of a vehicular collision that resulted in the deaths of the survivors' parents.


OVERVIEW: The parents of the survivors were killed in a vehicular collision on a highway. Their car, which was off to the side of the road, was hit by a State Police trooper's car, which was being driven in excess of the legal speed limit. The trial court concluded that both the decedents and the State Trooper were negligent and apportioned fault at two-thirds to the decedents and one-third to the Trooper. The trial court also awarded damages totaling more than $ 3.3 million to the survivors for which the State was held liable for one-third. Both parties appealed the judgment as to the apportionment of fault. The court held that the conclusions that the state trooper was partially at fault in causing the accident, that the decedents' conduct also contributed to the accident, and as to the apportionment of fault, were not manifestly erroneous. The court noted that while the decedents' stalled vehicle was not readily apparent at the time of the accident, it was discernible to a prudent motorist. The court noted that the decedents had ample time to realize that they would not be able to restart their vehicle and should have taken other measures to protect themselves from oncoming traffic.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

867 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Payne v. New Orleans Gen. Hosp.


No. 93-CA-0348 c/w NO 93-CA-0349


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


627 So. 2d 221; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3486



November 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NOS. 85-905 c/w 87-2789, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE GERALD P. FEDOROFF, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff medical malpractice claimants challenged the summary judgment dismissal of their suit by the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans, Division E (Louisiana), against defendants, physicians and excess liability insurers. Plaintiffs argued that the liability cap for damages under the Medical Malpractice Act, specifically La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.45A, was unconstitutional, and the limitation was not available to an insurer.


OVERVIEW: As to plaintiffs' assertion that the $ 100,000 liability cap for damages for a qualified health care provider was unconstitutional, the court pointed out that the state supreme court had recently considered the issue in an opinion in which it was stated that overall the Louisiana Medical Malpractice Act represented a reasonable but imperfect balance between the rights of victims and those of health care providers, and did not violate the state or federal constitutions. As to the argument that the limitation was a "personal defense" not available to the liability insurer, it had not been directly addressed by the state courts, but the court noted that in another opinion the supreme court, when considering another malpractice issue, stated that the limitation of the Louisiana Medical Malpractice Act, specifically La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.45A, applied to the insurer as well as the health care provider. Despite plaintiffs' counsel's urgings, the court refused to presume that the supreme court inferentially overruled the opinion when that court did not expressly do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the medical malpractice suit.

 

868 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bibb


No. 92-KA-998


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


626 So. 2d 913; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3500



November 10, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, NO. 91-2875, DIVISION "D", HONORABLE WALTER E. KOLLIN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: SENTENCES AND CONVICTIONS CONDITIONALLY AFFIRMED; REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT FOR EVIDENTIARY HEARING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which on remand by the court denied defendant's second motion for a new trial. Defendant alleged numerous errors, including that he was denied the right to a fair and impartial jury, that he was denied the right to a new trial, and that it was error to determine that defendant was competent to stand trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first degree murder of his children and attempted first degree murder of his wife. After his conviction for first degree murder, defendant was twice denied motions for a new trial. The second motion alleging juror misconduct was denied on remand by the court, on the grounds that it was untimely and not based on new evidence, and defendant appealed. The court conditionally affirmed defendant's convictions. The court held that because it was unclear as to whether illicit contact between a juror and the deputy sheriff occurred after the verdict but before sentencing, which was not prejudicial, or before the verdict, which could be prejudicial, an evidentiary hearing was needed to decide defendant's motion. The court therefore remanded the case. Notwithstanding its remand, the court addressed the denial of the motion and held that under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 851, defendant did not show grounds for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence, because the new information about jury misconduct was not admissible. The court held that defendant was competent to stand trial, because his mental capacity to proceed was supported by expert testimony.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally affirmed defendant's convictions. The court remanded for an evidentiary hearing to determine whether illicit contact between a juror and the deputy sheriff occurred before or after the verdict, because contact before the verdict that was found to be prejudicial was grounds for a new trial. Defendant was properly found competent to stand trial, because his mental capacity to proceed was supported by the evidence.

Cowart v. Lee


NUMBER 93-270


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


626 So. 2d 93; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3414



November 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 10, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Concordia, State of Louisiana; Honorable Leo Boothe, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from a judgment of the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Concordia, (Louisiana), which granted the exception of no cause of action filed by defendant school board, and dismissed his suit against the board. The employee's suit sought injunctive relief and money damages for his alleged unlawful termination from his non-tenured position as business manager.


OVERVIEW: The employee's petition alleged that the Superintendent of the board, in return for appointment to his position, promised the board that he would dismiss the employee and others, solely for reasons of political patronage. The petition also alleged that the dismissal without notice or a hearing, coupled with the board's failure to adopt rules for dismissal of non-tenured employees pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:81.5 violated his statutory and due process rights. On appeal, the court reversed the dismissal, and held that the petition stated a cause of action. The court ruled that the employee was not terminable at will, because § 17:81.5 specifically regulated that employment relationship. The court held that the board's authority was subject to legislative limitation under La. Const. art. VIII, and that § 17.81.5 purposefully removed such employees from "at will" status, entitling them to due process. The court held that without having enacted the required rules, the board exceeded its authority by terminating the employee in the absence of some demonstrable compelling need.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court judgment, which had granted the exception of no cause of action filed by the school board, and dismissed the employee's suit seeking injunctive relief and money damages for his alleged unlawful termination from his non-tenured position as business manager.

Hopkins v. Sovereign Fire & Casualty Ins. Co.


Nos. 93-246, 93-247, 93-248


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


626 So. 2d 880; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3421



November 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 10, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Eleventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Sabine, State of Louisiana; Honorable Robert E. Burgess, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents appealed an order from the Eleventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Sabine, State of Louisiana, finding that defendants, police officer, alcohol provider and driver, were not liable for the death of the parents' minor child.


OVERVIEW: The parents filed suit seeking to hold the driver, police officer and the alcohol provider liable for injuries sustained by the parents' minor child. The police officer, driver and alcohol provider filed motions for summary judgment, which were granted. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in the part the motions. As to the police officer, the court held that generally the duty owed by a police officer was to the public and not individuals. Thus, no liability occurred individually to any one person. The court concluded that even if the officer owed a duty to children, there was no breach because the officer had no reason to believe that the driver was intoxicated and to arrest her. Second, the court held that the driver was not entitled to summary judgment because there were genuine issues of material fact as to whether the driver was actually the driver. Credibility issues were not appropriate for summary judgment. Third, the court held that the alcohol provider could not escape liability for acts of the immediate purchaser of those items and where the quantity purchased by the minor indicated that more than one person would probably consume the items.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in part and reversed the judgment in part.

Cosse' v. Orleans Material & Equip.


No. 93-CA-0266


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


626 So. 2d 440; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3294



October 28, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 9, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION. NO. 91-10335, DISTRICT EIGHT. HONORABLE EDGAR COREY, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed the judgment of the Office of Workers' Compensation, District Eight (Louisiana), which held that he was not entitled to workmen's compensation after he suffered from a heart attack, because his illness began at home in bed, before he started work, and therefore was not work-related.


OVERVIEW: The employee suffered a heart attack and sought workmen's benefits. The Office of Workers' Compensation denied him benefits and he appealed the ruling. The court held that under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1021(7)(e), the employee was not entitled to benefits unless he demonstrated by clear and convincing evidence that his physical work was the predominant and major cause of the heart-related illness. The court stated that there was sufficient evidence to support the hearing officer's finding that the employee did not demonstrate by clear and convincing evidence that his work stress was extraordinary and unusual in comparison to that of the average layout and fitter. The court also determined that the employee did not prove by clear and convincing evidence that his work stress or exertion was the predominant and major cause of his heart attack. The court concluded that the employer should not pay benefits for health complications that began in the employee's bed. The court affirmed the hearing officer's decision, and denied the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the Office of Workers' Compensation.

Rogers v. Synthes, Ltd.

The court did not consider the patient's constitutional challenge, because it had not been raised in the district court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court judgment, which granted a dilatory exception of prematurity filed by the hospital and the manufacturer, because the patient's action had not first been presented to a medical malpractice panel under the Louisiana Medical Malpractice Act.

State v. W.A.S.


CA 92 1899


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


629 So. 2d 1209; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3204



October 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 6, 1993. Released for Publication December 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 62750), PARISH OF LIVINGSTON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE KENNETH J. FOGG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant putative father sought review of the judgment of the 21st Judicial District Court, Parish of Livingston (Louisiana), which decreed that he was the natural father of a minor child and ordered him to pay child support in a paternity action commenced by plaintiff State.


OVERVIEW: The putative father was ordered to undergo blood testing in the State's paternity suit. On appeal from the trial court's judgment decreeing parentage, the father argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:396 authorizing mandatory testing was unconstitutional. In affirming, the court ruled that an order for blood testing to determine paternity was a search and seizure within the meaning of the U.S. Const. amend. IV and that the issue was whether a court-ordered blood test was reasonable and justified under the circumstances. The court noted that a blood test was minimally intrusive, relatively painless, and medically safe and that, in facilitating a determination of paternity, blood tests were highly reliable and unequaled in evidentiary value. The court found that the father had voluntarily submitted to the test as ordered and waived the issue by failing to request a protective order or a hearing, but ruled that any failure of the trial court to conduct a preliminary hearing was harmless error in light of the mother's trial testimony regarding exclusive sexual contact with the father during the time of conception.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Duke


CR93-123


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


625 So. 2d 325; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2950



October 6, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 26, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-EIGHTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LASALLE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, THE HON. JIMMIE C. PETERS, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction of aggravated oral sexual battery, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43, and his sentence of 10 years at hard labor from the Twenty-Eighth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lasalle (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: The eight-year-old victim testified that defendant, his stepfather, had placed his penis in the victim's mouth on multiple occasions over the past three years. Another child testified that she believed that defendant had tricked her by placing his penis in her mouth by telling her it was candy. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court held that: (1) the inadvertent listing of the crime on the verdict sheet as indecent behavior with a juvenile was not reversible error given the number of times the trial court discussed the actual charge; (2) the second child's testimony was admissible to establish intent, knowledge, and system; (3) the victim's testimony of crimes other than the single charged incident, was admissible to establish intent; (4) the use of leading questions in the victim's videotaped statement did not render it inadmissible; and, (5) the sentence, which was twice the maximum sentence indicated by the sentencing guidelines, but well within the statutory maximum was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated oral sexual battery with instructions to inform defendant of the provisions regarding the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief.

 

876 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


In re Delaune


No. 92-CA-2569


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


625 So. 2d 269; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2903



September 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM 34th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, ST. BERNARD PARISH. NO. 63-572, DIVISION "C" (c/w No. 91-07695, Office of Workers' Compensation). HONORABLE MELVYN J. PEREZ, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed the judgment from the 34th Judicial District Court, St. Bernard Parish (Louisiana), which found that 1988 La. Acts 938, § 3 did not deprive the trial court of jurisdiction to approve the workers' compensation settlement between the employee and defendants, the employer and its insurer, and which dismissed his suit to annul the judgment approving the settlement.


OVERVIEW: An employee was injured in the course of his employment and received workers' compensation (WC) benefits. The employee and his employer and its insurer reached a settlement of the employee's claim. The trial court approved the settlement on the same day that the parties filed a joint petition to compromise the claim. After the employee received his payment, he filed suit to annul the judgment approving the settlement, and the trial court dismissed his suit. On appeal, the court reversed and granted the employee's petition. 1988 La. Acts 938, § 3, which divested the trial court of jurisdiction to approve WC compromise settlement claims, became effective before the parties filed their joint petition. Although the amendment to La. Const. art. V, § 16 became effective after the settlement was approved, the amendment was retroactive to the effective date of 1988 La. Acts 938, § 3 because Act 938 was procedural rather than substantive. Thus, under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. arts. 3 and 2002, the judgment approving the settlement was void and had to be annulled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that found that the trial court had jurisdiction to approve the workers' compensation settlement between an employee and an employer and its insurer, and that dismissed the employee's suit to annul the judgment approving the settlement. The court granted the employee's petition to annul the judgment.

State v. Ross


No. 92-KA-2344


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


625 So. 2d 284; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2880



September 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 354-286, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which found him to be a third offender and sentenced him to 10 years at hard labor with credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced defendant and defendant appealed, contending that the sentence imposed under the multiple offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, was illegal because it was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine or the due process and equal protection guarantees. The court refused to review the trial court's error in failing to state that the sentence was to be served without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence as required by § 15:529.1(G) because the trial court did not suspend any portion of the sentence or grant defendant probation. Moreover, the court held that it would not correct errors favorable to defendant when the State did not raise the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and sentence.

Buckbee v. United Gas Pipeline Co.


NUMBER 87-1201


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


626 So. 2d 1191; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2908



September 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 23, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of June 2, 1993, Reported at: 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2089.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant gas company sought an application for rehearing from a judgment of the trial court (Louisiana) requesting the court to address how interest should be computed upon the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought a rehearing from the trial court's judgment and the court granted the rehearing for the limited purpose of addressing the interest issue. The court held that the fluctuating interest rate was applicable. The plaintiffs filed their lawsuit after the effective date for the applicability of fluctuating interest rates under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2924(B)(2). La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4203 provided that legal interest attached from the date of judicial demand. The court concluded that the interest on the judgment was subject to fluctuating rates of judicial interest for all periods the plaintiffs' suit was pending from the date of judicial demand until paid.


OUTCOME: The court granted the rehearing on the subject of the interest rate and held that the fluctuating interest rate was applicable.

 

880 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. JUAREZ


No. 25,168-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


624 So. 2d 26; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2864



September 22, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 21, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 55,601. Honorable Cecil P. Campbell, II, Judge



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, defendant's conviction and sentence are AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the 26th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana, claiming that the sentence of five years at hard labor without probation or suspension of sentence imposed after he pleaded guilty to possession of marijuana with the intent to distribute in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 966(A)(1) was unconstitutionally excessive. Defendant's earlier motion to reconsider the sentence was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his brother were charged by bill of information with possession of marijuana with the intent to distribute, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A)(1). Defendant pleaded guilty to the charge but then appealed, claiming that the sentence imposed was unconstitutionally excessive. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, holding that the latter did not violate La. Const. of 1974 art. I, § 20. The sentencing guidelines suggested a four and one-half year sentence. However, defendant was a second felony offender. Hence, his sentence was required to be imposed without the benefit of probation or suspension, and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(B)(2) mandated a minimum sentence of five years at hard labor. The minimum sentence was compelled by law and therefore was presumed not to be excessive. On examination of the record, the court found no errors patent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Board of Comm'rs v. Missouri Pac. R.R.


No. 93-CA-0755


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


625 So. 2d 1070; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2831



September 22, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Limited Rehearing Granted November 18, 1993, Reported at: 1993 La. App. LEXIS 3501.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 92-04155, DIVISION J. HONORABLE GEORGE C. CONNOLLY, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a state authority, appealed the award of compensation granted by the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), in its judgment of expropriation. Defendant buyer challenged the judgment of expropriation, and in the alternative, sought an increase in its compensation award.


OVERVIEW: The authority sought to obtain land adjacent to its convention center in order to expand. After negotiations for the purchase of land from the prior owners failed, the authority instituted expropriation proceedings. The prior owners then sold the property as part of a larger tract to defendant buyer for 11 million dollars and added the buyer to the suit. The trial judge found that the authority met all statutory prerequisites to its expropriation suit and that it had met its burden of proving that the property was for a public necessity. A jury awarded 13 million dollars to the buyer. On appeal, the court held that the evidence established the right to expropriation based on public need. The evidence established a public need for the expansion of the convention center and that such an expansion would promote economic growth. The court rejected the authority's assertion that the buyer, as the new owner, could not be compensated for more than he paid for the property, where he knew the property was gong to be subject to expropriation. The court also held that the trial judge did not err in instructing the jury to determine the value of the property as of the date of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for a determination of attorney fees.
