State v. Claiborne


No. 93-KA-0082


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


624 So. 2d 17; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2775



August 31, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 352-538, SECTION "C". HONORABLE JEROME M. WINSBERG, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "C" (Louisiana), which was entered upon a jury verdict finding him guilty of manslaughter, and his sentence as a second felony offender to 35 years at hard labor to be served consecutively with any other sentence he was serving.


OVERVIEW: Three assailants approached the victim and her husband and attempted to rob them. The victim was shot and died later that night. Information implicating defendant and two others was obtained from an anonymous call to a tip line. The three were indicted for first-degree murder. The charge against defendant was subsequently amended to second-degree murder. A jury found him guilty of manslaughter. He was sentenced as a second felony offender to 35 years at hard labor to be served consecutively with any other sentence he was serving. On appeal, the court affirmed. Defendant's enhanced sentence was within the statutory limits and less than the maximum sentence allowable. The trial judge's stipulation that the sentence was to be served consecutively with other sentences was within his discretion. The circumstances of the crime and defendant's extensive criminal history put him in the most egregious class of offenders. There were no mitigating circumstances. A more severe sentence than that recommended by the sentencing guidelines was warranted. The record supported the trial court's deviation from the sentencing guidelines and the sentence imposed was not unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for manslaughter.

State v. Berniard


No. 92-KA-2020


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


625 So. 2d 217; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2692



August 11, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted Court En Banc September 30, 1993, Reported at: 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2904.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 304-240, SECTION "G". HONORABLE FRANK J. SHEA, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans, State of Louisiana, No. 304-240, Section "G," which convicted him of second degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1 and sentenced him to life imprisonment without parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Police officers saw defendant, dressed in female attire and wearing a wig, shooting a gun toward a house. Defendant admitted that he shot the victim who was found dead on the porch of the house and was to have been a state witness in the trial against defendant's mother. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment without parole, probation, or suspension for second degree murder under § 14:30.1. The court granted defendant a new trial. The court held that the instruction on the definition of reasonable doubt was erroneous because it contained a misdescription of the burden of proof that vitiated all of the jury's findings. The court determined that the deprivation of defendant's right to a jury trial under the Sixth Amendment was a structural defect worthy of departing from the policy against the plain error doctrine and overruling State v. Dobson, 578 So. 2d 533 (La. App. 4th Cir. 1991), which held that the instruction was not reviewable on appeal in the absence of a contemporaneous objection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and sentence and remanded the matter for a new trial.

Warren v. Warren


No. 93-C-0261


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


622 So. 2d 864; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2674



August 4, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 15, 1993.As Corrected August 6, 1993. As Corrected August 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: IN RE: LUCIUS WARREN AND JEANNE McNAIR DIRECTED TO: HONORABLE ROBERT A. KATZ, JUDGE. CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. DIVISION "B", NO. 88-10228 and 92-12903



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; MOTION GRANTED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband appealed a judgment from the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans Division "B" (Louisiana), which had denied his motion to employ the Louisiana Long Arm Statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3201 in a divorce proceeding to obtain jurisdiction over his non-resident spouse.


OVERVIEW: The husband had filed a motion to replace a curator, who was appointed to represent his non-resident spouse, and to employ the Long Arm Statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3201, to serve his wife. The trial court denied the motion. The court granted the writ application to obtain jurisdiction over a nonresident spouse in a divorce proceeding. The use of the state's Long Arm Statute was justified where there were minimum contacts within the state to make it reasonable and just according to traditional concepts of fair play and substantial justice. The court held that if the absent spouse was served pursuant to § 13:3201and claimed that the court did not have jurisdiction, that spouse had the right to challenge jurisdiction by an exception. Whether a defendant/spouse came under § 13:3201, and had minimal contacts with the state, was decided on a case by case basis. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3204 authorized service by registered or certified mail or actual delivery by a person authorized to serve process under the law of the place where service was to be made on a defendant over whom personal jurisdiction was obtained pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §13:3201.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ application permitting the husband to gain jurisdiction over his non-resident wife.

State v. Hardy


No. 92-KA-1761


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


622 So. 2d 858; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2672



August 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 353-536, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section F (Louisiana), which convicted him of possession of a firearm in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1 and which sentenced him to serve six years at hard labor in the department of corrections without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Police officers observed defendant in an area of a reported armed robbery. Upon conducting a pat down search, the officers retrieved a pistol with two live rounds from defendant's waistband. During the trial, a defense witness testified that when the officers stopped defendant he had just taken the gun from a male who jumped out of a car and pulled the gun on defendant. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred by ruling that statements made by defendant to the officers following his arrest would be admissible for impeachment purposes if defendant took the stand. The court found no merit in defendant's argument, concluding that defendant's direct examination was subject to impeachment by the State. Further, defendant did not preserve the issue for review because he did not file a pretrial motion. The court also rejected defendant's contention that the trial court erred in imposing an excessive sentence. The court found that the trial court considered the sentencing guidelines and that the trial court listed at least four aggravating circumstances, including a prior felony conviction, that justified a departure from the sentencing range.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for possession of a firearm.

Louisiana Health Serv. & Indem. Co. v. Tarver


No. 92 CA 0354


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


622 So. 2d 277; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2589



July 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 19, 1993. Released for Publication August 19, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NUMBER 357,731, HONORABLE CARL A. GUIDRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which dismissed the insurer's claim seeking a refund of sums paid to the state because of uncashed benefit checks issued to policyholders.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer paid almost $ 600,000 to the state for uncashed health and accident insurance benefit checks pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:180(A). The insurer then instituted an action to obtain a refund. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the state and dismissed the insurer's claim. On appeal, the insurer argued that § 9:180(A) was unconstitutional because it resulted in a taking of property without just compensation in violation of La. Const. art. 1, § 4. In affirming the trial court's judgment, the appellate court held that § 9:180(A) allowed property to be presumed abandoned even though the obligation had prescribed as between the owner and the holder. The court noted that the insurer was the holder of an obligation in favor of its insured and that the expiration of a prescriptive period merely barred the insured's remedy but did not extinguish the cause of action itself. The court held that the legislative action did not violate the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the state.

State v. Cash Totalling $15,156.00


CA 92 1238, CA 92 1239, CA 92 1240, CA 92 1241


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


623 So. 2d 114; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2605



July 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF TANGIPAHOA, NOS. 9002790 C/W 9002926, 9003420 & 9003422, HONORABLE ROBERT H. MORRISON, III, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Tangipahoa (Louisiana), which ordered the forfeiture of a handgun and cash pursuant to the Seizure and Controlled Dangerous Substances Property Forfeiture Act of 1989, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2601 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Based on an informant's tip, police executed a search warrant at a house owned by appellant. A narcotics dog sniffed out cocaine and $ 851 in one bedroom, and in another bedroom sniffed out over $ 15,000 that was stashed in a footlocker. Police also found a handgun in this bedroom. In reversing the judgment, the court held that the $ 15,000 was not in proximity to the cocaine for the purpose of permitting an inference under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2611(G) that it was proceeds of drug sales made by appellant's son. The court noted that appellant also supplied evidence that the $ 15,000 and handgun were not connected to the cocaine sufficient to rebut the presumption under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2611(H) that these items were subject to forfeiture. The court noted that appellant testified that the $ 15,000 was hers and was related to financing she obtained to build a house, and that the owner of the gun, appellant's ex-husband, testified that he had given it to appellant as a safety precaution because their children lived with appellant in the house and the house had been the target of attempted break-ins.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that ordered the forfeiture of more than $ 15,000 in cash and a handgun.

Netherton Co. v. Caddo-Shreveport Car Sales


No. 24,809-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


621 So. 2d 22; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2461



June 23, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 368,903. Honorable C. J. Bolin, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of a judgment of the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which granted appellee tax commission summary judgment in the contractor's action to recover $ 48,833 paid in protest through the tax commission to the city as a use tax. The contractor argued that he was entitled to a credit against the city's use tax for sales tax paid to the parish school board.


OVERVIEW: The school board and the city imposed a sales and use tax on tangible personal property purchased or used within its boundaries. The contractor, a road and bridge builder, had purchased equipment, some of which it later used on highway construction projects within the city limits. When the contractor purchased the equipment, he paid the state sales tax and the school board tax. The contractor argued that he should have been credited with the tax it paid to the school board under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2718.2A. The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of the commission. Specifically, the court held that § 33:2718.2A mandated that the contractor be credited against the sales and use tax imposed by the city where he had paid sales and use taxes to the parish school board based upon the same tangible personal property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment entered in favor of the tax commission and ordered that summary judgment be granted in favor of the contractor. Furthermore, the court ordered the tax commission to remit and return to the contractor the sum of $ 48,832.59, plus interest at the per annum rate established by statute, until paid.

Injury Hotline v. Houck


No. 24,818-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


621 So. 2d 127; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2458



June 23, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 12, 1993. Rehearing Denied August 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 40,209. Honorable James M. Dozier, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff law firm challenged a judgment from the Third Judicial District Court, Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana, which denied its request for mandamus, injunction, and declaratory judgment after defendants, the city, the sheriff, and the chief of police, denied the law firm's written request to inspect and copy vehicular accident reports on file at the police department.


OVERVIEW: The law firm filed an action for mandamus, injunction, and declaratory relief seeking the right to examine, copy, and microfilm motor vehicle accident reports in the city's custody. Defendants had denied an earlier written request. The trial court denied relief, holding that the law firm did not have the right to examine the public records because it was not an interested person under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:398(H). The law firm did not represent anyone involved in an accident, but sought access to the reports to solicit business. On appeal, the court reversed. The law firm made its written request to examine the reports and the trial court rendered its decision prior to the effective date of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:398(H). Because the statute affected a substantive right guaranteed by La. Const. art. 12 § 3, it could not be given retroactive effect. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:31 gave the law firm the right to free and unrestricted access to the records. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:398(D)(4) entitled the law firm to inspect, copy, or reproduce the reports. Defendants were ordered to grant the law firm access to all accident reports requested prior to the effective date of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of the law firm's request for mandamus, injunction, and declaratory judgment. The court ordered defendants to grant the law firm access to the accident reports it requested to inspect and copy.

LeBlanc v. Meza


No. 92-1040


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


620 So. 2d 521; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2347



June 16, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana; Hon. G. Bradford Ware, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed the judgment from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana) dismissing their medical malpractice action against defendant physicians and defendant hospital on the grounds that it was barred by the one and three prescriptive periods in La. Rev. Stat. Ann § 9:5628. The patient had contracted the HIV virus from a blood transfusion four years earlier.


OVERVIEW: In 1985 the patient was given a blood transfusion that contained the HIV virus which can lead to the development of AIDS. At the time, no test was available to test the hospital's blood supply. In 1989 the patient was diagnosed with HIV when she took a blood test for an insurance policy. The district court dismissed the claim as barred by § 9:5628. On review, the patient argued that she should have been advised by her doctor to test for HIV after her surgery, and that because of the failure, the doctrine of contra non valentem suspended the operation of the statute until her condition was diagnosed. The court rejected the argument, holding that the Louisiana Supreme Court had held that the doctrine did not apply in medical malpractice cases. The court found the result to be unfortunate but was nevertheless constrained to affirm the dismissal. The court determined that § 9:5628 was peremptive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court dismissing the patient's medical malpractice claim.

Reeves v. Allstate Ins. Co.


No. 92-1200


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


619 So. 2d 202; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2067



June 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Iberia, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Richard T. Haik, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a passenger who was injured in an automobile accident, and defendant, the uninsured motorist carrier of the driver's employer, appealed a judgment of the 16th Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia, Louisiana, which held that Arkansas law applied to construe the uninsured motorist coverage in an automobile insurance policy issued by defendant, the driver's uninsured motorist insurer.


OVERVIEW: The driver moved to Louisiana when he separated from his wife. He purchased an automobile insurance policy from an Arkansas insurance agent. The vehicle was purchased, financed, licensed, and registered in Louisiana. The policy was delivered to the driver's former address in Arkansas. The policy provided lower limits for uninsured motorist coverage than it did for bodily injury liability. The policy did not provide underinsured motorist insurance and there was no written waiver of the higher liability limits for selection of lower uninsured motorist limits. The trial court granted summary judgment to the driver's uninsured motorist carrier and held that Arkansas law, which did not require a written waiver, was applicable. The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The court held that Louisiana law applied to an insured vehicle that was registered, garaged, and licensed in Louisiana, even though the policy was neither delivered nor issued for delivery in Louisiana.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State Farm Fire & Casualty Ins. Co. v. Young


No. 92-1192


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


619 So. 2d 161; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2082



June 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 18, 1993. Rehearing Denied July 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE WORKER'S COMPENSATION BOARD, DISTRICT 3, HONORABLE MARK ZIMMERMAN, ADMINISTRATIVE HEARING OFFICER, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an employer and an insurer, sought review of a judgment of the Worker's Compensation Board (Louisiana), which dismissed their petition to modify a worker's compensation judgment for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The hearing officer had determined that jurisdiction was proper in the district court where a separate petition for modification had also been filed and judgment rendered.


OVERVIEW: The employer and insurer sought to have a worker's compensation judgment entered in favor of the employee modified by the district court so as to reduce the employee's benefits to supplemental earning benefits. The district court ultimately refused to modify the award. Subsequently, the employer and insurer filed a petition with the hearing officer asking that the same worker's compensation award be modified. On the basis that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction, the hearing officer dismissed the petition. The court affirmed. Specifically, the court held that the simultaneous repeal of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1331(C ) and the enactment of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.8(B) did not transfer subject matter jurisdiction to the Office of Worker's Compensation for modification cases pending but not yet heard or ruled upon in the district court. As such, the court found that the hearing officer had appropriately determined that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction in the matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the hearing officer's judgment dismissing the employer and insurer's petition or lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

 

895 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Elliott v. State


CA 92 0773


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


619 So. 2d 137; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2294



May 28, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, NO. 372,732, HONORABLE CARL GUIDRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, State of Louisiana and state officials, appealed a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which granted plaintiff inmates' motion for certification of a class action under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. arts. 591 and 592to challenge the constitutionality of legislation limiting the inmates' right to post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmates contended that the legislation, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8, unconstitutionally cut off their right to file motions for post-conviction relief. They contended that all of the inmates in the prison shared in this common right, so that the commonality prerequisite, La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 591(1), for a class action was met. In reversing the judgment, the court held that the trial court abused its discretion in certifying the class. The court noted several ways in which the inmate population did not share the same right with respect to post-conviction relief. For example, the court observed that many inmates had already exhausted their right to relief, so that the curtailment of the right had no effect on them. The court also noted that if even one inmate successfully obtained a declaration that art. 930.8 was unconstitutional, all of the similarly situated inmates would benefit from the declaration.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that granted class action status to the inmates' declaratory judgment action.

 

896 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Rick v. State


No. 92 CA 1000


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


619 So. 2d 1149; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2276



May 28, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM A JUDGMENT OF THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF TANGIPAHOA, SUIT NUMBER 8901980, HONORABLE KENNETH J. FOGG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the department of transportation and development (DOTD), appealed from the Twenty-First Judicial District in and for the Parish of Tangipahoa (Louisiana), which rendered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, the family of a deceased who was struck and killed by a train as she drove over a railroad crossing.


OVERVIEW: The crossing in question had a warning sign, a cross buck, and a stop sign. The DOTD contended that it had no duty to provide protective devices or signalize railroad crossings on roads which were not part of the state highway system. The trial court determined that the DOTD owed a duty to the decedent to see that this crossing was properly upgraded with the installation of active warning devices because it was aware of the high volume of traffic and the high number of trains traveling through the crossing, and because it was aware that the existing signs were inadequate. The court held that such circumstances constituted the assumption by the DOTD of the responsibility to upgrade the crossing. The failure to do so within a reasonable time after assumption of the responsibility constituted a breach of duty. Consequently, the court concluded that the trial court was not manifestly erroneous in determining that the DOTD had ample time to install the protective devices and upgrade the crossing and its failure to timely do so was a breach of duty. Moreover, the court agreed with the trial court that had active safety devices been installed, the accident would not have occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the deceased's family and against the DOTD.

 

897 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Trail Mining, Inc. v. Sun


92 CA 0970


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


619 So. 2d 118; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2274



May 28, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY, STATE OF LOUISIANA, SUIT NUMBER 9114205, THE HONORABLE STEPHEN A. DUCZER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company sought review of a judgment of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which denied its petition for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against defendant village.


OVERVIEW: A company sought to mine a gravel deposit on property that was located within the limits of a village. The village had an ordinance that prohibited the digging of a gravel pit within a 1,200 foot radius of any building that was used as a residence, unless those affected would waive the prohibition. Because the property owners within the 1,200 foot radius would not waive the prohibition, the company filed a complaint against the village in which it argued that the ordinance was unconstitutional, or in the alternative, the ordinance was invalid because it violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4723. The trial court dismissed the petition, and the company appealed. On review, the court reversed the judgment below. The court held that the village did not have a general plan, and there were no definitions, descriptions, or classifications for use in property development. Rather, the ordinance under scrutiny was a solitary, single industry restriction. Because there was no comprehensive plan, and the ordinance was not a comprehensive plan, the enactment of the ordinance did not comply with the statute and was invalid. The court did not address the constitutionality of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and rendered an order that a judgment be entered that declared an ordinance of the village invalid and unenforceable. Costs of the appeal were assessed against the village.

West Jefferson Levee Dist. v. Coast Quality Constr. Corp.


No. 92-CA-506, No. 92-CA-507, No. 92-CA-508

620 So. 2d 319; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2017



May 25, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 384-086 c/w 376-286 AND 383-659. DIVISION "G". HONORABLE M. JOSEPH TIEMANN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, AMENDED IN PART AND AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, levee district, challenged the decisions from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, which entered judgment in favor of appellees, landowners, in expropriations suits filed under the quick taking statutes, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 38:351 et seq.

Landowners filed answers and reconventional demands for additional amounts of compensation. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the landowners. Levee district appealed, alleging that the awards were excessive and that property was not valued correctly. OUTCOME: In an expropriations suit filed under quick taking statutes, the court affirmed the judgments in part, amended in part and affirmed as amended.

State v. Conrad


No. 93-KA-130


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


620 So. 2d 366; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2029



May 25, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 91-4068. DIVISION "A". HONORABLE G. THOMAS PORTEOUS



DISPOSITION: AMENDED, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64. On appeal, he argued that the evidence was insufficient for his conviction, his post-trial motions were improperly denied, his sentence was improper, and his motion to reconsider the sentence should have been allowed. The court also reviewed for errors patent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed pro se post-trial motions and his counsel filed an amended motion for new trial. On appeal, the court held that the pro se motions were not validly before it. Defendant could not be both represented and representative at the same time. Also, defendant's motions had no basis in law under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 859. The court held that the evidence was sufficient for conviction. Although defendant did not get away with the victim's purse, the facts were sufficient to establish the "taking" element under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64. The court held that the State proved beyond a reasonable doubt all the elements necessary to sustain the armed robbery conviction. Therefore, defendant's counsel's amended motion for new trial was properly denied. The court held that defendant's sentence of 49-1/2 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence with credit for time served was not excessive, and the record supported the sentence. Despite the trial court's failure to follow La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 (effective Jan. 31, 1992), the court affirmed the sentence. The court amended the sentence form to correct an error patent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for armed robbery and his sentence of 49-1/2 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence with credit for time served.

Saint Bernard Ass'n of Educators v. Saint Bernard Parish Sch. Bd.


No. 92-CA-2173


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


619 So. 2d 678; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1853



May 13, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE 34TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, ST. BERNARD PARISH. NO. 67-859. DIVISION "B". HONORABLE DAVID S. GORBATY, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school board appealed from a judgment of the 34th Judicial District Court, St. Bernard Parish (Louisiana) in favor of plaintiff teacher's union, which declared that under the parties' collective bargaining agreement and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 17:1201,1202, the board could deduct no more than the amount paid a substitute in the event of an unauthorized absence.


OVERVIEW: The parties' agreement provided for additional authorized sick days beyond the 10 days provided in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:1201(A)(1). The board asserted that for unauthorized sick days, beyond those provided in the agreement, the teacher should lose a day's pay. The union asserted that under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:1202, the deduction should be no greater than the amount paid for a substitute. The trial court found in favor of the union. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 17:1202 was intended to give teachers a fringe benefit, and the fact that the agreement provided additional sick days could not be construed as a waiver of the teacher's benefit under § 17:1202. The court found that this result did not create the potential for abuse of sick leave, because the board could remove such an abuser under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:443. The court ruled that this construction of the statutes and the agreement did not amount to an unconstitutional gift, because it was a benefit earned by the employment itself.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court judgment which declared that the board could deduct no more than the amount paid a substitute in the event of a teacher's unauthorized absence.

Jurisich v. Hopson Marine Serv. Co.


No. 93-C-0049


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


619 So. 2d 1111; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1915



May 13, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON SUPERVISORY WRITS FROM 25th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PLAQUEMINES PARISH. NO. 35-138. DIVISION "A". HONORABLE MICHAEL E. KIRBY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant energy corporation sought supervisory writs from an order of the 25th Judicial District Court, Plaquemines Parish (Louisiana), which denied defendant's exceptions to plaintiff leaseholders suit for damages to their oyster leases.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs bought suit against defendant energy corporation and others claiming damage to their oyster leases. The trial court denied defendant's exceptions. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that plaintiffs had the right to bring action for damage to their leases under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 56:422 et seq and 56:423(B). The court held that the wildlife and fisheries commission was not required to comply with public bidding procedures before it granted shell dredging leases because the harvesting of live oysters was not a mineral right as defined by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 31:4 of the Mineral Code. The court also held that the 1990 amendments to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 41:1214 which ratified and continued all oyster leases then in force was not special legislation and an unconstitutional attempt to ratify unauthorized acts. The court held that the leases were not disguised sales of navigable waterbottoms which was prohibited by La. Const. art. IX, § 3 or a donation of state property in violation of La. Const. art. VII, § 14 because the leases were not tantamount to full ownership, and there were serious obligations on the lessees which provided consideration for the leases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied defendant's exceptions to plaintiff leaseholders suit for damages to their oyster leases.

State v. Corley


No. CR92-1193


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


617 So. 2d 1292; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1720



May 5, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 7, 1993. Rehearing Refused June 9, 1993, Reported at: 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2310.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ELEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF SABINE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE ROBERT E. BURGESS, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 11th Judicial District Court, Parish of Sabine, State of Louisiana, which convicted him of second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was married to his wife for one week when he murdered her. He was convicted of second-degree murder and sentenced. He sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment on the grounds that defendant could not have used the insanity or intoxication defense because the fact that defendant was drinking before he committed the murder was not, of itself, sufficient to negate specific intent. The court held that defendant failed to establish a specific statutory provision to disqualify the district attorney's secretary from service on the grand jury. The court further ruled that voluntary intoxication was a defense to a prosecution for a crime only when the condition precluded the presence of a specific criminal intent or of a special knowledge required in that particular crime. The court concluded that defendant understood what he was doing and what was happening because he continued to refuse to give a statement until he spoke to an attorney his father was hiring. The court further decided that defendant's appearance and conduct after arrest further negated his intoxication defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of second-degree murder.

State v. Wright


No. 92-KA-1881


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


618 So. 2d 540; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1626



April 28, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 333-788. SECTION "I". HONORABLE SHIRLEY G. WIMBERLY, JR., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of distribution of heroin under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A)(1) and sentenced him to life imprisonment under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(B)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold 1.26 grams of heroin to an undercover officer and was convicted of distribution of heroin under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A)(1) and sentenced to life imprisonment under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:.966(B)(1). On appeal, the court held that the legal sentence in the transcript prevailed over the illegal sentence in the minute entry. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:966(A)(1), 40:966(B)(1) did not require a minimum amount of heroin in order for defendant to be convicted of heroin distribution and sentenced to life imprisonment. Thus, under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 787, 797(4) , 798(1), the trial court properly allowed the State to challenge for cause and properly disqualified those prospective jurors who stated that they disagreed with the mandatory life sentence regardless of the amount of heroin involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted defendant of distribution of heroin, and which sentenced defendant to life imprisonment.

Rey v. Guidry


No. 93-CA-52


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


618 So. 2d 425; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1674



April 27, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON. NO. 403-545. DIVISION "D". HONORABLE WALTER E. KOLLIN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA), appealed from a judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), in a personal injury action arising from an automobile accident, which granted partial summary judgment to the plaintiff's insurer, finding LIGA's coverage on behalf of an insolvent insurer to be primary, and held LIGA liable for plaintiff's damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was involved in an auto accident with another driver, whose insurer was insolvent. The LIGA was substituted for the insolvent insurer. The trial court found LIGA, in lieu of the insolvent insurer, had primary coverage, and not plaintiff's uninsured motorist (UM) insurer. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that under the 1992 amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386, plaintiff was required to exhaust his UM coverage before making a claim against LIGA. The court held that plaintiff's claim against LIGA was still "pending" under 1992 La. Acts 237, § 3, which amended La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386, when the trial court considered the issue of primary coverage between the UM insurer and LIGA, thus the trial court should have applied the 1992 amendment to § 22:1386 then in effect, which made the UM coverage primary. The court held that the legislature intended the amendment to be retroactive, and that this did not unconstitutionally interfere with any vested rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court judgment which granted partial summary judgment to plaintiff's insurer and found LIGA's coverage to be primary, and rendered judgment in favor of LIGA, holding the plaintiff's insurer primarily responsible for plaintiff's claim.

State v. All Pro Paint & Body Shop


No. 92 KA 0656


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


618 So. 2d 962; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1610



April 23, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, NUMBER 1-91-1, IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE FREDDIE PITCHER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a body shop and its owner, appealed a decision of the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which convicted them of illegal transportation and disposal of hazardous wastes. Defendants argued that the trial court erred in denying their motion to quash and in finding that the evidence was sufficient to convict them.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged by grand jury indictment and convicted of illegal transportation of hazardous wastes and illegal disposal of hazardous wastes under La. Rev. Stat. § 30:2183G(2). The trial court found that the body shop owner paid a third party to dispose of containers of spent paint thinner at two uninhabited houses. Tests conclusively proved that the substances were hazardous waste. Finding guilt, the trial court deferred sentencing, placed defendants on active supervised probation for three years, and applied special conditions to the probation. Defendants appealed. The court held that as the trial court accepted the testimony of the State's witnesses and rejected those presented by the defense, a rational trier of fact could have concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that every element of the offenses had been established. However, the statutory scheme did not define the felony offense; it merely set guidelines for the definition of the offense. Thus, the definition of hazardous waste and penalties for violations were left to the executive branch, and the court found that this constituted an unconstitutional delegation of constitutional authority to the executive branch.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had refused to quash the indictment as unconstitutional, and the motion to quash was granted. As a result, the convictions and sentences were reversed.

Thibodeau v. Mayor & Councilmen of Morgan City


No. 92 CA 1050


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


619 So. 2d 595; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1613



April 23, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, NO. 83,855, ST. MARY PARISH, LOUISIANA, HONORABLE PAUL J. DEMAHY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART, AFFIRMED IN PART, AMENDED IN PART, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an injured diver and his parents, and defendants, the City of Morgan City and the State of Louisiana, appealed from a judgment of the 16th Judicial District Court, St. Mary Parish (Louisiana), which found the diver, the city, and the State equally liable for damages awarded to the diver and his parents for injuries sustained by the diver in a lake leased from the State by the city, limited by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106.


OVERVIEW: The diver, an experienced swimmer, had been trained to dive in the Coast Guard, but dove from a bulkhead into two feet of muddy water when he saw swimmers in chest-deep water 20 feet ahead, resulting in quadriplegia. A sign erected by the city after a similar accident three years earlier stated "Swim and Dive at Your Own Risk." The trial judge found each party 1/3 liable, awarded the $ 500,000 limit against both the city and the State, denied the parent's claims for emotional distress, and awarded the parents damages for loss of consortium. On appeal, the court amended. The court held that the "recreational immunity" statutes did not immunized the city from liability arising from its use of the leased property, and that the lease did not transfer garde from the State to the city so as to relieve the State of its duty to the diver. The court found that the city and State owed a duty to the diver to warn of the danger, and the city's sign did not warn of the nature of the risk. The court held that the parents had no cause of action without being present at the scene, and their derivative claim was subject to son's § 13:5106 cap, which limited total damages against both parties.


OUTCOME: The court amended the district court judgment, which awarded damages to the diver and his parents for injuries sustained by the diver in a lake leased from the State by the city, and otherwise affirmed. The court reversed the award to the parents for loss of consortium, re-allocated fault, reduced damages for loss of wages, and applied the statutory limit to total both the city and State awards.

McElveen v. Vernon Parish Police Jury

909 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. Johnson


No. 92-126


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


617 So. 2d 1213; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1555



April 21, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 7, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana; the Honorable William Polk, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a wrongfully arrested person and her minor children, sought review of a judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana that granted defendants, the State, the Department of Public Safety, a trooper, and a lieutenant's, exceptions of lis pendens and prescription.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the fifth supplemental and amending petition filed by plaintiffs on the grounds that the same parties had litigated the same issues in a suit in another parish. The court reversed, holding that the fifth supplemental and amending petition was not so similar to the suit filed in another parish as to warrant a grant of lis pendens. The allegations in the amended petition related back to the original petition because they concerned facts and issues surrounding the arrest. Because it related back, the other parish suit was not the "first suit" as required by La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 531, consequently, lis pendens was not proper to preempt the progression of the amended case. The court also found that the grant of prescription to be error, pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1153. The amended petition related back, because there was a factual connexity between its allegations and those of the original pleadings, and the named defendants had sufficient notice of the allegations to preserve evidence and prepare a defense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court that dismissed the plaintiffs' claim and granted defendants' exceptions of lis pendens and prescription.

State v. Bennett


No. CR91-257


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


617 So. 2d 550; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1486



April 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 11, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Thirtieth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Vernon, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Roy B. Tuck, Jr., District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the 13th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Vernon (Louisiana), convicting him of solicitation to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of solicitation to commit murder, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:28.1, after he attempted to hire a hit man to kill a witness who was going to testify against him in a criminal trial. The hit man was actually an undercover police officer. The court reversed defendant's conviction on the basis of one assignment of error without discussing the remaining assignments. On appeal by the State, the supreme court reversed the court's judgment and remanded the case for consideration of the remaining assignments of error. In affirming the conviction, the court held that § 14:28.1 was not unconstitutionally vague because the State needed to prove incitement of either first or second degree murder to prove defendant guilty. The court also held that § 14:28.1 was not duplicative of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:28, incitement of a felony, because it dealt with incitement of two of the worst types of felonies. The court further held that it was irrelevant whether the jury found defendant guilty of soliciting first degree murder or second degree murder because solicitation of either was proscribed under the same statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:28.1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

911 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Deville v. Budd Constr. Co.


No. 92-221


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


617 So. 2d 570; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1422



April 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused May 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Robert Brinkman, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; AMENDED IN PART; RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State and its Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD) appealed from judgments of the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana) finding them liable to plaintiffs, parents for the death or injury of their minor and for loss of consortium. The parents of one minor appealed claiming that damages awarded for the injuries to their child and for their loss of consortium were inadequate.


OVERVIEW: A minor was killed when he drove his vehicle into a hole in a highway that was under repair. Two other minors, who were passengers, were seriously injured. The minors' parents recovered judgments for personal injury, wrongful death, and loss of consortium against the State and DOTD. The court affirmed a judgment that the State and DOTD were 80 percent at fault, but reduced the damages awarded to one minor to the maximum established by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106. The State and DOTD did not in fact contract away their responsibility to the general public for the road construction and the placement of warning signs, and that duty was nondelegable in any event. La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.6, providing for compensation for the mental anguish of bystanders did not apply to limit the damages for mental anguish awarded to one of the injured minors, which were for anguish from the injuries he suffered in the accident, and not for witnessing the deaths of his companions. The damages awarded for the injuries and future medical expenses of one of the minors and for the loss of consortium of that minor's parents were inadequate and an abuse of discretion, and were increased accordingly.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified to reduce the damages awarded to one minor against the State to the statutory maximum, and to increase the damages awarded for the injuries and future medical expenses of one of the minors, and for loss of consortium of that minor's parents. As so modified the judgment was affirmed.

 

912 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roger


Cr92-1270


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


616 So. 2d 830; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1494



April 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 11, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE BYRON HEBERT, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of contributing to the delinquency of a juvenile, violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:92(7). Defendant waived formal arraignment and entered a plea of not guilty in the 15th Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana). The jury found him guilty on both counts. Defendant was sentenced to two years at hard labor on each count, to run concurrent, with credit for time served. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of two counts of contributing to the delinquency of a juvenile and was concurrently sentenced to two years on each count. He contended the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict. He claimed the district court erred in overruling his objection to the admission of testimony as a victim's "first report" of sexually assaultive behavior. He claimed there was no "sexually assaultive behavior", nor any act or conduct of a sexual nature proven. As there was no need for actual physical contact for the actions of a person to have been considered sexually assaultive behavior under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 801(D)(1)(d), the testimony was properly admitted. He also claimed the district court erred in imposing an excessive sentence. Yet, after a review of the record and a request to the clerk, the court found that no motion to reconsider was made at sentencing or later filed, so defendant was precluded from raising this point on appeal. The district court's failure to have informed him of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief was not grounds to have reversed the sentence, but notice of the period was required within 10 days of this opinion.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and the sentences imposed were affirmed. Instructions were provided regarding the requirement that defendant be notified of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief.

 

913 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Interdiction of F.T.E.


No. 24,669-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


622 So. 2d 667; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1229



March 31, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted April 29, 1993. On Rehearing August 11, 1993, Reported at: 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2689.
Withdrawn from the Bound Volume On Grant of Rehearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 361,969. Honorable C. J. Bolin, Judge

Orginally Published at 619 So.2d 74 and Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent invalid appealed an order to pay attorney fees and expenses on behalf of petitioner, his brother, in an interdiction proceeding in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana). He argued that the trial court erred in finding that attorney fees were to be included as costs in an interdiction proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The invalid was involuntarily admitted to the hospital, and his brother petitioned for judicial commitment and interdiction. Following several hearings, the trial court committed the invalid to a nursing home and ordered an interdiction. The invalid appealed, and the court found that the trial court erred in ordering the involuntary judicial commitment and full interdiction of his person and property. It ordered the invalid, under a limited interdiction, to pay three-fourths of the brother's attorney fees and all expenses. The invalid appealed, and the court held that the trial court was correct in awarding fees to the brother for fees in the limited interdiction action. Yet, the trial court abused its discretion in determining the appropriate amount of the attorney fee award. Further, it determined that any argument as to the constitutionality of the statutes was not properly before the court. As the invalid had an opportunity to be heard and to defend his position, his constitutional attack on the interdiction proceeding was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment ordering the invalid to pay the attorney fees and expenses of his brother, but amended the award, calling it unreasonable.

 

914 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Evans


No. 24,718-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


627 So. 2d 664; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1259



March 31, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 16, 1993. Released for Publication January 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 49,119. Honorable John R. Joyce, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), which entered a jury verdict convicting him of theft of over $ 100.00 but less than $ 500.00.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in December 1989 with theft of over $ 500.00 in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:67. After trial in April 1992 defendant was convicted of theft of over $ 100.00 but less than $ 500.00. On appeal the court affirmed. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to quash on the basis of the expiration of the two-year time limitation for commencement of trial in felony cases pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 578. Under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 580 the running of the period of limitation was suspended upon the filing of a motion to quash or other preliminary plea; defendant's filing of a joint motion for a continuance in April 1991 constituted a preliminary plea such that the limitation period was suspended, giving the State a minimum of one year after the granting of the continuance to commence trial. The trial court did not err in failing to declare a mistrial after the jury became aware of a courthouse bomb threat; the trial court was in the best position to determine whether defendant was prejudiced and there was no indication in the record that the bomb threat affected the jury's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

915 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Perow


No. 24,582-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


616 So. 2d 1336; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1230



March 31, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 153,082. Honorable Eugene W. Bryson, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which entered a jury verdict convicting him of second degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, aged 15 at the time of the crime, allegedly said that he wanted to shoot somebody. Defendant pulled a rifle out of his trench coat and shot the victim as she walked through a nearby parking lot. Defendant was tried as an adult pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1570. On appeal from defendant's conviction the court affirmed. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motions for new trial and for post verdict judgment of acquittal; the evidence that defendant aimed the gun at the victim, announced his intention to kill somebody, and laughed after firing the shot was sufficient to establish specific intent. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion in arrest of judgment; La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1570, vesting jurisdiction over certain offenses committed by juveniles in the district court, and La. Const. art. V, § 19, which authorized La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1570, were not unconstitutional. The trial court did not err in admitting into evidence two photographs of the victim; any prejudicial effect of the photographs was outweighed by their probative value as corroborative of other evidence and to establish the location and severity of the wound.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

916 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Radiofone v. City of New Orleans


No. 92-CA-1271


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


615 So. 2d 1067; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1073



March 11, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 26, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 91-2760, DIVISION "K". HONORABLE RICHARD J. GANUCHEAU, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation appealed from a judgment of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, Louisiana, which granted summary judgment to defendant, the City of New Orleans, Louisiana, after holding that the "gross receipts tax" enacted in New Orleans, La., Mun. Code § 14211 did not violate La. Const. art. VI, § 28. Defendants, the City's mayor and council members, were also parties.


OVERVIEW: The tax enacted in New Orleans, La., Mun. Code § 14211 required any person who furnished telecommunications services for compensation to pay a tax for the privilege of engaging in such business in the City. The tax was based on a percentage of the gross receipts of the business. The corporation filed suit for a declaratory judgment that the tax was an occupational license tax that exceeded the maximum limits imposed by La. Const. art. VI, § 28, which prohibited a local government from imposing an occupational license tax not greater than that imposed by the state. Both the corporation and the City filed motions for summary judgment, and the trial court found in favor of the City. On appeal, the court held that the tax violated art. VI, § 28 because the operational effect of the tax was to raise revenues, which was an exercise of the City's taxing power rather than its police power. The court found that no matter how "occupational license tax" was defined, the City's tax fell within that definition for purposes of the prohibition set forth in art. VI, § 28.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and rendered judgment declaring that the tax was unconstitutional.

 

917 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


President & Bd. of Trustees of Spring Hill College v. New Orleans


No. 92-CA-1033


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


617 So. 2d 8; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1069



March 11, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused May 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 89-26507, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE ROBERT A. KATZ, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Board of Trustees of a college, brought suit to recover inheritance taxes paid under protest to defendant, the City of New Orleans. The college sought recovery of taxes collected by the City pursuant to New Orleans, La., Ordinance 11,262, § 28A-2(d). The Civil District Court, for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) sustained the city's exception of no cause of action. The college appealed.


OVERVIEW: The college argued on appeal that the city's inheritance tax, when levied against an educational institution like the college, conflicted with state constitutional statutory law and was thus invalid. Unlike the city's inheritance tax, New Orleans, La., Ordinance 11,262, § 28A-2(d), Louisiana's inheritance tax, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2402(6), exempted not only educational institutions located in Louisiana, but also those located in other states offering reciprocity to Louisiana institutions. The court found that there was no conflict between the city's ordinance and § 47:2402(6), because the state exemption applied only to the state inheritance tax. The ordinance thus did not conflict with the state statute. Further, the Louisiana Constitution granted home rule to the city, which thereby retained the power to tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment sustaining the city's exception of no cause of action.

State v. Moses


No. 92 KA 0394


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


615 So. 2d 1030; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1004



March 5, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 3, 1993. Rehearing denied April 28, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, (#90-CR2-45926), PARISH OF WASHINGTON, HONORABLE BRADY FITZSIMMONS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of Washington, (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of two counts of molestation of a juvenile and sentenced him to five years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant got a student out of her home economics class and took her to the band room to talk about her family problems. Defendant undid the student's top buttons and said he was checking for the rash that she said she had. Defendant put his hand on the student's bare breast and then performed oral sex on her. On another occasion defendant took another student into the school library to discuss rumors of her being pregnant. Defendant started rubbing the student's stomach. With her panties down defendant started touching her vaginal area. At trial defendant denied the allegations. He was found guilty of two counts of molestation of a juvenile and sentenced to five years imprisonment. On appeal defendant alleged the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions. The court affirmed the convictions, but vacated the sentences, and remanded the matter for resentencing. The court held that because the victims provided detailed information about the incidents, and none of defendant's allegations supported a finding that the jury's acceptance of the testimony of the victims was irrational the jury could have found the essential elements of the offenses beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions. The court vacated the sentence, and remanded the matter for resentencing.

Guillory v. Guillory


No. 92 CA 0051


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


615 So. 2d 975; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1036



March 5, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 28, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NO. 86,565), PARISH OF ST. MARY, HONORABLE PAUL J. deMAHY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father appealed an order of the 16th Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Mary (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment and dismissed his suit against defendant mother to disavow paternity. The father contended that the trial court erred in determining that he was prohibited under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 189 from litigating paternity of the child 13 years after his birth.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother were divorced, and the father was ordered to pay child support. Thirteen years after the child's birth, the father filed a suit for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief and an action en desaveu, which alleged that he was not the biological father of the child. The mother filed a peremptory exception of no cause of action and a motion for summary judgment. The trial court granted the motion for summary judgment and the father appealed. The father contended that the trial court erred in determining that he was prohibited from litigating paternity of the child 13 years after his birth, under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 189. The court affirmed and held that the father's right to disavow paternity was extinguished under the statute. The court rejected the father's argument that the legal presumption of paternity under La. Civ. Code Ann. arts. 184, 187 was unconstitutional. The court held that the rebuttable presumption was rationally related to the state's vital interest in preserving the integrity of the family unit and avoiding the stigma of illegitimacy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court which dismissed the father's suit against the mother to disavow paternity of the couple's child, 13 years after the child's birth.

 

920 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pierre


No. CR92-921


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


614 So. 2d 1309; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 989



March 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Twelfth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Michael J. Johnson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant minor sought review of a jury decision from the Twelfth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana), convicting him of manslaughter in the killing of a 13-year-old boy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his manslaughter conviction, based solely on circumstantial evidence and a jailhouse informer's testimony, finding that he had aided and abetted three other minors in abducting, raping, and murdering a 13-year-old boy more than five years before trial. On appeal, the court held that the juvenile bindover statue, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1570 (1984), was constitutional even though it did not require a preliminary hearing to decide whether defendant were mature enough to be tried as an adult. Defendant lacked standing to raise the issue of whether the Fifth Amendment rights of a co-defendant, the State's star witness who unexpectedly recanted on the stand his previous statements implicating defendant, had been violated. The State was permitted to declare the recanting witness hostile and to cross-examine him pursuant to La. Code Evid. Ann. arts. 607 and 613. The jailhouse informer was not an "agent" of the State because he received nothing of value in exchange for his testimony against defendant. The trial court properly restricted defense counsel's repetitive voir dire examination. Circumstantial evidence of defendant's complicity was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Van Buren


No. 92-KA-1249


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT.


615 So. 2d 455; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 876



February 26, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 353-377, SECTION "I". HONORABLE SHIRLEY G. WIMBERLY, JR., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "I" (Louisiana), which had convicted him of simple burglary of an inhabited dwelling, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence, which was granted, and a motion to suppress identification, which was denied. Defendant contended that both the one-on-one identification made immediately after he was apprehended and the in-court identification by witnesses should have been suppressed. On appeal the court held that during identification, even though defendant was required to wear clothes found beside him when he was arrested, where the circumstances necessitate such a procedure and when the identification is not overly suggestive to violate defendant's due process rights, such identification may be allowed. The in-field identification in this case was not so suggestive. The identifications were made shortly after the burglary, and they were not the products of a lineup. Identifications based on clothing, where the clothing had been suppressed, were not unconstitutional where the evidence would have been discovered or obtained in a legal fashion. The positive identifications were not a direct result of the police's use of the illegally seized clothes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for simple burglary of an inhabited dwelling.

State v. Wheelwright


No. 92-KA-697


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


615 So. 2d 385; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 943



February 25, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON. NO. 92-907, DIVISION "S". HONORABLE JOSEPH F. GREFER, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him with possession of cocaine under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967C. Based upon a multiple offender bill and defendant's guilty plea, he was sentenced to seven years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted with possession of cocaine under § 40:967C and sentenced to five years at hard labor. The State filed a multiple offender bill and defendant entered a plea of guilty. The trial court vacated its original sentence and sentenced defendant to seven years at hard labor. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that defendant did not file a motion to suppress at any time before, during, or after trial; therefore he could not argue that the objects were seized pursuant to an unconstitutional search. The court concluded that the cocaine seized was not the fruit of an illegal seizure of defendant. The State proved beyond a reasonable doubt all the elements necessary to sustain defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine. The court ruled that the record proved that defendant's counsel informed the trial court that defendant wanted to plead guilty to the charge. Defendant stated that he agreed with the plea and understood his right to a hearing, but wished to waive the hearing and enter his plea. Therefore, defendant intelligently waived his rights and plead guilty to the multiple bill.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for possession of cocaine.
