State v. Wiley


No. 24,551-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


614 So. 2d 862; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 742



February 24, 1993, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 29,735. Honorable Leon H. Whitten, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson (Louisiana), which convicted him of distribution of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A) and sentenced him as a habitual offender to 15 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with selling cocaine during an undercover investigation. On appeal of his conviction, he argued, among 29 points of error, that the information was defective, that the trial court erred in its evidence rulings, and that he was deprived of exculpatory evidence. In affirming, the court ruled that the identity of the buyer of the drugs was subject to discovery and not required to be specified in the information. The court reviewed the evidence rulings and held that the trial court determination of relevance was afforded great weight and was not disturbed absent an abuse of discretion, which the court did not find. The court held that admission of the record of defendant's prior drug conviction to impeach his testimony was error because the record included a nolle prosequi of another charge, contrary to La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 609.1(C), but that the error was harmless. The court also ruled that the prosecution should have informed defendant that his co-defendant had pleaded guilty and denied that defendant was involved in the sale, but that this error was harmless because the co-defendant was a witness for the defense and testified to the same statement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence by the trial court.

 

924 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Jordan v. Intercontinental Bulktank Corp.


No. CA 90 2146


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


621 So. 2d 1141; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2448



February 19, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 28, 1993. Released for Publication June 23, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE EIGHTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF WEST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NUMBER 21,033, DIVISION "D", HONORABLE JACK T. MARIONNEAUX, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; AMENDED AND AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged an order in the District Court for Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which after jury trial awarded appellee injured seaman substantial damages under the Jones Act, codified at 46 U.S.C.S. § 688.


OVERVIEW: Employer claimed that the trial court erred by: (1) failing to properly control the proceedings; (2) failing to confine closing arguments within proper bounds; (3) excluding the testimony of its expert economist; (4) allowing punitive damages; (5) allowing $ 17.00 per day in maintenance cure, and (6) awarding prejudgment interest. The court amended its judgment but affirmed. The court said that a trial court had a wide berth when it came to control of the proceedings and that it would not have reversed unless a clear abuse of that discretion was shown. In addition, the court said that the trial court had abused its discretion in excluding the testimony of a substitute witness, but that the error was harmless. The court also held that the maintenance award should have been calculated at $ 8.00 per day, not $ 17.00 per day. Additionally, the court said that prejudgment interest was only proper from date of judgment, not the date of suit. Finally, it reduced the punitive damages by one-half, and it refused to address the constitutional claims as they were not preserved for appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was amended to reduce the award for lost wages, reduce the award for maintenance to and reduce the punitive damages award by one-half the award. The legal interest was amended from only the date of judgment, and the remainder of the judgment was affirmed. The court ordered employer to pay all costs of the appeal.

 

925 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Miles v. Connick


No. 92-CA-2002


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


613 So. 2d 1169; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 476



February 11, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused March 10, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 92-8872, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE MAX N. TOBIAS, JR., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant district attorney appealed from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, Division "L" (Louisiana), which entered judgment granting plaintiff inmate's petition for a writ of mandamus compelling the district attorney to produce to a third party all documents relating to the inmate's criminal case. The district attorney claimed that the trial court improperly applied La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:32(C)(2) (amended 1992).


OVERVIEW: After the district attorney denied the inmate's request for documents in the district attorney's possession relating to his case to be provided to a third party, the inmate obtained a writ of mandamus compelling production. On appeal, the court affirmed. The district attorney claimed that the trial court improperly applied La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:32(C)(2) (amended 1989) instead of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:32(C)(1)(a) (Supp. 1992). The court disagreed, pointing out that the 1989 amendment did not change the language of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:32(C)(2) (amended 1989). The court held that the legislature intended to legislature to establish the procedure for obtaining access to public records from the custodian of non-state agencies, clerks of courts, and state agencies. The district attorney's office was a state agency; hence, the trial court did not err when it applied La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:32C(2) (Supp. 1992). The court also held that § 44:32(C) was not unconstitutionally ambiguous. The court further denied the inmate's request for damages under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 44:35 (Supp. 1992) and La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2164 (1961).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which issued a writ of mandamus compelling the district attorney to provide copies of the requested documents. Costs of the appeal were assessed against the district attorney.

Greis v. Lake Charles Memorial Hosp.


No. 92-97


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


613 So. 2d 1023; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 375



February 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, Honorable Charley Quienalty, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee filed an appeal from the decision of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which dismissed the claims of the employee and ordered that all future matters on the claim were to be litigated before the office of workers' compensation.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured while working for appellee employer. A compensation claim was filed with the office of workers compensation for resolution of the claim after the employer and its insurer refused to pay worker's compensation benefits. The parties received the recommendation of the office, and the recommendation was rejected. The employee filed a petition for worker's compensation benefits and penalties and attorney's fees in the district court. The employer filed a declinatory exception of subject matter jurisdiction. The trial court sustained the exception. The employee challenged the decision. The court disagreed with the trial court. The court found that the employee's claim was filed with the office prior to January 1, 1990. Since one of the parties rejected the office's recommendation, the claim had not been resolved. The exception of subject matter jurisdiction was overruled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which dismissed the claims of the employee and ordered that all future matters on the claim were to be litigated before the office of workers' compensation.

Cornett v. State


No. 92-148


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


614 So. 2d 189; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 366



February 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, Honorable James C. McInnis, District Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the State of Louisiana through a hospital, appealed from a judgment of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which was entered in favor of plaintiffs, a decedent's wife and their two children, in a wrongful death and survival action pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39 et seq. The trial court limited plaintiffs' recovery to $ 500,000 pursuant to § 40:1299.39.


OVERVIEW: The decedent suffered from symptoms of acromegaly and sleep apnea, and he died from cardio-pulmonary arrest after being diagnosed and treated in the hospital. The hospital contended that the trial court erred in finding that it breached the relevant standard of care. Plaintiffs filed motions to supplement the record on appeal to assert that the hospital was liable for its primary or independent negligence, as well as vicarious liability. In affirming the trial court's judgment, the court held that (1) there was no error in the finding that the hospital breached the standard of care that it owed the decedent based on evidence that the decedent's condition was treatable and that he would have survived if he had received appropriate medical treatment, (2) there was no abuse of discretion in the award of loss of future earnings and the damages payable to the decedent's children, (3) the motions to supplement the record were denied because of plaintiffs' failure to previously allege the hospital's direct liability, and (4) plaintiffs' challenge to the limitation of damages under § 40:1299.39 would not be considered because the attorney general was not served as a party.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment awarding damages in favor of plaintiffs.

State v. Jack


No. CR92-666


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


614 So. 2d 215; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 308



February 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF CALCASIEU, STATE OF LOUISIANA, BEFORE THE HONORABLE WILLIAM MCLEOD, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which convicted him of aggravated rape, attempted second degree murder, and aggravated crime against nature.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for aggravated crime against nature, aggravated rape, and attempted second degree murder. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion for mistrial due to a reference by the prosecution to inadmissible evidence of other crimes allegedly committed by him. Defendant also claimed that there was insufficient evidence to convict him, and that the trial judge failed to adequately articulate the reasons and factual basis for imposition of sentence as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1(C). The court rejected these arguments. The court held that the victim's testimony and the factfinder's discretion in weighing credibility, together with the physical evidence introduced at trial, when viewed in the light most favorable to the prosecution, would allow a reasonable trier of fact to find guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. Further, the sentence pronounced by the trial court was proportional to the seriousness of the offenses and the offender's criminal history.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Bryant v. Heritage Life Ins. Co.


No. 92-149


COURT OF APPEALS OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


613 So. 2d 1044; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 382



February 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Twelfth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Michael J. Johnson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insureds appealed from a judgment of the Twelfth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana), which rendered summary judgment in favor of defendant bank in the insured's action for damages in which it alleged that the bank failed to acquire adequate credit disability insurance as requested by the insureds.


OVERVIEW: The insureds secured a loan and home mortgage from the bank. They alleged that they asked the bank to obtain policies of credit disability insurance on their behalf, naming the bank as beneficiary of the policy. They claimed that they paid $ 3,000 in premiums for the insurance. One of the insured became disabled, and the insurance company made mortgage payments for approximately one year. A year after the insurance company stopped making payments, the law governing such payments was enacted, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 6:1124. The statute provided, inter alia, that it applied retroactively. The insureds brought this action, and the trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the bank. On review, the court held that in this particular case, the statute did not apply retroactively because the rights of the insureds vested under the contract a year before the legislation became effective. The insureds also filed suit against the insurance carrier, but it was not a party to the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that granted summary judgment to the bank and remanded the matter for further proceedings. The court ordered the bank to bay the costs of the appeal.

Hillman v. Akins


No. 92-407, CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 92-408, CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 92-409, CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 91-700, CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 91-644, CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 91-1208, CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 91-1210

614 So. 2d 234; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 435



February 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court; Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana; Honorable Gregory D. Lyons, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patients challenged a judgment of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court; Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana) which granted defendant physician's peremptory exception of prescription in their actions for damages sustained as a result of a spinal implant, designed to enhance the chance of a solid fusion.


OVERVIEW: The patients brought suit against the physicians for damages arising out of the implantation of devices designed to facilitate spinal fusion. The suit was filed more than three years after the implantations, and the physicians filed peremptory exceptions of prescription under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 , which the trial court granted. The plaintiffs appealed, contending that the claims were not prescribed because they were treated on an ongoing basis, thus tolling the prescriptive period. On appeal, the court held that the plaintiffs' actions were based in malpractice arising out of the implantations, and therefore the prescriptive period began to run from the date of implantation. The court held that because the plaintiffs could not show any tolling period, the claims had prescribed, and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

931 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


No. CR92-355


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


614 So. 2d 270; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 440



February 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Concordia, State of Louisiana; Hon. Leo Boothe, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mayor appealed a decision of the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Concordia (Louisiana), which convicted him of one count of malfeasance in office, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:134, and sentenced him to four years at hard labor, two years suspended, placed him on active supervised probation for five years, fined him, and ordered him to pay restitution.


OVERVIEW: The mayor was found guilty of malfeasance in office. He alleged that the evidence had not supported a finding of guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:404 imposed a duty on all mayors to administer in conformity with the ordinances adopted by the board of aldermen. This was an affirmative duty, a violation of which could have constituted the crime of malfeasance in office. Looking at all of the evidence, a reasonable trier of fact could find the mayor knew that payment of accrued annual leave and sick leave was in violation of ordinances. Therefore, his actions not in conformity with the statute breached his duty and constituted malfeasance. As for the mayor's claim that the indictment was fatally defective, the omission of "sacramental language" was a defect of form only and was cured by amendment before trial. Although the indictment was not dated as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 462, the filing dates of the original and amended indictments were noted on both indictments. As for the mayor's argument that the amended indictment was defective as not signed by the jury foreman, no requirement mandated his signature on an amendment of this nature.


OUTCOME: The mayor's conviction and sentence on one count of malfeasance in office was affirmed. The case was remanded for determination of whether a motion to sever was granted and, if not, for a proper disposition of the remaining charges.

Fuge v. Uiterwyk

Chamberlain v. State


CA 91 1942


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


621 So. 2d 1118; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 2441



January 20, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 23, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF TERREBONNE, NO. 88836, HONORABLE PAUL R. WIMBISH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment from the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), entered judgment against the State in a personal injury suit filed by appellee survivors and awarded damages of more than $ 3 million, but were limited the amount of general damages to $ 500,000.


OVERVIEW: The minor child nearly drowned and suffered severe brain damage as a result of an accident near the State's fender system. The parents, individually and on behalf of their son, filed a personal injury action against the State claiming the electrical system on the fender, under the control of the State, was defective, causing electrical currents to leak into the water. The trial court awarded the victim $ 3,453,781.42 in special damages for past and future medical care and loss of earning capacity. With respect to general damages, the trial court held that his general damage claims, along with his parents' loss of consortium claims, constituted "one claim" and were subject to the $ 500,000 cap. The court found no manifest error in the trial court's conclusion that there was a light bulb in the southwest navigation lantern and that the parents' evidence established that wire to be the source of the leaking electrical current. The court determined that the cap on general damages was not unconstitutional because it was reasonably related to the legitimate state interests in providing compensation for tort victims and protecting the public welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the State in a personal injury action filed by the parents of a minor child who sustained severe injuries when he was electrocuted in a swimming accident and which limited the states' liability to $ 500,000.

City of New Orleans v. Board of Comm'rs


No. 92-CA-0148


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


612 So. 2d 318; 1993 La. App. LEXIS 33



January 14, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused February 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 91-18588, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE ROBERT A. KATZ, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the city, appealed from the Civil District Court, for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which maintained the Board of Commissioners of the Orleans Levee District's exception of no cause of action, and dismissed the city's petition for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The City, through its Department of Safety and Permits and the City Planning Commission commenced the action for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief.The City alleged that the Board was in the process of developing a marina, and that an ordinance mandated City approval for marinas and developments. The City appealed the trial court decision maintaining the Board's exception of no cause of action and dismissing the City's petition for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court and held that the provisions of the City's Home Rule Charter did not empower the City to require the Board to comply with the City's zoning regulations in the construction and development of the marina. The court held that the municipal zoning ordinances could not control the state's use of its property when it is performing a governmental function. Thus, the marina was properly considered a governmental project.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court in favor of the Board was affirmed.

Hawkins v. State


NUMBER CA 91 2079


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


613 So. 2d 229; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 4243



December 23, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended on Grant of Rehearing March 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 355,494, DIVISION "M"), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE JOSEPH F. KEOGH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Louisiana, through the Department of Health and Hospitals, challenged a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which had ruled in favor of the State, a former employee of appellant, in her action to recover wages, penalties, and attorney's fees under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:631 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The former civil employee sued the State for unpaid wages, penalty wages, and attorney's fees, following her discharge. The State had failed to inform the employee that her term of employment had ended, and she was inadvertently allowed to work hours at no pay. The trial court denied the State's exception of lack of jurisdiction over the subject matter. The sole issue on appeal was whether the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction to render a money judgment in favor of the employee pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:631 et seq. Because her cause of action for unpaid wages, penalty wages, and attorney's fees did not arise until after her discharge, the court held find that it was not an employment related matter subject to the exclusive authority of the State Civil Service Commission. The Commission had no authority to adjudicate this type of dispute. Constitutional provisions, which delegated judicial authority to the Commission, were narrowly construed since they represent exceptions to the general rule that district courts have jurisdiction over all civil matters under La. Const. art. V, § 16(A).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the employee in her action against the State to recover pay.

Salter v. State


No. CA 91 2081


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


612 So. 2d 163; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 4254



December 23, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 28, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF TANGIPAHOA, SUIT NO. 82450, HONORABLE KENNETH J. FOGG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state appealed an order of the 21st Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Tangipahoa (Louisiana), which entered judgment for plaintiff patient and ordered the state to pay pre-judgment interest in excess of six percent.


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, judgment was rendered in favor of the patient in his suit to recover damages for injuries received while he was being treated at a state hospital. The trial court ordered that the state pay pre-judgment interest at the prevailing legal rate, rather than the six percent rate established by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5112(C). The trial court held that the state was not entitled to the statutory rate because it did not plead § 13:5112(C) as an affirmative defense. The court held that § 13:5112(C), as the more specific statute, applied over the general interest rate provided by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4203 and La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2924. The state was not required to plead that judgments against the state were limited by statute because legal interest was not an affirmative defense since it did not have the effect of defeating the suit on the merits. The court also held that § 13:5112(C) did not violate La. Const. art. XII, § 10 because the state retained the power to provide for the effect of a judgment, and interest was a natural effect of a judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for the patient and rendered judgment for the state.

Dufrene v. Moore


No. 92-CA-524


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


612 So. 2d 147; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 4033



December 16, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 17, 1993.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchasers appealed a judgment from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division F (Louisiana), which found for defendant sellers in plaintiffs' action in ejectment or to quiet title to real property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs purchased the property, but came delinquent in taxes in 1933. They redeemed it at a tax sale. The property again was sold for taxes two years later, this time to defendants, who went into possession. Fourteen years later, plaintiffs again paid the taxes that were due for 1933, the redemption statute having been declared unconstitutional in 1937, and received a redemption certificate. They filed suit in 1955, but this was dismissed in 1965. Plaintiffs did not further contest the ownership until 1980. In affirming the judgment for defendants, the court held that defendants had proved acquisitive prescription under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3475. The court held that defendants acted in good faith as bona fide purchasers in the tax sale, notwithstanding that their title was invalid. The court next held that defendants had had continuous, uninterrupted, peaceable, public, and unequivocal possession for 10 years, evidenced by their grants of leases and servitudes, and their payment of taxes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for defendants in plaintiffs' action to determine ownership of the property.

 

939 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Kenner v. Southeast Equip. Co.


92-CA-499


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


611 So. 2d 785; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 4046



December 16, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted January 20, 1993, Reported at 1993 La. App. LEXIS 55.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 327-284. HONORABLE HUBERT VONDENSTEIN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, company and individual, appealed a decision from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) granting a permanent injunction to plaintiff city to enjoin the expansion of a nonconforming use in an area zoned two-family residential.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from a decision granting an injunction to a city to enjoin the expansion of a nonconforming use by a company and individual, the court reversed and rendered the decision. The location was zoned two-family residential. The nature of the business was selling and leasing construction equipment. The company supplied contractors with equipment. The types of equipment supplied were backhoes, bulldozers, and large equipment. The company argued that it enjoyed an exception of a legal nonconforming use. The city argued that to do so, the business had to meet the same nonconforming use classification enjoyed by its two predecessors. The court considered whether the company's predecessor continued the light industrial use or whether it changed the use to the restrictive use of special industrial. The court held that a zoning ordinance, being in derogation of the rights of private ownership, had to be construed, when it was subject to more than one reasonable interpretation, according to the interpretation which allowed the least restricted use of the property. The company fell within the light industrial classification provided for in the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered the trial court decision. Judgment was rendered in favor of a company and an individual, dismissing a city's action seeking to enjoin the expansion of a nonconforming use.

Phelps v. Louisiana State Racing Com.


No. 92-CA-0046


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


611 So. 2d 739; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3847



December 15, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 90-18785, DIVISION "J". HONORABLE GEORGE C. CONNOLLY, JR., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Louisiana State Racing Commission sought review of a judgment from the Civil District court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which reversed the commission's decision to suspend the license of plaintiff horse trainer following a positive drug test.


OVERVIEW: The horse trainer asserted that the Human Drug Testing Rules of the Louisiana State Racing Commission were unconstitutional. The trial court ruled in favor of the horse trainer. In reversing, the court held that prior decisions had already found the rules to be constitutional. The horse trainer argued that the rules were not designed to promote safety and did not detect if the drug use occurred during the professional practice. The court found that the government did have a legitimate interest in protecting the integrity of the horse racing industry, along with ensuring its safety. The horse trainer also argued that the rules were arbitrary, with no written procedures, and gave unbridled discretion to the stewards to determine who to test. The court acknowledge that the Louisiana Supreme Court should revisit the constitutionality of the rules, particularly in light of the passage of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:1015, but found that under current caselaw, the rules were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that reversed the commission's decision to suspend the license of the horse trainer.

 

941 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Watson


No. CR 92-191


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


609 So. 2d 1198; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3788



December 9, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, the Honorable William L. McCleod, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which convicted him of distributing cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A)(1), adjudged him to be a second felony offender, and sentenced him to serve 15 years at hard labor, without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of distributing cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A)(1). The trial court sentenced defendant to serve 15 years at hard labor, without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence after it adjudged him to be a second felony offender. On appeal, defendant raised 29 errors, including 17 allegations of ineffective assistance of counsel against his attorneys. The trial court's judgment was affirmed on appeal. The court found no error in the trial court's determinations that the initial police report had not been altered and that the cocaine used as evidence had not been tampered with. The court also found no evidence, as contended by defendant, that defendant had been coerced or otherwise forced to abandon his right to testify at trial. The court found no error in the sentence handed out by the trial court because the sentence was within the allowable sentencing range and complied with the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. Finally, in addition to numerous other findings, the court found that defendant had failed to prove that his trial counsel had been ineffective in having failed to obtain potential testimony.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of distributing cocaine and sentenced him to serve 15 years at hard labor, without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence after it adjudged him to be a second felony offender, was affirmed.

 

942 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Albritton


No. 91-1335


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


610 So. 2d 209; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3811



December 9, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Thirty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson Davis, State of Louisiana; Honorable William N. Knight, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRM.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant claimants appealed a default judgment from the 31st Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson Davis, State of Louisiana, in favor of plaintiff State in the State's seizure and forfeiture action pursuant to the Seizure and Controlled Dangerous Substances Property Forfeiture Act of 1989, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2612.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped the claimants' vehicle for an expired license tag. The claimants' demeanor aroused suspicion, and the officer obtained permission to search the car. He found beepers, a small scale, and $ 5,530 in cash in one claimant's purse. A check revealed that the claimants had a history of drug-related offenses. The beepers and currency were seized. The district court struck the bond and answer filed by the claimants and the State obtained a default judgment. The district court had authority to strike the bond under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 5123 when it had no proof of the surety's solvency. The answer was then properly stricken under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2612(E). The claimants were not entitled to notice of same. They waived their argument that the forfeiture statute was unconstitutional because they failed to specifically plead such in the district court. The court found that there was sufficient probable cause under the totality of circumstances to justify the seizure as required under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2606(B). The claimants did not meet their burden to prove by a preponderance of evidence that the money came from an independent, non-drug-related source.


OUTCOME: The judgment ordering the forfeiture of the claimants' money and beepers was affirmed.

 

943 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Kniepp v. Shreveport


No. 24,216-CA, No. 24,217-CA, No. 24,218-CA (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


609 So. 2d 1163; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3733



December 2, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 14, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 347,441, 350,622, 356,427. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, III, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff store owners sought review of a judgment from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which was rendered in favor of defendant city because the acts or omissions of the police department were neither a legal cause nor a cause in face of their damages resulting from a neighborhood riot.


OVERVIEW: The stores instituted an action against the city for negligent acts and omissions by the police department at the scene of a homicide which allegedly triggered a neighborhood riot. The trial court found that the acts or omissions of the police department were neither a legal cause nor a cause in fact of the store owners' damages. The trial court further found that the police chief's decision to redeploy the officers to the perimeter of the crime scene was a discretionary act which rendered the city immune under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1. The court held that the trial court was neither clearly wrong, manifestly erroneous, nor in error as a matter of law. The court determined that the record supported the finding that the city's choices were reasonably related to a public policy-based governmental objective to protect life. The court determined that the chief made discretionary tactical decision, which he should have been able to make without worry about allegations of negligence and the city was immune under the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which was rendered in favor of the City because the acts or omissions of the police department were neither a legal cause nor a cause in face of the store owners' damages resulting from a neighborhood riot.

 

944 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brewster


No. 24,299-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


609 So. 2d 1094; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3750



December 2, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 14, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 91-F9275. Honorable Charles E. Joiner, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the sentence imposed by the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana) on his conviction of five counts of simple burglary of an inhabited dwelling, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.2.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced defendant to 12 years at hard labor on each of the five counts of burglary. The sentence on counts 1, 2, and 3 were to be served consecutively; counts 4 and 5 were to be served concurrently with each other and with the other three sentences. The first year of each sentence was without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence, as required by statute. Defendant appealed the sentences as unconstitutionally excessive. On appeal the court held that defendant's claim was not properly before the court due to defendant's failure to comply with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1, which provided that a defendant could file a motion to reconsider his sentence within 30 days following imposition of the sentence or within such longer period as the trial court might set at sentencing. Article 881.1(A)(2) required that the motion set forth the specific grounds on which the motion was based. Failure to make a motion for reconsideration at all, or failure to include a specific ground for the claim, precluded the State or defendant from raising an objection to the sentence or urging any ground not raised in the motion on appeal or review.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences on five counts of burglary were affirmed.

State v. Smith


No. 92-KA-1764


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


610 So. 2d 152; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3583



December 1, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Substituted December 3, 1992. Rehearing Refused January 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 352-083, SECTION "B". HONORABLE PATRICK G. QUINLAN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of purse snatching under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65.1 (1986), and which sentenced him as a second offender under the Louisiana Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 (1992), to 15 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: As a woman was walking home from a store, defendant pushed her to the ground, grabbed her purse, and ran. As a result, defendant was convicted of purse snatching under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65.1 (1986) and sentenced as a second offender under the Louisiana Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 (1992), to 15 years at hard labor. On appeal, the court noted that the victim positively identified defendant as her assailant. Under the criminal seriousness level of La. Sentencing Guidelines § 403(A), plus defendant's prior purse snatching history classification of "D," defendant's maximum sentence under the guidelines was 5 1/2 years, and the minimum sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:65.1 (1986) and 15:529.1 (1992) was 10 years. There were no aggravating circumstances. Thus, under La. Sentencing Guidelines § 309(B), defendant's maximum sentence had to be the minimum sentence of 10 years under the Louisiana Habitual Offender Law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted defendant of purse snatching, but vacated his sentence of 15 years at hard labor as a second offender under the Louisiana Habitual Offender Law. The court remanded the case for resentencing to a term not more than the 10 year minimum sentence under the Law.

Thompson v. Capital Steel Co.


No. CA 91 1619


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


621 So. 2d 1101; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 4362



November 25, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 4, 1993. Released for Publication June 23, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKER'S COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION, (NUMBER 90-01556), DISTRICT FIVE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE NORBERT RAYFORD, HEARING OFFICER PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a steel company and an insurance company, sought review of a judgment from the Office of Worker's Compensation Administration, District Five (Louisiana), which was rendered in favor of plaintiff employee, awarding him compensation benefits and medical expenses.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a disputed claim for compensation with the office of worker's compensation administration. The employee sought compensation benefits and medical expenses for an on-the-job injury to his right hand from an accident. The employer admitted that the accident occurred, but asserted as an affirmative defense that due to claimant's intoxication at the time of the accident that he was not entitled to compensation pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1081. The workmen's compensation hearing officer rendered judgment in favor of the employee and awarded him compensation benefits and medical expenses. The court held that the test results were inadmissible under the statute to prove the employee's use of a controlled substance at the time of the accident; thus, defendants were not entitled to the presumptions that would otherwise apply the statute. The court concluded that the hearing officer was not manifestly erroneous in concluding that the steel company and insurer failed to carry their burden of proving that the employee was intoxicated at the time of the accident, or that the use of marijuana by the employee resulted in intoxication causing the accident.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment of the hearing officer to reduce the award of the employee for disability benefits from $ 3,341.44 to $ 1,879.56. The judgment, as amended, was affirmed.

State v. Vining


No. 91-KA-2749


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


609 So. 2d 984; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3632



November 24, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 351-633. SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED; AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of carnal knowledge of a juvenile, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:80(A)(1), by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section J (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty and was convicted. On appeal defendant alleged that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:80(A)(1), carnal knowledge of a juvenile, was unconstitutional, and that the trial judge should have granted his motion to quash the bill of information because it excluded females and, therefore, discriminated on the basis of sex and violated the equal protection clauses of the United States and Louisiana Constitutions. On appeal the court held that the protection of young females from pregnancy, and from possible injury to their reproductive systems as well as lingering mental impairment, was a legitimate area of state concern justifying the gender classification involved in the statute. As such, the gender classification in the statute does not violate the Equal Protection Clauses in the Constitutions of the United States or Louisiana. The court also found that that portion of defendant's sentence imposing time in jail if he could not pay the court costs was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of carnal knowledge of a juvenile, but amended the sentence to delete that portion of the sentence which required time in jail if defendant could not pay the court cost.

State v. Knighten


No. 92-KA-0341


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


609 So. 2d 950; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3635



November 24, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 353-149. SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of illegal possession of a firearm, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1785. The sole assignment of error was the district court's denial of defendant's motion to quash the jury based on the prosecution's alleged discriminatory use of peremptory challenges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged Batson violations. The prosecutor used all six of her available peremptory challenges on African-Americans, after conversing directly with only one of the dismissed jurors. Upon objection, the prosecutor gave four reasons: (1) she is African-American, (2) some dismissed jurors were inattentive, (3) two had either criminal or civil arrest records, and (4) one served on a jury which rendered an acquittal. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that the defendant had established a prima facie Batson violation, requiring the State to provide race neutral explanations in rebuttal. The court found the prosecutor's reference to her heritage was merely an assertion of good faith, which alone did not suffice. The court noted that the defense had no notice of arrest records, and none were produced, and neither of venireperson dismissed for that reason expressed any resentment toward the State or police. The court also noted that two white venirepersons also served on acquitting juries, and were not rejected. The court thus found that for three peremptory challenges, the State did not meet its burden.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court judgment, which convicted defendant of illegal possession of a firearm, and remanded for a new trial.

State ex rel. Counterman v. Whitley


KW 92 0619


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


611 So. 2d 661; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3663



November 20, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 28, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NUMBER 10-82-151, HONORABLE MICHAEL R. ERWIN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: WRIT OF CERTIORARI DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applied for and was issued a writ of certiorari for review of a judgment from the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which denied his motion to extend the time limit for filing his application for post-conviction relief pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8. Petitioner also filed a writ of mandamus to obtain his transcribed court record.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted and sentenced in 1983. He filed an out-of-time appeal over a year later. The supreme court ultimately ordered the district court to treat the appeal as an application for post-conviction relief and to allow him more time to amend his application. The court amended petitioner's sentence but twice denied his application for writ of mandamus to compel production of transcribed court records. La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8 was then enacted, which limited the time for filing for post-conviction relief and allowed a one-year grace period for previously convicted felons to file for such relief. The district court denied petitioner's motion for extension as untimely. The court found that art. 930.8 was not an ex post facto law. It did not alter the definition of the crimes or increase petitioner's punishment. The legislature could shorten the statute of limitations to make application for relief where it provided a reasonable time for petitioner to bring his application. Promulgation of the law was deemed adequate notice to petitioner. Petitioner could seek production of the trial records under the Public Records Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:35.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's writ of certiorari was denied.

Airline Adult Video v. St. Charles Parish Council


No. 92-CA-462


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


609 So. 2d 320; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3618



November 12, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 18, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 39,208. DIVISION "E". HONORABLE JOEL T. CHAISSON, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a corporation, appealed from a decision of the Twenty-Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Charles (Louisiana), which dissolved a restraining order and declared that an ordinance concerning obscenity was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Parish of St. Charles adopted an ordinance that declared illegal the distribution of obscene video material. The corporation filed suit alleging that it was in the business of leasing certain videos which could be determined to be obscene under the terms of the ordinance. The petition alleged that the ordinance was unconstitutional because the specific designation of the relevant community standard from which to judge whether the material was obscene was that of St. Charles Parish. The court held that the reference to St. Charles Parish as the community standard by which to judge what was obscene was illegal and had to be removed from the ordinance. The declared purpose of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:106E was to promote uniform obscenity legislation throughout the state and proscribed ordinances which exceed its provisions. The subject ordinance did that, for by declaring with specificity that the standards of St. Charles Parish be applied, it exceeded the general standard of any contemporary community standards. The rest of the ordinance was proper and could be enforced.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision to dissolve the restraining order and its decision declaring an order concerning obscenity constitutional.

State v. Seventy-Seven Thousand Fourteen & No/100 etc.


No. 91-282


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


1992 La. App. LEXIS 3584



November 6, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication December 10, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, the Honorable William Polk, Judge, presiding.

Original Opinion of June 29, 1992, Reported at 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2066.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On an application for rehearing, plaintiff State sought review of the court's decision to reverse a judgment from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which held that the State established probable cause to forfeit defendant claimant's money pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2601 et seq. and that the claimant failed to establish by a preponderance of the evidence that the money was not subject to forfeiture.


OVERVIEW: The state police received information from a customs agent that the claimant would be arriving at the regional airport carrying narcotics or a large sum of money. When the claimant left the airport, a trooper stopped her for a traffic violation. The trooper found a large sum of money after the claimant consented to a search. Upon reconsideration, the court adhered to its original decision to reverse the trial court's judgment. The court concluded that the State did not meet its burden under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2601 et seq. to connect the claimant's money to illegal narcotics violations. The court found no evidence, direct or circumstantial, that connected the claimant to drug trafficking. The evidence connecting the money seized to drug trafficking was based upon the fact of the seizure, the claimant's previous trips out of town, and inferences and conclusions drawn by an expert witness. Although there was testimony that a drug detection dog gave a positive alert to the presence of drug residue, the State did not have the tote bag and money analyzed at a laboratory. The court found more reason to believe that the money was generated by prostitution than by drug trafficking.


OUTCOME: The court adhered to its original decision to reverse the trial court's judgment.

State v. Gachot


No. CR92-313


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Twelfth Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana), which convicted him upon a jury verdict of manslaughter in the shooting of his father and of second-degree murder in the shooting of his mother. OVERVIEW: Defendant was 15 years old when he shot his parents during the course of a family argument. On appeal the court rejected defendant's numerous claims of error. Ann. art. 651 such evidence was inadmissible because defendant failed to plead not guilty by reason of insanity. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for manslaughter and for second-degree murder.

 

953 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Trahan


No. CR92-353


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


607 So. 2d 1016; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3494



November 4, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 10, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Thirtieth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vernon, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Ted R. Broyles, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Thirtieth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vernon, State of Louisiana, which convicted him based upon a guilty plea to theft and simple escape and sentenced him to serve 37 months at hard labor. Defendant claimed that the sentence was unconstitutionally excessive and unduly harsh because the district court did not properly consider the guidelines.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the district court failed to properly consider the guidelines of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1. The court found that those sentencing guidelines were no longer in effect when defendant was sentenced on February 24, 1992. Instead, under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1, defendant had to make or file a motion to reconsider his sentence, based upon a specific ground such as excessiveness, within 30 days of its imposition, or he could not argue that ground or object to the sentence on appeal or review. Defendant had objected to the sentence at the sentencing hearing, but he had not filed a motion to reconsider his sentence. The record was prepared 30 days after sentencing, so he was precluded from raising the claim of excessiveness on appeal. La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1 was to become effective on January 1, 1992, or 30 days after the effective date of the sentencing guidelines, whichever was later. Under an emergency rule, the sentencing guidelines had become effective on January 1, 1992. Therefore, art. 881.1 became effective 30 days later on January 30, 1992, and defendant's assignment of error was not properly before the court on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal.

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section C (Louisiana), which convicted him of distribution of heroin, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966 and sentenced him to life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested as a result of an undercover police operation. At trial, two police officers both identified defendant as the man who sold the heroin to another officer. The court ruled that defendant had not received ineffective assistance of counsel because ineffectiveness claims which fell within the ambit of trial strategy did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of aggravated rape, aggravated kidnapping, and armed robbery, appealed the sentences imposed by the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which ordered defendant to serve 40 years at hard labor on the rape conviction, life imprisonment on the kidnapping conviction, and seven years at hard labor on the robbery conviction, but without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.

Ann. § 14:65B and needed to be vacated.

State v. Russell


No. 91-KA-2264


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


607 So. 2d 689; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2943



October 15, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 11, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 348-132, SECTION "C". HONORABLE JEROME M. WINSBERG, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgments of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section C (Louisiana), that convicted them of attempted simple robbery and simple robbery, arguing that the evidence was legally insufficient to sustain their convictions and that the sentences imposed by the trial court were excessive.


OVERVIEW: Disguised as police officers, defendants stopped the victims, conducted a search, and misappropriated money under the guise of searching the victims and the vehicle for drugs. They were charged with and convicted of attempted simple robbery and simple robbery. They appealed their convictions, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence and the sentence imposed. In affirming, the court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions where the defendants misrepresented themselves as police officers, ordered the victims from their vehicle, and used intimidation in attempting to take and actually taking valuables from the victims. The victims were clearly intimidated by the display of a badge, the threat of trouble, and a general demeanor and aura of authority. Further, the sentence imposed was not unconstitutionally excessive. Although one of the defendants had no prior record, he had an extensive arrest record, including a prior arrest for impersonating a police officer. Because the trial court determined that defendants would likely commit other offenses if not incarcerated, there was not error in concluding that a need existed for a corrective environment.


OUTCOME: The judgments of conviction and the sentences imposed were affirmed.

 

958 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


92-KA-441


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


606 So. 2d 586; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3032



October 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 17, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 90-5567. HONORABLE RONALD P. LOUMIET, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED AND AS AMENDED AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the 24th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, which convicted and sentenced him to a term of 15 years without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence for his conviction pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3 and 40:967 for distribution of cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of selling cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school. He contended that the definition of school property in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3 was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that § 40:981.3 was clearly and readily understandable, gave adequate notice of what conduct was proscribed, and provided adequate standards for determining the guilt or innocence of the accused. Any reasonable person could understand that § 40.981.3 proscribed trafficking controlled dangerous substances while on or within 1,000 feet of school property, and the statute's definition of school property clearly encompassed the school property involved in the case. The court also rejected defendant's contention that the statute was overbroad. Section 40:981.3 did not violate the equal protection clause by not making an exception for periods when school was not in session because the legislature had a legitimate goal of protecting school age children from the dangers of drugs and drug related crime and § 40:981.3 was rationally structured to effectuate that purpose. Section 40:981.3(E)(1) was not ambiguous. The court reduced defendant's sentence to give him credit for time served.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but amended his sentence to reflect credit for time served.

 

959 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anseman


No. 92-KA-243


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


607 So. 2d 665; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3038



October 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 17, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 90-3892, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE ROBERT J. BURNS, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, parents of a deceased child, appealed from judgments of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted them of manslaughter in connection with the death of their child under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31, and sentenced them to serve 21 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' 13-month old daughter died in of wasting and nutritional deprivation. Defendant mother had been entitled to receive government-provided health care services and food for the child, but did not avail herself of those services. Defendants were convicted of manslaughter under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31A(2)(a) for unintentionally causing the child's death while engaged in perpetrating a felony, and were sentenced to serve 21 years at hard labor. The court held that the predicate felony of cruelty to juveniles supported the convictions under § 14:31A(2)(a), and that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because any person of reasonable intelligence was able to understand it. The mother's motion to withdraw a plea of guilty, and to plead not guilty by reason of insanity, was properly denied as untimely. Accordingly, evidence relating to the mother's mental condition was properly excluded, as it was not relevant to the mother's defense, and could not relieve the father of his duty to see that his children were properly cared for. The evidence was sufficient to support the convictions, and the sentences were not illegally excessive considering the nature of the offense.


OUTCOME: The judgments convicting and sentencing defendants were affirmed.

State v. Hurst


No. CR92-21


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


606 So. 2d 965; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2824



October 6, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana; the Honorable John Rixie Mouton, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which had convicted him of aggravated rape of a nine-year-old girl in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42A(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in not permitting him to present certain witnesses and evidence in defense of the charge of aggravated rape; in allowing the State to lead witnesses, to present certain testimony; and the trial court's denying objections to testimony and in interrupting defendant's opening argument. On appeal the court held that evidence of intoxication and drug use to which defendant would have testified, had its introduction been allowed, was not a material fact and was properly excluded. The trial judge's failure to sustain defense objections did not constitute reversible error, and defendant showed no prejudice as a result of the trial court's ruling on his counsel's opening statement. The ruling, if incorrect, constituted harmless error. Defendant was convicted for aggravated rape under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42A(4). The degree of force was not a factor to be considered by the jury based on the fact that the victim was only nine years old.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated rape.

State v. Ristom


No. CR91-1283


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


607 So. 2d 655; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2831



October 6, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 16, 1992. Rehearing Refused November 11, 1992, Reported at 1992 La. App. LEXIS 3612.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF CALCASIEU, STATE OF LOUISIANA, BEFORE HONORABLE FRED R. GODWIN, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which had convicted him of vehicular homicide, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to a charge of vehicular homicide, reserving his right to seek review of pretrial motions. He contended that the trial court erred in its failure to grant his motion to suppress; its failure to grant the motion to quash; and in the excessiveness of his sentence. Defendant's blood alcohol level following a vehicle collision, where he was driving one vehicle, was in excess of the established level for intoxication. One person died in the accident. On appeal the court held that the trial court properly accepted the qualifications of the blood alcohol analyst. The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1 was constitutional. The fact it did not require the State to obtain two blood samples at separate time intervals to more accurately determine a defendant's blood alcohol level at the time defendant was operating the motor vehicle was not a violation of due process. Defendant's sentence was deemed by the court not to have been excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of vehicular homicide.

Youn v. Maritime Overseas Corp.


91-CA-407


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


605 So. 2d 187; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2377



July 27, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 19, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. JAMES - STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 19,400. HONORABLE JOHN L. GOLDSMITH.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED IN PART; SET ASIDE AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, ship operator and insurance company appealed the judgment of the Twenty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of St .James (Louisiana), which held that they were liable to plaintiff boatswain for an injury he received while working on a ship.


OVERVIEW: The boatswain was working on a ship when an accident occurred damaging his leg. The boatswain sued the ship operator and his insurance company under the Jones Act, 46 U.S.C.S. § 688, and unseaworthiness. The trial court found in favor of the boatswain, and an appeal was taken. The court held that the trial court correctly refused to hold a jury trial, because only the boatswain in an admiralty case could request trial by jury. The court also determined that the boatswain successfully proved that his injury was caused by the ship's unseaworthiness, and therefore he was entitled to recovery under negligence and the Jones Act, because the ship operator failed to properly train or supervise the ship employees. In addition, the court observed that the boatswain was entitled to future medical expenses, but prejudgment interest on the award was unavailable. Finally, the court concluded that the boatswain was not entitled to recovery for the amount of money that the ship operator would have spent on the boatswain if he actually lived on the ship, because he failed to present any loss. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded the matter for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the lower court, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Talley v. Succession of Stuckey


NUMBER 91-216


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


604 So. 2d 1375; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2294



July 8, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Martin, State of Louisiana, the Honorable C. Thomas Bievenu, Jr., District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the unmarried partner of a testator, appealed from a judgment of the 16th Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Martin, State of Louisiana, which denied her request to annul the testament based on the subsequent birth of an illegitimate child to the testator, pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1705. Article 1705 provided that a testament was revoked by the birth of an illegitimate child only under certain conditions.


OVERVIEW: The testator was divorced. He lived with his new partner after his divorce, but never married her. His partner gave birth to a child less than one year before the testator's death. In an olographic will, made 18 years before his death, the testator left a portion of his estate to his former wife. Following the testator's death, a court order recognized the testator as the father of the partner's son. In her action seeking to annul the testament, the partner contended that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1705 was unconstitutional because it provided that a testament was revoked by the subsequent birth of a legitimate child but did not provide revocation by the subsequent birth of an illegitimate child, except on certain conditions. On appeal, the court noted that classifications based on illegitimacy were not suspect. The court found that the classification based on illegitimacy was based on a legitimate state interest because the difficulty in proof of legitimacy constituted a permissible state interest. Therefore, the court concluded that the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court and assessed all costs of the appeal to the partner.

Reed v. St. Charles General Hosp.


No. 89-CA-1754 c/w, No. 91-CA-0114 c/w, No. 91-CA-1080 and No. 91-C-2533


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


602 So. 2d 784; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2068



July 1, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 3, 1992.
Writ granted by, in part, Writ denied by, in part, Remanded by Reed v. St. Charles Gen. Hosp., 815 So. 2d 319, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1386 (La.App. 4 Cir., Mar. 27, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS NO. 88-18141, HONORABLE RICHARD J. GARVEY, JUDGE, DIVISION "C" HONORABLE ROBIN GIARRUSSO, JUDGE, DIVISION "G".
Reed v. St. Charles General Hosp., 556 So. 2d 21, 1990 La. LEXIS 13 (La., 1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a husband and wife, appealed an order of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, (Louisiana), which granted an exception filed by defendant hospital and denied the wife's request for a hearing on a motion for new trial. The case was a medical malpractice action against defendants, the hospital, a blood center, an insurer, and a laboratory. The husband contracted AIDS through a blood transfusion. The wife also contracted AIDS.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife filed a medical malpractice action against defendants after the husband contracted AIDS from a blood transfusion and later transmitted it to the wife. The husband subsequently died. The district court granted an exception of prescription filed by the hospital. The wife filed a motion for new trial, requested a Sibley hearing, and argued that the district court had granted the exception without allowing her an opportunity to amend her petition. The district court denied the motion and issued an amended judgment maintaining the exception of prescription. The wife appealed and argued the constitutionality of the statute of limitations. The court vacated the amended judgement because a substantive change was made, and it reversed the original judgment because it did not give the wife time to amend. The court held that the district court erred in failing to rule on the constitutional issue and in failing to hold an evidentiary hearing as requested by the wife. The court also set aside an order which granted an exception filed by the laboratory, based on the rulings related to the other judgments.


OUTCOME: The court vacated a judgment of the trial court which granted an exception filed by the hospital in the medical malpractice action filed by the husband and wife. The court also held that the trial court erred in failing to hold an evidentiary hearing on the wife's motion for a new trial. The case was remanded.

State v. Florant


No. 91-KA-2332


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


602 So. 2d 338; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2031



June 30, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 11, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 339-232, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section F (Louisiana), that convicted him of simple robbery, arguing that the State failed to prove that he was guilty of simple robbery beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: A tourist felt pressured into permitting the persistent defendant to shine his shoes. The tourist handed the defendant a $ 20 dollar bill and asked for change, at which point the defendant laughed, took the bill, and informed the tourist that he had been "had." The tourist filed a complaint with police, indicating that he had been defrauded and intimidated by the defendant. Defendant was charged with and convicted of simple robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65. He appealed his conviction and sentence, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence. In reversing, the court concluded that the defendant was not guilty of simple robbery, and the appropriate charge was theft of property, which was not a responsive verdict to simple robbery. The defendant engaged in no force or intimidation, which was necessary for a robbery conviction, and the court rejected the State's argument that a victim could be intimidated by a look in a perpetrator's eye. While the defendant cheated and defrauded the tourist, he did not commit simple robbery.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were reversed.
