Convent Marine Cos. v. State


No. 91 CA 0968


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


603 So. 2d 790; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2309



June 29, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 10, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NO. 359,506), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE ROBERT D. DOWNING, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which overruled its exception and rendered judgment in favor of appellee taxpayer in the taxpayer's suit to recover sales taxes which it paid to the State voluntarily and without protest.


OVERVIEW: The basis of the State's exception was that the taxpayer failed to pay the tax under protest and failed to follow payment with a timely suit for a refund. The taxpayer claimed that it had a right of action under the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1481 et seq. and under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2301 et seq. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, finding that under the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1576, a pre-requisite to the taxpayer's exercise of access to the trial court was that the taxpayer had paid under protest. The court found that the taxpayer, who paid without protest and whose claim was rejected by the Board of Tax Appeals for the State of Louisiana, had exhausted his remedies, was barred by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1846 from appealing the rejection, and was barred from a trial de novo by his own failure to satisfy the requisites of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1576. Further, the court rejected the taxpayer's claim of right of action under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2301 et seq., finding that the cited articles did not apply to a claim by a taxpayer against a taxing authority for a refund. The court dismissed the taxpayer's suit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that overruled the State's exception to the taxpayer's suit for a tax refund. The court dismissed the taxpayer's suit.

Morgan City v. Louisiana Dep't of Environmental Quality


91 CA 0531


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


604 So. 2d 144; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2317



June 29, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, SUIT NUMBER 310,377, THE HONORABLE DOUGLAS GONZALES, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant-sponsor police juries sought review of a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), that was made in favor of appellant-opponents, a mayor and a parish council, by reversing a water-quality certification issued by appellee Louisiana Department of Environmental Quality. The trial court found that the Department had failed to follow the procedure imposed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:957.


OVERVIEW: The parish police juries applied, and the Department issued a water-quality certification for a watershed project. The Department's secretary denied any requested post-issuance relief, and the mayor and parish council sought review in the trial court, which reversed the certification. On appeal, the court found that the reversal was based on La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:957, which required that as the assistant secretary that issued the certification did not hear the case or read the record, the parties had to be served with a proposed order, and the opportunity had to be afforded to adversely affected parties to respond to the proposed order; this was not done. Based on the facts, the court found that § 49:957 mandated that the proposed order be served and that the police juries, the mayor, and the parish council be given the opportunity to file exceptions, submit briefs, and make oral argument to the assistant secretary before he made his decision. The court also ruled that the hearing officer's apparent consideration- -no matter how minimal- -of aerial-survey information was erroneous because the record showed that no aerial-survey information had been admitted into evidence.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the mayor and parish council and against the police juries, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment that reversed the issuance of the water-quality certificate and remanded the matter to the Louisiana Department of Environmental Quality. The court assessed costs against the police juries.

Francis v. Accardo


CA 91 0574


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


602 So. 2d 1066; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2318



June 29, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 27, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 85,885), PARISH OF ST. MARY, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE ROBERT M. FLEMING, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor sought review of a judgment from the 16th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Mary (Louisiana), which ordered the doctor to comply with a subpoena for testimony and production of business records issued by plaintiff, the Administrator of the Office of Employment and Training, Louisiana Department of Labor (Department), pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1660.


OVERVIEW: The Department issued a subpoena to the doctor, an individual employer, for testimony and the production of business records. The doctor refused to comply and the Department obtained an order from the trial court compelling him to comply. On appeal, the doctor did not argue that he was not an "employing unit" subject to the Louisiana Employment Security Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1471 et seq. Rather, he argued that the routine practice of random audits by the Department of individual citizens' private papers violated U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court affirmed the judgment ordering him to comply with the administrative subpoena and held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1660 could be constitutionally applied to an unincorporated individual. The records required to be kept pursuant to § 23:1660 had a public aspect for purposes of constitutional analysis and were not private papers entitled to the protection of U.S. Const. amends. IV and V. The doctor did not allege that the Department had proceeded without lawful authority or that it abusively or oppressively exerted its subpoena power. Therefore, there was no defect in the Department's exercise of its subpoena power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment ordering the doctor to comply with the administrative subpoena.

Hackney v. G.T. Contractor


No. 23,687-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


602 So. 2d 268; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1971



June 24, 1992, Rendered

State v. Gilmer


No. 23,926-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


604 So. 2d 117; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1963



June 24, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 20, 1992.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Gilmer v. Carmouche, 661 So. 2d 463, 1995 La. LEXIS 2236 (La., Oct. 6, 1995)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Gilmer v. State, 694 So. 2d 235, 1997 La. LEXIS 1853 (La., May 30, 1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Gilmer v. State, 920 So. 2d 224, 2006 La. LEXIS 178 (La., Jan. 13, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Gilmer v. State, 938 So. 2d 73, 2006 La. LEXIS 2807 (La., Oct. 6, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex.rel Gilmer v. State, 83 So. 3d 1035, 2012 La. LEXIS 513 (La., 2012)
Related proceeding at Gilmer v. La. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr., 2015 La. App. LEXIS 1735 (La.App. 1 Cir., Sept. 18, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 152,394. Honorable Scott Crighton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him for armed robbery and aggravated burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for armed robbery and aggravated burglary. The court affirmed defendant's convictions. The trial court properly required defendant to reveal his gold tooth to the jury because the victim described her assailants, specifically testified as to the gold tooth, but failed to positively identify defendant. Thus, the evidence was admissible under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 401, 402 because defendant's identity was a fact of consequence and whether he had a gold tooth was relevant to the identity issue. Furthermore, requiring a defendant to exhibit identifying characteristics was demonstrative evidence and not violative of the Fifth Amendment right against compulsory self-incrimination. Defendant's sentence was not excessive because the trial court adequately articulated the factors that it considered in imposing the sentence under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1. The trial court considered defendant's prior felony convictions and acts that involved guns and violence, his young age, the fact that he came from a broken home, and that because of financial difficulty his family was forced to live in a high crime area.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for armed robbery and aggravated burglary.

State v. Hookfin

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 322-358, SECTION "A". HONORABLE MIRIAM G. WALTZER, JUDGE.
State v. Hoofkin, 596 So. 2d 536, 1992 La. LEXIS 1446 (La., 1992)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of obstruction of justice in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:130.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of obstruction of justice under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:130.1 and appealed. The state supreme court remanded the matter to the court to examine the constitutionality of § 14:130.1. Defendant asserted the phraseology that the crime of obstruction of justice is any of the following when committed with the knowledge that such act has, reasonably may, or will affect an actual or potential present, past, or future criminal proceeding was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that a statute was unconstitutionally vague if it did not give individual adequate notice that certain conduct was proscribed and punishable by law, and if it did not provide adequate standards for those charged with determining the accused's guilt or innocence. Here, defendant claimed the term "affect" was vague because it presumed an adverse effect and was not modified by the necessary adverbs to clarify the statute's intent. That argument construed "affect" out of context however, and overlooked the fact that the statute required that an offender act with the specific intent of distorting the results of any criminal investigation or proceeding. The defendant's conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

973 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Kenner v. New Orleans Aviation Bd.


No. 92-CA-82, c/w No. 92-CA-83


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


603 So. 2d 220; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1792



May 26, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 422-394 C/W 422-469, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE ERNEST V. RICHARDS



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant aviation board sought review of a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, Division B, which granted a preliminary injunction in favor of plaintiffs, a city and two rental car companies, restraining, enjoining, and prohibiting the board from enforcing a permit agreement and prohibiting the board from denying certain access to an airport.


OVERVIEW: The board operated an airport and the rental car companies, which were located off-site, picked up customers at the airport. The board adopted a resolution requiring off-site rental car companies to pay a privilege fee for the privilege of access to the airport to conduct business at the airport. The city filed a declaratory judgment action, which was joined by the rental car companies, alleging that the privilege fee imposed by board was an unconstitutional, illegal, invalid, and unenforceable tax. The trial court granted the preliminary injunction and the board sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the permit fee agreement clearly violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 2:605D because § 2:605D only permitted imposition of a fee that was fair, reasonable, and not unjustly discriminatory. The court found that § 2:065D specifically forbid the fees from having the effect of substantially lessening competition and mandated that the fees be based on cost to the airport of the particular facilities or services used by the offsite companies. The court held that a municipality was without authority to enact ordinances that were inconsistent with state law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Hodges Ward Purrington Properties v. Lee


No. 92-CA-117, C/W 92-CA-118


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


601 So. 2d 358; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1801



May 26, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. DIVISION "G". NO. 422-183 C/W 423-421. THE HONORABLE M. JOSEPH TIEMANN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant purchaser sought review of an order from the 24th Judicial District Court, Division G, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which ordered the sheriff to accept a certain sum owed by plaintiff property owner necessary to redeem as of the date of tender and to execute a certificate of redemption on the property.


OVERVIEW: The purchaser bought title to the property at a tax sale when the property owner failed to pay the property taxes. The purchaser refused to accept the amount of taxes owed on the property from the property owner. The property owner and the mortgage holder sought the redemption of the property. The court found that the mortgage holder made no claim that it notified the tax collector of its mortgage as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180.1A. Therefore, the mortgage holder had not met the burden of proof that the sale was invalid for failure to afford proper notice to the mortgage holder pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180.1. The court also found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180.1B(2) prohibited annulment of a tax sale due to lack of notice to the mortgagee. Because the trial court decided incorrectly that the tax sale was invalid ab initio, the record contained insufficient evidence on the matter of redemption and the monetary amount necessary for redemption for the court's review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which found the tax sale was invalid ab initio.

Ann. §§ 40:964, 40:967 F. The trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent sentences of 12 years at hard labor. State v. Shillow


No. CR91-1090


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


602 So. 2d 28; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1522



May 20, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline, State of Louisiana; Honorable Preston N. Aucoin, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of his conviction and sentence from the 13th Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana). A bill of information charged him with, inter alia, two counts of distribution of cocaine within 1000 feet of a school in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:967A(1), 40:981.3. He was tried by a jury for one count of distribution of cocaine within 1000 feet of a school and was found guilty.


OVERVIEW: The transaction occurred after school hours. One of the officers present testified that it was about 7:45 p.m., that it was dark outside, and that only adults were present. However, the evidence was clear that defendant distributed cocaine outside in a parking lot. The court affirmed the judgment of his conviction and sentence. In response to the challenge raised by defendant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3, the court opined that the application of the statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad. Further, the court found that the state proved beyond a reasonable doubt the existence and location of the school zone, and that the transactions occurred within 1000 feet of the school property. The court found that such question was for the jury to decide, and that the jury was free to believe the civil engineering expert, who testified as to his opinion of the official boundary of the school property. Finally, from the testimony of the officers who purchased the drug and transported it to the crime lab, and the chemist who analyzed and identified the cocaine, the state established the chain of custody of the alleged crack cocaine beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for distribution of cocaine within 1000 feet of a school.

State v. Stills


No. 23,805-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


600 So. 2d 134; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1375



May 13, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 18, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 151,745. Honorable James Stewart, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the 1st Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), convicting defendant of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. Defendant was sentenced to an eight-year term of hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for possession of a firearm by convicted felon asserting that he was entitled to mistrial, that certain evidence was improperly admitted, and that his sentence was excessive. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence. First, the court held that references by witnesses to evidence that was previously suppressed or that was extraneous and unnecessary did not necessarily give rise to such prejudice that a mistrial was mandated. The court held that the minute entry was admissible to prove defendant's prior conviction. The portion of the minute which mentioned a firearm was extraneous but did not cause such prejudice to require a mistrial. Second, the court held that the trial court had great discretion in determining whether the state established a proper chain of custody and that the trial court's finding was not an abuse of discretion. Third, the court held that the trial court's sentence of eight years at hard labor was within the statutory limits for the crime. The trial court evaluated the evidence and circumstances and found it logical that the gun was used in furtherance of selling illegal drugs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a firearm by a convicted felon and defendant's eight year sentence of hard labor.

 

979 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wigley


No. K-91-526


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


599 So. 2d 858; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1540



May 4, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR SUPERVISORY WRITS FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF CALCASIEU, STATE OF LOUISIANA, BEFORE HONORABLE ARTHUR J. PLANCHARD, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This case was before the court by writ of certiorari on remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court. The writ application concerned the request for payment of reasonable attorney's fees and expenses filed by relator attorneys, who were appointed to represent indigent defendants charged with murder. During the criminal prosecution, motions for payment of compensation and expenses were filed. The writ arose from the denial of the payment request.


OVERVIEW: This case turned on the violation of the attorneys' rights to substantive due process, which protected against an oppressive interpretation of the law and which was, in many ways, similar to the La. Const. art. I, § 4 "taking" clause. The court appointments, from a non-voluntary list, to defend a person charged with a capital offense without compensation was, in itself, onerous and oppressive. Given the extreme nature of the burden of a capital case appointment, it was unrealistic to conclude otherwise. Involvement in a capital case required the attorney to forego profitable employment. The attorneys' involvement directly and adversely impacted on the attorneys' financial resources. Furthermore, a capital case placed the most demands on the attorneys' skills and time. Although there was no evidence as to the total number of hours devoted to the case, the guilty pleas were not accepted until a significant time after appointment. Therefore, not compensating the attorneys constituted an abusive extension of their professional obligations, so the Indigent Defender Board was ordered to compensate them for the maximum amount paid to appointed voluntary attorneys.


OUTCOME: The district court's denial of the motion for reasonable compensation was reversed. It was ordered that the Indigent Defender Board pay the attorneys the maximum amount allowable according to law.

Ellis v. Louisiana Ins. Guaranty Ass'n


No. 90-942


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


606 So. 2d 800; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1098



April 16, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] On Rehearing June 16, 1992, Reported at 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1823.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the City Court, Alexandria Ward, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana; Hon. Edward E. Roberts, Jr., City Court Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action filed by plaintiff against defendant Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA) seeking a declaration of the validity of a consent judgment, the City Court, Alexandria Ward, Rapides Parish, Louisiana, held the judgment was valid and enforceable. The trial court made an alternative ruling that if its ruling was reversed, then the statute under which LIGA had proceeded was unconstitutional. LIGA appealed.


OVERVIEW: LIGA, which chose to contest the consent judgment, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1382(A)(4), alleged that: (1) the settlement was not authorized by an insurer, and (2) the settlement was excessive and not supported by medical evidence. The trial judge maintained plaintiff's exception of no cause of action, but overruled her exception of res judicata. The instant court concluded that the allegations asserted by LIGA, even if true, did not constitute grounds for nullity. Thus, the trial court correctly maintained plaintiff's exception of no cause of action. Regarding the constitutionality of § 22:1382(A)(4), the instant court observed that LIGA could not simply refuse to pay a judgment upon its own unilateral review of the settlement or release upon which a judgment was based. The statute did not grant LIGA that right. Because the operation of § 22:1382(A)(4) did not deprive plaintiff of her property without due process of law, the statute did not violate the due process clause of the United States or Louisiana Constitutions. Judgment in favor of plaintiff was premature.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case was remanded for a full trial on the merits. The instant court affirmed the trial court's decision maintaining plaintiff's exception of no cause of action. However, the trial court erred in finding the statute unconstitutional. Costs of the appeal were to be paid by LIGA to the extent allowed by law.

Wicker v. Wicker


NUMBER 90-1177


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


597 So. 2d 1273; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1132



April 16, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Alfred Mansour, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant former husband appealed from a judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, which was entered on plaintiff former wife's rule to show cause seeking permanent alimony. The trial court held that there was jurisdiction over the husband, who was living in Florida when the rule was filed, since service of process was made pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3201A(6).


OVERVIEW: The wife obtained a divorce from the husband on the grounds of his adultery. The trial judge found that the wife was free of fault in awarding her alimony. The husband contended that the trial court did not have personal jurisdiction over him and erred in allowing evidence of fault in the hearing on the rule. In affirming the judgment, the court held the state had sufficient minimum contacts with the husband to establish jurisdiction over him for the purpose of awarding alimony pursuant to § 13:3201A(6) because he formerly resided in the state with the wife. The court further held that the trial court was correct in awarding alimony to the wife. The court stated that the husband could raise the issue of the wife's fault at the hearing on the rule even though he filed no answer asserting fault on her part as an affirmative defense. After a review of the record, including the husband's proffer of proof, the court found that there was no evidence in the record of fault on the wife's part that would preclude her from receiving permanent alimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment awarding the wife permanent alimony.

State v. Carson


No. 90-KA-1974


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


598 So. 2d 576; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1059



April 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 341-106, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted her of cruelty to a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:93, and which sentenced her to 10 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sent her 10-year-old daughter out to obtain cigarettes for defendant and then beat her daughter when her daughter returned home without any cigarettes. As a result, defendant was convicted of cruelty to a juvenile under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:93 and was sentenced to the maximum term of 10 years at hard labor. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the trial court properly particularized the factors in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 984.1 to defendant. The daughter's eye was bleeding as a result of her beating, and the daughter had multiple healing wounds and scars on her back and extremities. Thus, the evidence supported the conviction and the sentence was not excessive. Pursuant to La. Code Evid. arts. 607(C) and 403, the trial court properly limited defendant's right under La. Code Evid. 611(B) to cross-examine the daughter about her hospitalization after a car accident, where the probative value of the questions was substantially outweighed by the danger of prejudice and confusion. Therefore, the judgment was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted defendant of cruelty to a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:93, and which sentenced her to 10 years at hard labor.

State v. Montgomery


No. 90-KA-0507


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


598 So. 2d 553; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1113



April 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 299-455, SECTION "F", HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED, AND AFFIRMED AS AMENDED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of attempted simple burglary, and which sentenced him under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 as a second offender to 12 years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, suspension of sentence, or good time.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's fingerprints were found on an office safe that had been pried open and paper towels with defendant's blood type were found in the office. As a result, defendant was convicted of attempted simple burglary and sentenced as a habitual offender to 12 years at hard labor without benefit of probation, suspension of sentence, parole, or good time. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction but modified the sentence to allow defendant the benefit of parole and good time. Defendant's counsel was not ineffective for not filing a motion to suppress the evidence taken from the office, because under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 703, only unconstitutionally seized evidence could be suppressed. Under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 806, the trial court properly declined to instruct the jury on whether defendant was left or right handed, because the issue was a fact of the case. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 did not prohibit parole, and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.3 permitted defendant to earn good time. Therefore the judgment was proper, but the sentence had to be amended to allow parole and good time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted defendant of attempted simple burglary, and which sentenced him as a habitual offender to 12 years at hard labor without probation or suspension of sentence. The court modified the sentence to allow defendant the benefit of parole and good time.

State v. McHugh


No. KW 91 0664


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


598 So. 2d 1171; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1211



April 10, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF ST. MARY, DOCKET NUMBERS 130,419; 130,424; 130,504; 130,421; 130,418; 130,428; HON. RICHARD T. HAIK, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF DISTRICT COURT IS REVERSED AND MOTIONS TO SUPPRESS ARE GRANTED. CASES ARE REMANDED TO THE DISTRICT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On a writ of certiorari to the court, defendants sought review of the ruling of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Mary (Louisiana), which denied defendants' motions to suppress the evidence and statements relating to the charges of possession of untagged deer meat, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:125(B).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were traveling in two boats on the Intracoastal Waterway when an agent of the Department of Wildlife and Fisheries stopped them. Agents of the department were conducting game violation and boat safety checks in that location. The agent recognized one of the defendants as someone he knew had past hunting violations. The agent saw a buck head in the boat, and a fully dressed and quartered deer that had not been tagged. Defendants were charged with possession of untagged deer meat, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:125(B). After hearing testimony, the trial court denied defendants' motions to suppress evidence and statements and they sought review on a writ of certiorari. The court reversed the denial of the motions to suppress, holding that the stop of defendants' boats was conducted illegally under the La. Const., art. I, § v. The court concluded that reasonable suspicion did not support the stop and that the limitations on sobriety roadblocks were also applicable to the State's random stops for game violation checks. The illegality of the initial stop required suppression of the resulting evidence and statements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of defendants' motions to suppress evidence and statements related to the possession of untagged deer meat.

State v. Batchelor


CA 91 0169


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


597 So. 2d 1132; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1219



April 10, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY, NO. 8913509 A, HONORABLE FRANCE W. WATTS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual, on behalf of herself and her minor child, sought review of the judgment from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which nullified a support judgment on the reasoning that the judgment had been obtained by "fraud and ill practices."


OVERVIEW: Appellant brought suit which for paternity and child support against a third party. The third party admitted paternity and the parties entered into a consent judgment which awarded appellant $ 420,000 for past, present and future support of the child. While the child support/paternity action was ongoing, appellee State was proceeding against the third party for violations of the drug racketeering act. The State obtained a writ of seizure and while attempting to execute it, the State learned appellant had seized some assets under the support judgment. The trial court declared the support judgment null and void. The court noted that appellant and the third party lived together and during that time appellant was the bookkeeper for the third party's company. Appellant was aware of the drug activities and benefited from them. The court noted that the lump sum figure of $ 2,000 per month was for a child who was not yet 2 years old at the time of the filing of the suit, and was an excessive amount under ordinary circumstances. The trial court did not abuse its great discretion when it concluded that the support judgment was rendered through "fraud or ill practice."


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which held that a child support judgment was null and void because it was obtained through fraud or ill practice, was affirmed.

State v. Flowers


No. 91 KA 0051


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


598 So. 2d 1144; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1220



April 10, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NO. 8-74-3005), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE J. MICHAEL MCDONALD, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED, CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which granted his motion for post-conviction relief from an illegally lenient sentence and resentenced him to 45 years at hard labor with credit for time served and without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to 45 years' imprisonment at hard labor, with credit for time served, for armed robbery. The trial court granted defendant's post-conviction motion to correct an illegally lenient sentence and resentenced him to 45 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence and with credit for time served. Defendant appealed. The court held that, absent an allegation of prejudice, defendant was not denied the right to the assistance of counsel under La. Const. art. I, § 13, because counsel was appointed to represent him at resentencing. The court held that the correction of the sentence was not unconstitutional or unfair, particularly because defendant raised the issue that his sentence was illegally lenient. However, the court vacated and remanded the matter for resentencing because the record did not reflect that the resentencing judge considered whether the original sentencing judge intended to allow parole eligibility.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's corrected sentence and remanded the case to the district court for resentencing.

In re American Waste & Pollution Control Co., etc.


CA 89 0906-R, CA 90 1398


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


597 So. 2d 1125; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1234



April 10, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE DEPARTMENT OF ENVIRONMENTAL QUALITY, STATE OF LOUISIANA, DOCKET NO. D-079-1912.

ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, NO. 339,964, HONORABLE JOSEPH KEOGH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH ORDER


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant permit applicant appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which dismissed its petition to review a permit denial by appellee, department of environmental quality (DEQ), for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. At issue was the retroactivity of an amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:2024(A) vesting jurisdiction in the trial court to conduct a de novo review of DEQ permit decisions.


OVERVIEW: The DEQ denied the applicant's application for a permit to construct a solid waste landfill. The applicant contended that § 30:2024 was unconstitutional because it vested jurisdiction to review DEQ actions directly in the appellate court, thereby bypassing the trial court. The court found that the provision vesting jurisdiction in the trial court to review the DEQ's action was a procedural one because it prescribed a method of enforcing a right of judicial review of an administrative decision which previously existed. This provision in no way impaired vested rights; it merely changed the forum in which the applicant could exercise its previously existing right of judicial review. Further, the vesting of subject matter jurisdiction to entertain an appeal in the trial court did not effect a change in the substantive law which gave an aggrieved party the right of judicial review of adverse administrative decisions. Moreover, the provision requiring the trial court to conduct a de novo review was a remedial and procedural provision entitled to retroactive application because it changed the form of the judicial review proceeding to be conducted in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter to the trial court to conduct a de novo review of the DEQ's denial of the applicant's permit application.

 

988 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Moonmaid Marine, Inc. v. Larpenter


No. CA 90 0789, No. CA 90 0790, No. CA 90 0791, No. CA 90 0792


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


599 So. 2d 820; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1819



March 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 28, 1992. Rehearing Denied May 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, NOS. 89971, 90150, 90117, 90118, IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF TERREBONNE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE EDWARD J. GAIDRY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporations sought review of a decision from the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), which dismissed their claim filed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2108.1against appellee, the Parish, to recover property taxes paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The corporations filed an action against the Parish to recover 1986 and 1987 property taxes paid under protest. They claimed that § 47:1951, which imposed the taxes was unconstitutional, because it failed to apportion the tax based upon the vessels' actual activities in the State and the Parish. The district court dismissed their claims, ruling that the corporations' vessels were not engaged in "international trade" and thus were not subject to the exemption. The court reversed the judgment and ordered the Parish to reimburse the corporations. The court ruled that the vessels were engaged in international trade and were subject to the exemption. The court concluded that the vessels spend much of their time in international waters and did not travel between different point between states in the United States; thus the corporations proved that they were not engaged in international trade.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the corporations' claims to recover property taxes paid in protest. The court rendered judgment ordering the Parish to refund the money to the corporations with interest.

 

989 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Bergeron v. Blake Drilling & Workover Co.


DOCKET NOS.: CA/1322/90C, CA/1323/90C, CA/1324/90C


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


599 So. 2d 827; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1821



March 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 28, 1992. Rehearing Denied May 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FOR THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, NUMBER 88797, 88809, 89074, PARISH OF TERREBONNE, HONORABLE WILMORE J. BROUSSARD, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND AS AMENDED AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, drilling companies and employer, appealed the judgment of the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), which held that they were liable to plaintiffs, injured employees and family of a deceased employees, after the employees suffered injuries during a premature explosion during a drilling operation.


OVERVIEW: An employer hired an independent contractor to perform drilling work on a barge. An explosion prematurely occurred during a wireline perforating, and two employees were injured, while another died. A lawsuit was brought against the employer and the drilling companies. The trial court found in favor of the employees, and an appeal was taken. The court held that admiralty law did not apply, because even though the accident occurred on a barge that was in navigable waters, the drilling did not involve maritime nexus, and was an activity related to the oil and gas industry. The court also determined that the employer could not avoid liability on the grounds that the explosion was incurred by an independent contractor, because the employer could not avoid liability for an ultrahazardous duty, such as wireline perforating. In addition, the court observed that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the admission of videos of the employers receiving treatment because it was not prejudicial. The court concluded that the trial court's award of damages was excessive, and reduced the amount of their recovery.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the lower court, and affirmed the judgment as modified.

Branton v. Webster Parish School Bd.


No. 24,197-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


596 So. 2d 840; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 862



March 20, 1992, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 51,688. Honorable Harmon Drew, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, voters and property taxpayers, appealed the judgment of the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court, Parish of Webster (Louisiana), which found in favor of the school board in an action to invalidate a school district bond election.


OVERVIEW: The voters and property taxpayers filed suit to declare void the special election in their school district. The election concerned the issuance of bonds to be retired by an increase of ad valorem taxes on property situated in the school district. The election was open to all registered voters. The voters and property taxpayers contended that, under the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 39:702, the "qualified" voters in an election to levy a special tax to benefit public schools were restricted to property taxpayers only. They complained that the election should not have been open to all registered voters. The trial court found in favor of the school board, and the voters and property taxpayers appealed. On appeal, the court held that the special interest property taxpayers have in bond elections was not the compelling State interest that would justify excluding a large portion of the electorate that have a substantial stake in public education.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the action of the district court in favor of the school board in an action to invalidate a school district bond election.

St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co. v. Smith


No. 90-954 Consolidate with No. 90-955


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


596 So. 2d 272; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 619



March 11, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana, the Honorable John Rixie Mouton, Sr. District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff worker's compensation insurer sought review of a judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana, which held in favor of plaintiff injured employee in the tort action against defendant truck owner. The insurer sought reimbursement for worker's compensation benefits paid to the employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who was a flagman, was injured when the truck improperly changed lanes into a construction zone and ran into equipment owned by the road construction company that was the employer. Plaintiffs brought an action against the truck owner. Subsequently, plaintiffs petitioned the trial court for a declaratory judgment as to the proper apportionment of the insurance proceeds. The trial court rendered a declaratory judgment in favor of the employee, giving him preference in payment from the insurance proceeds for his general damages before the insurer could recover any reimbursement. The insurer sought review arguing that the trial judge erred, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1103, in rendering a declaratory judgment holding that the employee would receive all sums awarded him for his non-economic damages arising from the accident in preference to payment of reimbursement to it. On appeal, the court reversed and rendered the judgment. The court held that the 1989 amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1103(B) was interpretive and retroactive. The court found that the trial court erred in failing to apply the 1989 amended statute, thus, the insurer was entitled to recover.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered the judgment.

Casse v. Department of Health & Hosp.


NUMBER CA 91 0072


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


597 So. 2d 547; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 610



March 6, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM A DECISION OF THE STATE CIVIL SERVICE COMMISSION (NUMBER S-7345); HONORABLE JAMES A. SMITH, CHAIRMAN; A. J. CAPRITTO, VICE-CHAIRMAN; EDWARD C. ABELL, JR., BURL CAIN, EDWIN C. HARBUCK, JOHN W. SCOTT AND DIANNE C. TROULLIER, MEMBERS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED, WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant civil service employees sought review of a decision by the State Civil Service Commission. The main issue presented in the appeal was whether the Commission erred in summarily disposing of portions of the appeal prior to a public hearing on the merits by concluding that some allegations by the employees either had not been pled with sufficient factual detail or was not a violation of La. Const. art. X, part I or a civil service rule.


OVERVIEW: The employees had filed an appeal with the Commission challenging a layoff plan, which took effect the following day. The Commission summarily disposed of portions of the appeal. The court reversed in part and affirmed in part and remanded with instructions. The court noted that the allegations of discriminatory treatment were not supported by any facts and that the allegations, as pleaded, were conclusory and failed to allege sufficient detail as required by Civ. Serv. R. 13.11(d). The court held that the allegations that the layoff plan was approved too quickly and that the Department of Civil Service had failed to issue appropriate orders to insure that the layoffs were fair satisfied the pleading requirements of Rule 13.11(d) and reversed the Commission's summary disposition of those issues. The court found no merit in the allegations relative to a duty to review outside agency contracts. The court found that the allegations that the layoff plan failed to address the budgetary measures taken to avoid the layoff was preserved for a hearing on the merits. The court ordered the Commission to refer to a hearing on the merits those allegations deemed by the court to have merit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part, affirmed in part, and remanded the case to the Civil Service Commission with instructions to hold hearings on those allegations determined by the court to have merit.

In re R.W.T. Applying for Adoption of J.D.


No. 23,604-JA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


594 So. 2d 1383; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 459



February 26, 1992, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Juvenile Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 8133. Honorable Andres B. Gallagher, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant natural father sought review of a judgment from the Juvenile Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which granted the adoption of his son by appellee stepfather. The natural father contended that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:422.1 was unconstitutionally excessive punishment for the failure to pay child support and that the trial court was wrong in determining that the adoption was in the best interests of the child.


OVERVIEW: The natural father had failed to pay child support for some time prior to the adoption proceedings. In addition, he had been violent with the child's mother. The mother remarried, and the juvenile court granted the stepfather's adoption petition. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court noted that the natural father failed to raise the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2422.1 in the juvenile court and failed to join the attorney general. The court held that the evidence supported the determination that the adoption was in the best interests of the child. There was no error in the finding that the stepfather was well suited as a prospective adoptive parent. Also, the court held that any meaningful parenting bond that existed between the natural father and the child had dissipated prior to the filing of the adoption petition. Further, the court found that the juvenile court properly considered evidence of the natural father's misconduct that occurred after the petition was filed. The testimony was offered as additional proof of the nonexistence of a parent-child relationship between the natural father and the child. The testimony did not expand the pleadings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the juvenile court.

West Cent. Louisiana Entertainment, Inc. v. Leesville


No. 90-832


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


594 So. 2d 973; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 456



February 12, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Thirtieth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vernon, Honorable Ted R. Broyles, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee challenged an order of the Thirtieth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Vernon (Louisiana), which held that Leesville, La. City Ordinance 14:63 was not manifestly unconstitutional and was a legitimate exercise of the police power of defendant municipality.


OVERVIEW: The licensee operated an after-hours club and allowed patrons to bring in alcohol beverages. Patrons 18 and older entered for a cover charge. After several months of operation under an occupational license, the municipality informed the licensee that the business violated Ordinance 14:63 and would be closed down if it continued to operate. In affirming, the court noted that there was no fundamental right or suspect class involved that required heightened scrutiny of the ordinance. The police testified that there was an increase in both criminal activity and the number of arrests in the area of the club, and that minors were arrested on the club's premises. The court found that the ordinance was rationally related to the legitimate government objectives of reducing alcohol consumption by minors and crimes committed by intoxicated persons, and protecting minors from the corrupting influences of older patrons. Thus, the ordinance was constitutional under substantive due process and equal protection analyses. Further, the ordinance was designed to accomplish a purpose and properly fell within the scope of the municipality's police power. Finally, the ordinance was not broad or vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court at the licensee's costs.

State v. Perkins


No. 90-KA-1038


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


593 So. 2d 904; 1992 La. App. LEXIS 86



January 30, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 12, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 334-041, SECTION "I". HONORABLE SHIRLEY WIMBERLY, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which convicted him of simple burglary of an inhabited dwelling in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14.62.2, found him to be a second offender, and sentenced him to serve six years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred by granting the state's challenge for cause and by imposing an excessive sentence. The court determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting a challenge for cause directed to a juror who testified that she had known defendant most of her life and knew his sisters "real well." The court found that the record clearly indicated that the prospective juror's relationship with defendant and his family could have influenced his verdict. Although the juror had not had any contact with defendant for 10 years, she testified that it would be hard for her to be fair and impartial as a juror. Under the circumstances, the court concluded that the trial court properly granted the challenge pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 797. The court determined that under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, the maximum sentence that defendant could have received as a second offender was 12 years. The court concluded that because defendant received only half of the maximum sentence, the trial court did not abuse its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Watson v. Nile


No. 90-CA-2174


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


591 So. 2d 1343; 1991 La. App. LEXIS 3522



December 30, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 10, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 89-265, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE REVIUS O. ORTIQUE, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant dog owner appealed an order of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which dismissed dog owner's rule for costs and attorney's fees in his third party petition for declaratory judgment against the state that alleged that a certain legislative act was unconstitutional. Dog owner contended he should have been awarded fees in his successful suit because his claim was based on federal law as well as state law.


OVERVIEW: Dog owner was sued in a dog bite case. Dog owner filed a third party petition for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against the state and alleged that a certain legislative act was unconstitutional. Dog owner prevailed, and then filed an action for costs and attorney's fees against the state. The trial court dismissed the suit and dog owner appealed. Dog owner contended that the trial court erred in failing to award fees because he based his claim not only on state law but on federal law, and was entitled to relief under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The court affirmed and held that the trial court based its decision of state law in finding the legislative act unconstitutional, and the judgment did not refer to federal law. Therefore, fees were properly denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court, which dismissed dog owner's rule for costs and attorney's fees in his third party petition for declaratory judgment against the state that alleged that a certain legislative act was unconstitutional.

State v. Hookfin


No. 90-KA-1688


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


601 So. 2d 320; 1991 La. App. LEXIS 3769



December 30, 1991, Decided  
December 30, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 27, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. SECTION A, NO. 322-358. HONORABLE MIRIAM G. WALTZER, JUDGE

Previously Reported as Unpublished Table Case at 1991 La. App. LEXIS 3559.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant complained of his conviction and sentence by the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which were entered upon a jury finding of guilty of attempted possession of cocaine with intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the State proved defendant had constructive possession of the cocaine found in the kitchen. Mail addressed to the defendant that established his residency, coupled with his having exercised dominion and control, by his sale of cocaine to an undercover narcotics investigator, over the other cocaine that was flushed down the toilet led to the conclusion that the cocaine found in the kitchen was subject to his dominion and control as well. The court held that defendant's sale of the two ounces of cocaine to the investigator, and the paraphernalia for distribution, consisting of the baggies, the metric scale, and the walkie-talkies, was sufficient evidence to support the inference of the intent to distribute cocaine. Defendant did not raise properly the issue of the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:130.1 in the trial court either by way of a motion to quash under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 532 or by way of a motion in arrest of judgment under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 859. The court, therefore, refused to consider this argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Greenleaf v. DHH, Metro. Developmental Center


CA 90 1847, CA 90 1848


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


594 So. 2d 418; 1991 La. App. LEXIS 3654



December 27, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE STATE CIVIL SERVICE COMMISSION, NOS. 7435 CONSOLIDATED WITH 7591, HONORABLE JAMES A. SMITH, CHAIRMAN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee appealed a decision from the State Civil Service Commission (Louisiana), which confirmed his 90 day suspension without pay pending an investigation into his conduct and his subsequent demotion and transfer.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a classified civil service employee, insisted upon the fiscally irresponsible actions of delaying recoupment of state funds and issuing a check to a vendor without the proper authorization in spite of contrary advice by his fiscal officers. These actions impaired the efficient and orderly operation of his agency. In affirming the decision to suspend, demote, and transfer the employee, the court held that none of the procedures applicable to the employee under the Louisiana Civil Service Rules denied him due process of law. In particular, the court held that La. Civ. Serv. R. 1.40 and 12.2 did not contravene La. Const. art. X, § 8(A). The court next held that La. Civ. Serv. R. 13.15, 13.17, and 13.18 did not infringe impermissible on the employee's due process right to a speedy resolution of his case. The court also held that the essentials of due process were met in the pre-deprivation proceedings. The court further held that the Commission had no jurisdiction to adjudicate the employee's invasion of privacy and defamation claims. The court held that the Commission's decision was not arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to suspend, demote, and transfer the employee.

Allen v. Louisiana State Bd. of Dentistry


CA 90 2107


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


595 So. 2d 320; 1991 La. App. LEXIS 3621



December 27, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, NO. 356,307, HONORABLE JOSEPH KEOGH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH ORDER


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State Board of Dentistry challenged a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) to the extent it found venue proper in East Baton Rouge Parish in appellee dentist's action to recover costs for administrative proceedings under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:965.1 after fines and discipline against him were overturned by the Louisiana Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: The dentist was the subject of disciplinary action that resulted in fines and suspension. He appealed, and the case was ultimately heard by the Louisiana Supreme Court which found in his favor. He thereafter filed an action to recover costs and attorney's fees under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 13:5101, and 13:5104, and the Board filed a change of venue motion under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:964(B) of the Louisiana Administrative Procedure Act, seeking venue in Orleans Parish, where the Board had its offices and was therefore domiciled. The trial court denied the request, holding that because the dentist and the witnesses were largely in East Baton Rouge Parish, venue was proper there. The board appealed, and the court reversed and remanded for transfer. The court held that because his claim for litigation expenses was brought under the authority of the Act, it should have been filed in the district court of the parish in which the agency was located, and the trial court erred in denying the Board's requested change of venue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Livingston Parish Police Jury v. Lee


NUMBER 90 CA 2098


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


598 So. 2d 1086; 1991 La. App. LEXIS 3628



December 27, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 9, 1992, Reported at 1992 La. App. LEXIS 1786.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, NO. 61331, LIVINGSTON PARISH, LOUISIANA, HONORABLE JOSEPH E. ANZALONE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant proprietor sought review of a judgment from the 21st Judicial District Court, Livingston Parish (Louisiana), which granted plaintiff parish police jury a preliminary injunction prohibiting the proprietor from operating a salvage yard site without a permit and in violation of Livingston Parish, La., Code § 10-8.


OVERVIEW: The parish police jury brought suit against the proprietor seeking injunctive relief from his alleged violation of Livingston Parish, La., Code § 10-8 governing the establishment and operation of automobile salvage yards. The trial court granted the parish police jury a preliminary injunction, which enjoined the proprietor from operating a salvage yard site without a permit and in violation of § 10-8. The proprietor contended that § 10-8 was unconstitutionally vague, overly broad, and indefinite. On appeal, the court determined that the parish police jury had no right of action and reversed the trial court's judgment. The court found that the parish police jury was a creature and a subordinate political subdivision of the state, and, as such, possessed only those powers conferred upon it by the state's constitution and statutes. The court ruled that the parish police jury had no right to enforce its ordinance with an injunction because there was no constitutional or statutory authority for it to do so.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that granted the parish police jury a preliminary injunction.
